Salah — Prayer

Minimum Followers for Jumu‘ah: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on minimum followers for Jumu‘ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the minimum number of followers for Jumu‘ah and explain the linguistic and Qur'anic evidence each side uses.

Core Idea
Jumu‘ah requires at least three followers besides the imam — the dual is not a true plural.

The Friday prayer is a weekly obligation that requires a congregation (jamā‘ah). But how many people must be present? Within the Hanafi school, a well-known dispute arises over the minimum number of followers besides the imam. This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies the positions of Abu Hanifah, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and explains the linguistic reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad: at least three followers besides the imam are required for Jumu‘ah.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Abu Yusuf holds that two followers besides the imam suffice. Note that this is only Abu Yusuf's view, not the Sahibayn collectively.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Abu Yusuf argues that the dual number (two) entails gathering (ijtimā‘), and Jumu‘ah is derived from jam‘ (gathering), so two are sufficient.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifah and Muhammad respond that the true plural (jam‘ al-sahīh) applies only to three or more. They cite the Qur'anic address 'fas‘aw' (Q. 62:9) which is plural, implying at least three addressees besides the imam.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If only two followers attend besides the imam, Jumu‘ah is valid per Abu Yusuf but invalid per Abu Hanifah and Muhammad. The practical consequence is that such a prayer must be repeated as Ẓuhr.
The mufta bihi view is three besides the imam.

کے قول کے مطابق بھی امام کے ساتھ یل کا تین ہو جاتے ہیں۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جماعت علیحدہ شرط ہے اور امام کا ہونا عید ہ شرط ہے۔ اس لئے کہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول فان قوا
And among its conditions is the congregation, because Jumu‘ah is derived from it. And the minimum (number) according to Abu Hanifah is three besides the imam. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: two besides him. He (the author al-Marghinani) said: 'And the most correct is that this is the saying of Abu Yusuf alone.' For him (Abu Yusuf) there is the argument that in the dual there is the meaning of gathering (social), and Jumu‘ah indicates it. For them (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad) there is the argument that the true plural is only three, because it is plural in name and meaning. And the congregation is a separate condition, and likewise the imam is a separate condition, so he is not counted among them. Explanation: Congregation is a condition for Jumu‘ah by consensus. However, there is a difference regarding the number of individuals. Accordingly, according to Imam Abu Hanifah, the presence of at least three people besides the imam is necessary. This is also the saying of Imam Zufar. And according to the Sahibayn, at least three besides the imam? No, according to Sahibayn two suffice. This is according to the statement of al-Quduri. The author of al-Hidayah says: 'The correct matter is that the presence of two followers besides the imam is only the saying of Abu Yusuf. As for Imam Muhammad, his saying agrees with Imam Abu Hanifah.' According to the author of al-Hidayah, the result is that according to the two sides (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad), the presence of three people besides the imam is a condition for Jumu‘ah. And according to Imam Abu Yusuf, two besides the imam suffice. The condition of congregation for Jumu‘ah is because Jumu‘ah is derived from congregation. Therefore Jumu‘ah cannot be realized without congregation, just as 'darib' (striker) is derived from 'darb' (striking) and cannot be realized without striking. Regarding the number of the congregation, the evidence of Imam Abu Yusuf is that the lexical meaning of Jumu‘ah is gathering, and the meaning of gathering exists in two because one comes together with another. So when the lexical meaning of Jumu‘ah is realized by the number two, then the presence of two besides the imam is sufficient for Jumu‘ah. The evidence of the two sides is: Undoubtedly Jumu‘ah indicates the meaning of assembly, but in the saying of Allah Most High 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah', the address 'fas‘aw' (hasten) is plural, i.e., the plural form is used for address. And the correct plural is applied to at least three, because the number three is plural both in name and meaning. Therefore we say that at least three besides the imam are necessary. The phrase 'the congregation is a separate condition' is an answer to a question: The question is that according to Abu Yusuf's saying also, along with the imam three individuals become present. The answer is that the congregation is a separate condition, and the presence of the imam is a separate condition. This is because the saying of Allah Most High 'fa in qawa' [incomplete].
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage addresses the condition of congregation (jamā‘ah) for the Friday prayer. It begins by stating that jamā‘ah is a condition because 'Jumu‘ah' is derived from 'jam‘' (gathering). The core intra-Hanafi dispute concerns the minimum number of participants besides the imam. According to Abu Hanifah, at least three men besides the imam are required (total four). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) initially appear to say two suffice. However, the author of al-Hidayah clarifies that this is only Abu Yusuf's view; Imam Muhammad actually agrees with Abu Hanifah. Abu Yusuf's reasoning is that the dual number already involves gathering (two people coming together), and the word 'Jumu‘ah' etymologically indicates gathering, so two besides the imam suffice. The majority (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad) argue that the true plural (jam‘ al-sahīh) is three or more, as the term 'jam‘' in Arabic applies to three and above. They also cite the verse 'fas‘aw ilā dhikrillāh' where the command 'fas‘aw' is in the plural form, implying at least three addressees besides the imam. The passage also addresses a potential objection: if Abu Yusuf's view of two plus the imam makes three total, why is that not sufficient? The answer is that the congregation is a separate condition, and the imam is counted separately; the condition requires a certain number of followers besides the imam. Thus, the imam is not included in the count.

Key Terms
جماعت (jamā‘ah): A congregation of Muslims for prayer, specifically a group including an imam and followers.
جمع (jam‘): Gathering; plural form in Arabic grammar. The dispute hinges on whether dual (2) counts as jam‘.
امام (imām): The leader of the prayer, not counted among the minimum required followers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the minimum number of participants besides the imam required for Friday prayer?
A) Two men besides the imam
B) Three men besides the imam
C) Four men including the imam
D) One man besides the imam

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Jumu‘ah requires at least three followers besides the imam, based on the true plural form in Arabic and the Qur’anic address, with the imam counted separately.

Minimum Number for Jumu'ah Congregation: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Stating the condition of congregation and minimum participants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum number of men required for Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, identify the differing view of Abu Yusuf, and explain the linguistic and Qur'anic proofs for each position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa requires three men besides the imam; Abu Yusuf suffices with two. The relied-upon position is three.

Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) is a fard 'ayn, but its validity depends on congregation. Within the Hanafi school, there is a subtle difference of opinion on the minimum number of participants besides the imam. This lesson unpacks the arguments of the founding Imams and clarifies which view is adopted for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the ruling according to Abu Hanifa, Imam Muhammad, and the mufta bihi: three men besides the imam.
This is the position attributed to the majority of the school.
2
Identify the Opposing View
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that two men besides the imam suffice. Note that this is his individual view, not shared by Muhammad.
The text explicitly states that the Sahibayn's view is actually only Abu Yusuf's.
3
Analyze the Proofs
Compare the proofs: Abu Yusuf uses the lexical meaning of 'jumu'ah' as gathering, which can occur with two. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rely on the Quranic plural command 'fas'aw' which implies at least three.
Also consider the principle that a true plural requires three.
4
Understand the Tarjih
The author of al-Hidayah declares Abu Yusuf's view as less correct; the mufta bihi is three. Explain why the plural argument is stronger.
The imam is not counted among the followers; the verse indicates four total persons.
5
Apply the Practical Consequence
If only two men are present besides the imam, according to the mufta bihi, Jumu'ah is invalid and must be prayed as Zuhr. According to Abu Yusuf, it would be valid.
In fatwa, the stricter view is taken to ensure validity.

مقتدی ہوں۔ اس سے ظاہر ہوا کہ امام کا شمار ان تین میں نہیں ہوگا بلکہ امام کے علاوہ تین آدمیوں کی جماعت کا ہونا شرط جمعہ ہے۔
And among its conditions is congregation, because Jumu'ah is derived from congregation. According to Abu Hanifa, the minimum besides the imam is three. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: two besides him. The author said: the more correct view is that this is the saying of Abu Yusuf alone. He has that in the dual there is the meaning of social gathering, and it indicates it. And they (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) have that the true plural is only three, because it is plural in name and meaning. And congregation is a separate condition, and likewise the imam, so he is not counted among them. Translation: And among the conditions of Jumu'ah is congregation because Jumu'ah is derived from congregation. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the minimum congregation besides the imam is three men. And the two (Sahibayn) said that besides the imam two suffice. The author said that the more correct is that this is the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf alone. Abu Yusuf's proof is that in two there is the meaning of social gathering, and Jumu'ah indicates it. The proof of the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the true plural is only in three, because three is plural both in name and meaning, and congregation is a separate condition. Similarly, the imam is a separate condition, so he is not counted among them. Explanation: Congregation is unanimously a condition for Jumu'ah, but there is a difference about the number of individuals. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, at least three men besides the imam are necessary. This is also the view of Imam Zufar. According to the two (Sahibayn), besides the imam two are sufficient. However, the author of Hidayah says that the correct view is that the presence of two followers besides the imam is only the view of Imam Abu Yusuf. As for Imam Muhammad, his view agrees with Imam Abu Hanifa. According to the author of Hidayah, the result is that according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) the condition for Jumu'ah is the presence of three men besides the imam, while according to Imam Abu Yusuf two men besides the imam are sufficient. The condition of congregation for Jumu'ah is because Jumu'ah is derived from congregation. Therefore Jumu'ah cannot be realized without congregation, just as ضارب (striker) is derived from ضرب (striking), so the striker cannot be realized without striking. Regarding the number of congregation, the proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that the lexical meaning of Jumu'ah is gathering, and in two the meaning of gathering is present in the sense that one is together with the other. So when the lexical meaning of Jumu'ah is realized with the number two, the presence of two men besides the imam is sufficient for Jumu'ah. The proof of the two sides is that no doubt Jumu'ah indicates the meaning of gathering, but in the statement of Allah Most High 'فاسعوا إلى ذكر الله', the word 'فاسعوا' is a plural address, meaning an address with the plural form. And the true plural applies to at least three, because the number three is plural both in name and meaning. Therefore we said that at least three men besides the imam are necessary. 'And congregation is a separate condition' answers a question: According to Imam Abu Yusuf's view, with the imam the total becomes three. The answer is that congregation is a separate condition and the imam is a separate condition. Because the word 'فاسعوا' in Allah's statement requires three individuals, and 'إلى ذكر الله' requires one dhikr-maker (the imam). So from the verse four men are established: the congregation includes one imam and three followers besides him. This shows that the imam is not counted among those three; rather the condition for Jumu'ah is the congregation of three men besides the imam.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the minimum number of persons required for the Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) congregation. The author begins by stating the condition of congregation (jamā'ah) for Jumu'ah, deriving it linguistically from the word itself. He then presents the ikhtilāf: Imam Abū Ḥanīfah (and later Imām Muḥammad according to the correct view) requires at least three men besides the imam, while Imām Abū Yūsuf suffices with two besides the imam. The text clarifies that the view attributed to 'the two' (Ṣāḥibayn) is actually only Abū Yūsuf's; Muḥammad agrees with Abū Ḥanīfah. Each side provides its proof: Abū Yūsuf relies on the lexical meaning of 'gathering' being present in two, while Abū Ḥanīfah and Muḥammad rely on the Qur'anic address 'fas'aw' (plural form) which implies at least three, and on the principle that a true plural (jama' ṣaḥīḥ) requires three. The passage also explains why the imam is not counted among the three followers: the verse indicates four persons total (imam + three followers) because the plural command 'fas'aw' requires three addressees, and 'ilā dhikri llāh' points to one imam. This resolves a potential objection to Abū Yūsuf's view that the total with the imam would be three. The relied-upon position (muftā bihī) is that of Abū Ḥanīfah and Muḥammad: three men besides the imam are required.

Key Terms
الجَمَاعَة (al-jamā‘ah): Group of people praying together with an imam; minimum number is disputed.
الجُمُعَة (al-jumu‘ah): Friday congregational prayer; derived from jamā‘ah (gathering).
شَرْط الانعِقاد (sharṭ al-in‘iqād): Condition for the validity (initiation) of the prayer; if missing, the prayer does not begin validly.

When the Congregation Leaves During Jumu'ah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Jumu'ah validity when congregation departs prior to one rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the validity of Jumu'ah when the congregation departs early and explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, and Zufar.

Core Idea
Congregation is a condition for Jumu'ah, but is it required only at the start or throughout? The Hanafi imams differ.

This passage examines a scenario that tests the limits of the congregation requirement for Friday prayer. The congregation departs during the prayer, leaving the imam alone. The Hanafi school internally debates whether this invalidates the prayer. We will explore the reasoning of the major Hanafi figures and the practical implications for the imam.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the three scenarios (before start, after start but before one rak'ah, after one rak'ah) and the rulings of Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, and Zufar.
Unanimous: if they leave before start, Jumu'ah invalid.
2
Understand the key concepts
Differentiate between 'shart al-in'iqad' (condition for initiation) and 'shart al-dawam' (condition for continuation).
Sahibayn hold congregation is only shart al-in'iqad; Zufar holds it must continue like time.
3
Follow the proofs
Examine the analogies: Sahibayn compare congregation to the sermon (condition only at start), Zufar compares to time (must be present throughout), Abu Hanifa uses the concept of a complete rak'ah.
Abu Hanifa: less than a rak'ah is not prayer, so congregation must last until a rak'ah.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: what should the imam do in each scenario according to each imam?
After one rak'ah: three agree Jumu'ah valid; Zufar disagrees.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Recognize that the relied-upon position is that of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) that after one rak'ah Jumu'ah is valid.
Before one rak'ah, there is divergence; precaution may be to pray Zuhr.

Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on Friday prayer when the congregation leaves the imam during the prayer. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute involving Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Zufar. The author outlines three scenarios: (1) before the prayer starts: unanimous that Jumu'ah is invalid and Zuhr must be prayed. (2) After starting but before completing one rak'ah (i.e., before ruku' and sujud): Abu Hanifa says Jumu'ah is invalid and Zuhr must be prayed; the Sahibayn say Jumu'ah is valid and should be continued. (3) After completing one rak'ah (i.e., after ruku' and one sajdah): the three (Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn) agree Jumu'ah is valid and should be continued; Zufar says it is invalid and Zuhr must be prayed. The reasoning: The Sahibayn hold that congregation is a condition for the initiation (in'iqad) of Jumu'ah, but not for its continuation (dawam), similar to the sermon (khutbah) which is required before the prayer but not during it. Abu Hanifa holds that validity (in'iqad) requires the completion of a full rak'ah because less than a rak'ah is not considered prayer; thus congregation must remain until one rak'ah is completed. Zufar analogizes congregation to time: it must be present throughout the entire prayer. The text also clarifies that women and children do not count towards the required congregation because Jumu'ah is not valid with them as followers. The mufta bihi position is that of the three imams: if one rak'ah has been completed, Jumu'ah is valid; otherwise, if they leave before that, the view of Abu Hanifa (Zuhr) is precautionary but the fatwa may follow the Sahibayn in many cases. However, the text does not explicitly state which is relied upon.

Key Terms
شَرْط الانعِقاد (sharṭ al-in‘iqād): Condition for the initial validity of an act; if missing at the beginning, the act is invalid even if later fulfilled.
دَوَام (dawām): Continuity of a condition throughout the act.
رَكْعَة (rak‘ah): Unit of prayer consisting of standing, bowing, and two prostrations. Minimum complete unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For Jumu'ah validity, the Hanafi school requires congregation at start; whether it must continue depends on the imam: after one rak'ah it's valid by consensus of the three, but before that there is a difference.

When Congregation Leaves During Jumu'ah: The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on congregation leaving during Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the effect of congregation leaving during Jumu'ah and explain the key difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the timing of the condition.

Core Idea
The condition of congregation for Jumu'ah is shart al-in'iqad, not shart al-wujub; only continuity through the first rak'ah is required.

What happens if worshippers leave in the middle of a Friday prayer? Does the imam continue as Jumu'ah or switch to Zuhr? This passage from Al-Hidayah presents three answers from within the Hanafi school. The dispute hinges on a subtle but critical distinction: is congregation a condition for the validity of the prayer (shart al-in'iqad) that drops once the prayer is validly started, or must it persist throughout (shart al-dawam)? The positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam Zufar offer three different resolutions, each supported by a distinct analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State what each imam (Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, Zufar) says about the effect of congregation leaving during Jumu'ah. Note the threshold: before ruku and sujud of the first rak'ah, after takbir, or any time.
Abu Hanifa: leaves before ruku & sujud → Zuhr; after → Jumu'ah. Sahibayn: after takbir → Jumu'ah always. Zufar: any time → invalid.
2
Analyze each position's proof
For each, identify the reasoning: Abu Hanifa argues in'iqad requires completion of one rak'ah; Sahibayn analogy to khutbah (condition for validity, not continuity); Zufar analogy to time (condition must persist throughout).
The proofs are based on qiyas (analogy) to khutbah and to time.
3
Distinguish shart al-in'iqad vs shart al-dawam
The usul distinction: a condition for validity (shart al-in'iqad) need not persist after the act is validly begun, while a condition for obligation (shart al-wujub) or for continuity (shart al-dawam) must last. Apply this to congregation.
Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa treat congregation as shart al-in'iqad; Zufar treats it as shart al-dawam.
4
Apply to a scenario
Suppose the imam says takbir, then all men leave before he bends for ruku. According to each view, what should the imam do? Practice applying the rule.
Abu Hanifa: switch to Zuhr. Sahibayn: continue Jumu'ah. Zufar: invalid, pray Zuhr.
5
Note the special case of women and children
The passage explicitly states that women and children do not count for Jumu'ah congregation. Their presence is irrelevant to the condition. Understand why: Jumu'ah is not valid through them.
This reinforces that the congregation must be of eligible men.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان نفر الناس قبل أن يركع الإمام ويسجد إلا النساء والصبيان استقبل الظهر عند أبي حنيفة وقالا إذا نفر عنه بعد ما افتتح الصلاة صلى الجمعة فإن نفروا عنه بعد ما ركع وسجد سجدة بنى على الجمعة خلافا لزفر. زفر يقول: إن الجماعة شرط فلابد من دوامه كالوقت. ولهما أن الجماعة شرط الانعقاد فلا يشترط دوامها كالخطبة. ولأبي حنيفة أن الانعقاد بالشروع في الصلاة ولا يتم ذلك إلا بتمام الركعة لأن ما دونها ليس جماعة انعقاداً بالصلاة فلابد من دوامها إليها بخلاف الخطبة فإنها تنافي الصلاة فلا يشترط دوامها ولا معتبر ببقاء النسوان وكذا الصبيان لأنه لا تنعقد بهم الجمعة فلا تتم بهم الجماعة.

صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر نماز جمعہ کو چھوڑ کر لوگ فرار ہو گئے اور عورتیں اور بچے باقی رہ گئے تو ان کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ تنہا عورتوں اور بچوں سے جب جمعہ منعقد نہیں ہوتا تو ان کے ساتھ شرط جماعت بھی پوری نہ ہوگی۔ فوائد: امام صاحب کی دلیل پر ایک اشکال ہو سکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ جب ایک رکعت سے کم سے نماز منعقد نہیں ہوتی تو نفل شروع کر کے توڑنے سے قضاء واجب نہ ہونی چاہئے جب تک کہ رکعت تک پڑھ کر نہ توڑے۔ جواب: رکعت سے کم نماز میں دو حالت ہیں۔ اول یہ کہ تحریمہ پایا گیا پس اس جہت سے تو وہ نماز ہے اور چونکہ نماز نام قرأت ورکوع جمود کا ہے یہ نہیں پایا گیا تو اس جہت سے نماز نہیں پھر نفل توڑنے کے مسئلہ میں ہم نے احتیاط پر عمل کرتے ہوئے پہلی جہت کا اعتبار کر کے قضاء واجب کی کہ اس میں بالیقین قصور سے بچ گیا۔ اور جمعہ کے مسئلہ میں ہم نے دوسری جہت کا اعتبار کیا۔ کیونکہ ظہر پڑھنے سے بالیقین فرض ادا ہو گا۔
And if the people depart before the imam performs ruku and sujud, except women and children, then he (the imam) should pray Zuhr according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If they depart from him after he has commenced the prayer, he should pray Jumu'ah. And if they depart from him after he has performed ruku and one sujud, he builds upon the Jumu'ah, contrary to Zufar. Zufar says: Congregation is a condition, so its continuity is necessary like the time. And for the two (Sahibayn): Congregation is a condition for the validity (in'iqad), so its continuity is not required, like the khutbah. And for Abu Hanifa: The validity occurs by commencing the prayer, and it is not complete except with the completion of a rak'ah, because what is less than that is not a prayer (salat) by which congregation is established? (the text is ambiguous) So its continuity up to that point is necessary, unlike the khutbah, for it is contradictory to prayer, so its continuity is not required. And consideration is not given to the remaining of women nor children, because Jumu'ah is not valid through them, so congregation is not completed through them.

The author of Al-Hidayah says: If people flee from the Jumu'ah prayer and women and children remain, then their (women/children's) presence is not considered because Jumu'ah is not valid through women and children alone, so the condition of congregation is not fulfilled through them. Benefits: An objection can be raised on Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: When a prayer (even less than a rak'ah) is not valid (in'iqad), then breaking a nafl prayer after starting it would not necessitate qada (making up) unless one completes a rak'ah and then breaks it. Answer: In a prayer of less than a rak'ah, there are two aspects: First, the takbir (tahrimah) has been performed, so from that aspect it is a prayer; but since the essence of prayer includes recitation, ruku, and sujud, which are not present, from that aspect it is not a prayer. In the matter of breaking a nafl prayer, we act on precaution by considering the first aspect and thus making qada necessary, so that one certainly avoids deficiency. In the matter of Jumu'ah, we consider the other aspect, because by praying Zuhr one certainly fulfills the obligatory prayer.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage from the bab of Jumu'ah addresses a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when the congregation (other than women and children) leaves during the Friday prayer? The Arabic matn from Al-Hidayah presents three positions. Abu Hanifa holds that if the congregation leaves before the imam performs ruku and sajdah of the first rak'ah, then the Jumu'ah becomes invalid and the imam must pray Zuhr. If they leave after that, he continues with Jumu'ah. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say that if they leave after the prayer has commenced (after takbir), he continues Jumu'ah, regardless of whether they left before or after ruku and sajdah. Imam Zufar takes a stricter view: the congregation must be present throughout, like the time window for prayer; if anyone leaves, Jumu'ah is void. The commentary then explains the reasoning: Sahibayn liken congregation to the khutbah—a condition for validity but not for continuity. Abu Hanifa argues that validity occurs by starting the prayer, but the prayer itself (and thus its validity) is only established after one complete rak'ah; therefore, the congregation must persist until the end of the first rak'ah. Women and children do not count because Jumu'ah is not valid through them. The 'Benefits' section answers a potential objection: why does breaking a nafl prayer before completing a rak'ah still require qada? The answer distinguishes two aspects of prayer—the takbir (which makes it a prayer) and the actual components (which make it a full prayer). For nafl, they follow the first aspect out of caution; for Jumu'ah, they follow the second to ensure the obligation is firmly fulfilled by praying Zuhr.

Key Terms
جماعة (jama'ah): The presence of at least three men (muqtadi) besides the imam for Jumu'ah to be valid.
انعقاد (in'iqad): The validity or proper establishment of the Jumu'ah prayer, specifically that it counts as Jumu'ah rather than Zuhr.
دوام (dawam): The requirement that the condition (congregation) persists throughout the prayer, as argued by Imam Zufar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the primary difference between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the congregation condition for Jumu'ah?
A) Abu Hanifa requires congregation throughout; Sahibayn only at the start
B) Abu Hanifa requires congregation until the end of the first rak'ah; Sahibayn only require it at the start (takbir)
C) Abu Hanifa allows Jumu'ah even if congregation leaves before takbir; Sahibayn do not
D) Abu Hanifa requires three men; Sahibayn require four

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that congregation is a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah at the start, and although Abu Hanifa extends that requirement through the first rak'ah, the Sahibayn's view is lenient, allowing continuation once the prayer begins.

Salah — Prayer

Dispute on the Condition of Congregation for Jumu'ah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on persistence of congregation for Friday prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the persistence of congregation for Friday prayer and state the practical consequence of each position.

Core Idea
Congregation for Friday prayer must persist until the first rak'ah is completed, or the prayer becomes invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

This passage examines a disagreement within the Hanafi school about when Friday prayer becomes invalid if the congregation leaves. The Sahibayn argue that congregation is only required at the start, while Imam Abu Hanifa insists it must continue until the first rak'ah. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to define in'iqad (validity) and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and both positions
The core question: When does Friday prayer become invalid if the congregation leaves? The Sahibayn say it remains valid; Abu Hanifa says it invalidates before one rak'ah.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
They argue congregation is a condition for validity (in'iqad), not persistence, similar to the sermon (khutbah). Once the prayer is valid at takbir, continuation is not required.
This relies on a distinction between shart in'iqad and shart ada'.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's counter-proof
He refines in'iqad: 'prayer' linguistically applies only to a complete rak'ah. Thus validity is established only after the first rak'ah's ruku' and sujud. Congregation must persist until that point.
He cites Quran 47:33 (لا تُبْطِلُوا أَعْمَالَكُمْ) to argue that less than a rak'ah is not a 'deed' that can be invalidated.
4
Understand the distinction from khutbah
Abu Hanifa responds to the analogy: the sermon is not required to persist because it is contrary to prayer (reciting it in prayer invalidates), whereas congregation is not contrary, so it must persist.
This shows how the nature of the condition affects its requirement.
5
Apply the practical consequence
If people leave before ruku' of first rak'ah, Abu Hanifa says the imam must pray Zuhr; Sahibayn say continue. Most Hanafi practice follows Abu Hanifa's cautionary view.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the actual ruling that changes between the two positions.

نماز شروع کرنے سے ہوتا ہے اور نماز کا اطلاق ایک رکعت مکمل ہونے سے ہوگا کیونکہ ایک رکعت سے کم کو نماز نہیں کہا جاتا یہی وجہ ہے کہ ایک رکعت سے کم کو اگر چھوڑ دیا گیا تو وہ لا تُبْطِلُوا أَعْمَالَكُمْ کے تحت نہیں آتا۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ نماز کا اطلاق کم از کم ایک رکعت پر ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ ہوا کہ جماعت انعقاد جمعہ کی شرط ہے اور جمعہ منعقد ہوتا ہے نماز جمعہ شروع ہونے سے اور نماز کا اطلاق کم از کم ایک رکعت پر ہوتا ہے تو گویا نماز پس ایک رکعت پوری ہونے سے شروع ہوگی۔ پس ایک رکعت پوری ہونے تک جماعت کا پایا جانا شرط ہوگا۔ اور رکعت پوری ہوتی ہے رکوع اور سجدہ سے تو پہلی رکعت کے رکوع سجدہ تک اگر جماعت پائی گئی تو جمعہ منعقد ہو گیا۔ اب اگر امام کے رکوع سجدہ کرنے کے بعد لوگ بھاگ گئے اور جماعت فوت ہو گئی تو جمعہ فوت نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس سے پہلے بھاگ گئے تو جماعت فوت ہو جائے گی تو چونکہ نماز جمعہ منعقد ہونے سے قرار نہیں دی گئی۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر نماز جمعہ کو چھوڑ کر لوگ فرار ہو گئے اور عورتیں اور بچے باقی رہ گئے تو ان کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ تنہا عورتوں اور بچوں سے جب جمعہ منعقد نہیں ہوتا تو ان کے ساتھ شرط جماعت بھی پوری نہ ہوگی۔ فوائد . امام صاحب کی دلیل پر ایک اشکال ہو سکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ جب ایک رکعت سے کم سے نماز منعقد نہیں ہوتی تو نفل شروع کر کے توڑنے سے قضاء واجب نہ ہونی چاہئے ۔ جب تک کہ رکعت تک پڑھ کر نہ توڑے۔

جواب رکعت سے کم نماز میں دو حالت ہیں۔ اول یہ کہ تحریمہ پایا گیا پس اس جہت سے تو وہ نماز ہے اور چونکہ نماز نام قرأت ورکوع و سجود کا ہے یہ نہیں پایا گیا تو اس جہت سے نماز نہیں پھر نفل توڑنے کے مسئلہ میں ہم نے احتیاط پر عمل کرتے ہوئے ایک جہت کا اعتبار کر کے قضاء واجب کی کہ اس میں بالیقین قصور سے بچ گیا۔ اور جمعہ کے مسئلہ میں ہم نے دوسری جہت کا اعتبار کیا۔ کیونکہ ظہر پڑھنے سے بالیقین فرض ادا ہو گا۔
Chapter of Friday Prayer

The proof of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that congregation is not a condition for performing Friday prayer, but rather a condition for the validity (in'iqad) of Friday prayer, just as the sermon is a condition for the validity of Friday prayer. And a condition of validity does not need to persist from beginning to end; rather, it is necessary only up to the point of validity. After that, it is not necessary. So if congregation was present at the time of takbir al-tahrimah, Friday prayer became valid. After that, the continuation of congregation is not a condition. Therefore, the loss of congregation after the validity of Friday does not cause Friday to be lost. And when Friday is not lost, the imam completes it and does not pray Zuhr.

The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that indeed congregation is a condition for the validity of Friday, as you also say, but the validity of prayer occurs from the start of prayer, and the application of the term 'prayer' is from the completion of one rak'ah, because less than one rak'ah is not called prayer. This is why if less than one rak'ah is abandoned, it does not fall under 'Do not invalidate your deeds.' Thus it is established that the term 'prayer' applies to at least one rak'ah. The result is that congregation is a condition for the validity of Friday, and Friday becomes valid from the start of the Friday prayer, and the term 'prayer' applies to at least one rak'ah, so the prayer begins after the completion of one rak'ah. Therefore, the presence of congregation is condition until one rak'ah is completed. And a rak'ah is completed by ruku' and sujud. So if congregation was present until the ruku' and sujud of the first rak'ah, Friday became valid. Now if after the imam's ruku' and sujud the people leave and congregation is lost, Friday is not lost. But if they leave before that, congregation is lost. Since the condition of validity (congregation) was lost before Friday was valid, Friday becomes invalid (fasid), and it becomes obligatory for the imam to pray Zuhr.

As for the sermon being a condition for validity, but it is not necessary to persist until one rak'ah is completed, the answer is that indeed the sermon is a condition for validity, but because the sermon is contrary to prayer (if it is recited during prayer, it invalidates the prayer), its continuation until one rak'ah is not made a condition.

The author of al-Hidayah says: If people flee abandoning Friday prayer, and only women and children remain, they are not considered. Because when Friday is not valid with only women and children, the condition of congregation is not fulfilled with them.

Benefits: On Imam Abu Hanifa's proof, an objection may arise: when less than a rak'ah does not constitute prayer, then if one begins a supererogatory prayer and breaks it, qada should not be obligatory unless he completes a rak'ah.

Answer: In prayer less than a rak'ah, there are two aspects. First, the takbir al-tahrimah is present, so from that aspect it is prayer. And because the name 'prayer' includes recitation, ruku', and sujud, which are not present, from that aspect it is not prayer. In the matter of breaking a supererogatory prayer, we acted on caution and considered the one aspect to make qada obligatory, to be safe from deficiency. In the matter of Friday, we considered the other aspect, because by praying Zuhr, the obligatory is certainly fulfilled.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the condition of congregation (jama'ah) for the validity of Friday prayer. The issue arises when people leave after the initial takbir but before completing one rak'ah of the Friday prayer. The Sahibayn argue that congregation is a condition for the validity (in'iqad) of Friday prayer, not for its continuation, similar to the sermon (khutbah). Just as the sermon is only required at the beginning, congregation is only required at the start, at the time of takbir al-tahrimah. Therefore, if people leave later, the Friday prayer remains valid and the imam continues it. Imam Abu Hanifa responds by refining the concept of 'in'iqad'. He argues that the term 'prayer' (salat) applies only to a complete rak'ah; less than a rak'ah is not called prayer. Therefore, the validity of the Friday prayer is not established until the completion of the first rak'ah (specifically its ruku' and sujud). The condition of congregation must persist until that point. If people leave before the first rak'ah is completed, the condition was not fulfilled, and the Friday prayer is invalid (fasid). The imam must then pray Zuhr. The author of al-Hidayah adds a clarification: if only women and children remain after others flee, they do not count for congregation because Friday prayer is not established with them alone. A further objection is addressed: why is qada obligatory for breaking a supererogatory prayer even before a rak'ah? The answer distinguishes two aspects of a prayer less than a rak'ah: the takbir makes it a prayer in one sense, but the actions (recitation, ruku', sujud) are absent. For supererogatory prayers, caution dictates that breaking it requires qada, but for Friday, the other aspect is considered to avoid hardship.

Key Terms
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbir al-tahrimah): The opening takbir that initiates the prayer and makes actions unlawful (haram) except prayer.
انعقاد (in'iqad): The establishment or validity condition of a prayer or act, as opposed to performance (ada').
جماعت (jama'ah): A congregation of two or more persons (including the imam) for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if after the initial takbir of Friday prayer, all the worshippers leave before the imam rises from ruku' of the first rak'ah, what is the ruling?
A) The Friday prayer is valid and the imam continues.
B) The Friday prayer is invalid and the imam must pray Zuhr.
C) The Friday prayer is valid only if the imam makes up the missed congregation.
D) The Friday prayer becomes optional for the imam.

Key Takeaway
The duration of the condition of congregation for Friday prayer hinges on the definition of 'prayer' and whether in'iqad requires a complete rak'ah.

Salah — Prayer

Exemptions from Jumu'ah and Validity if Attended
Lists exemptions and validates attendance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five categories exempted from Jumu'ah and explain the Hanafi ruling that their attendance fulfills the obligation, using the principle of hardship (haraj).

Core Idea
Exemption from Jumu'ah is for ease; attending despite exemption is valid and fulfills the obligation.

Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) is a weekly obligation for qualified Muslims. However, certain individuals are excused due to hardship. This passage from Al-Hidayah lists five exempted categories and clarifies an important principle: exemption does not render the act invalid—if they choose to attend, their prayer counts. We will parse the categories, understand the rationale, and explore the proof by analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exempted categories
List the five types of people mentioned: traveler (musafir), woman (imra'ah), sick person (mariid), slave ('abd), and blind person (a'ma). Note that each is excused from attending Jumu'ah.
The exemption is from obligation, not from permissibility.
2
Understand the basis for exemption
For the traveler, sick, and blind, the basis is physical hardship (haraj) in reaching the mosque. For the slave and woman, it is their service obligations to master and husband respectively. The common thread is removal of harm and difficulty.
Hanafi fiqh recognizes 'haraj' as a valid cause for dispensation (rukhsah).
3
Analyze the ruling if they attend
The text states that if any of these individuals attend and pray Jumu'ah with the congregation, it suffices for the obligatory Zuhr of that time. Their prayer is valid and no makeup is required.
This ruling applies even though they were originally excused.
4
Trace the proof (qiyas)
The proof is an analogy: just as a traveler in Ramadan is allowed to skip fasting but if he fasts it is valid and even better, similarly the exempted persons, by attending Jumu'ah, have borne hardship, so their prayer is accepted.
The underlying principle is that the exemption was for ease, not because the act is inherently invalid for them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجب الجمعة على مسافر ولا امرأة ولا مريض ولا عبد ولا أعمى لأن المسافر يحرج في الحضور وكذا المريض والأعمى والعبد مشغول بخدمة المولى والمرأة بخدمة الزوج فعذر وادفعا للحرج والضرر

ترجمہ: اور جمعہ واجب نہیں کسی مسافر پر اور نہ عورت پر اور نہ بیمار پر اور نہ غلام پر اور نہ اندھے پر کیونکہ مسافر کو حاضری میں جہد و تشق لاحق ہو گا۔ اور یہی بیمار اور اندھے میں ہے اور غلام اپنے آقا کی خدمت میں مشغول ہے اور عورت اپنے شوہر کی خدمت میں مشغول رہتی ہے پس یہ لوگ حرج اور ضرر کو دور کرنے کے واسطے معذور قرار دیے گئے۔

تشریح: ادا جمعہ نہ مسافر پر واجب ہے نہ عورت پر نہ بیمار پر نہ غلام پر اور نہ نابینا پر دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسافر بیمار اور نابینا کو جمعہ میں ہونے سے حرج لاحق ہو گا اور غلام اپنے آقا کی خدمت میں اور عورت اپنے شوہر کی خدمت میں مشغول ہے۔ پس حرج اور ضرر کو دور کرنے کے لئے ان حضرات کو حاضری جمعہ سے معذور قرار دیا گیا۔

جن پر جمعہ فرض نہیں اگر انہوں نے جمعہ پڑھا تو وقتی فرض ادا ہو جائے گا

فإن حضروا فصلوا مع الناس أجزأهم عن فرض الوقت لأنهم تحملوه فصاروا كالمسافر إذا صام

ترجمہ: پھر یہ لوگ حاضر ہوئے اور انہوں نے لوگوں کے ساتھ جمعہ پڑھا تو اس وقت کے فرض سے ان کو جمعہ کافی ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ ان لوگوں نے حرج اور مشقت کو برداشت کیا تو ایسے مسافر کے مانند ہو گئے جس نے روزہ رکھا۔

تشریح: جن لوگوں کو ادا جمعہ سے معذور قرار دیا گیا ہے اگر انہوں نے جمعہ میں حاضر ہو کر لوگوں کے ساتھ نماز جمعہ ادا کی تو ان کا فریضہ وقت ادا ہو گیا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان لوگوں سے جمعہ کا ساقط ہونا کسی ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے نہیں تھا جو نماز میں پایا جائے بلکہ ان سے جن کو اور ضرر کو دور کرنے کے لئے فرضیت جمعہ ان سے اٹھالی گئی ہے۔ لیکن جب ان لوگوں نے حرج اور مشقت کو برداشت کیا اور ہمت کر کے لے کر نماز جمعہ ادا کر لی تو یہ لوگ اس مسافر کے مانند ہو گئے جس نے حالت سفر میں روزہ رکھا۔ حالانکہ بنظر مشتقت مسافر کو رمضان المبارک میں روزہ نہ رکھنے کی اجازت ہے لیکن اگر اس نے روزہ رکھ لیا تو جائز ہے بلکہ افضل ہے کیونکہ اس نے مقیم کی بہ نسبت زیادہ مشقت اٹھائی۔ اسی طرح اگر ان لوگوں نے مشقت اٹھا کر جمعہ کی نماز پڑھی تو جائز ہے۔
And Friday prayer is not obligatory for a traveler, nor a woman, nor a sick person, nor a slave, nor a blind person, because the traveler experiences hardship in attending, and likewise the sick and the blind; the slave is occupied with the service of his master, and the woman with the service of her husband. So these are excused to remove hardship and harm.

Explanation: It is said that Friday prayer is not obligatory for a traveler, woman, sick, slave, or blind. The proof is that the traveler, sick, and blind would face hardship in attending, and the slave is engaged in serving his master, and the woman in serving her husband. So to remove hardship and harm, these individuals are excused from attending Friday.

Those upon whom Friday is not obligatory, if they pray Friday, it will suffice for the obligatory of the time.

For if they attend and pray with the people, it suffices for them for the obligatory of the time, because they undertook (the hardship) and thus became like a traveler who fasts.

Translation: Then these people attended and prayed Friday with the people, so Friday sufficed for them for the obligatory of the time. Because they bore the hardship and toil, so they became like a traveler who fasted.

Explanation: Those who are excused from attending Friday, if they attend and pray Friday with the people, their obligatory of that time is fulfilled. The proof is that the dropping of Friday obligation from them was not due to something inherent in the prayer itself, but rather to remove hardship and harm. But when they bore the hardship and exerted themselves to pray Friday, they became like a traveler who fasts in the month of Ramadan. Although a traveler is permitted not to fast due to hardship, if he fasts, it is permissible, indeed better, because he endured more hardship than a resident. Similarly, if these people endure hardship and pray Friday, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on who is exempted from the obligation of Friday prayer and the ruling if they attend. The exempted categories are: traveler (musafir), woman, sick person (mariid), slave (abd), and blind person (a'ma). The reason is hardship: the traveler faces difficulty in reaching the mosque, the sick and blind face physical hardship, the slave is bound to serve his master, and the woman is bound to serve her husband. These are excused to avoid hardship and harm. However, if any of these individuals choose to attend and pray Friday with the congregation, their Friday prayer is valid and suffices for the obligatory Zuhr prayer of that time. The proof is analogical: just as a traveler in Ramadan is allowed to skip fasting due to hardship, but if he fasts, it is valid and even praiseworthy because he endured extra hardship. Similarly, the exempted individuals, by attending Friday, have taken on hardship, so their prayer is valid. The underlying principle is that the exemption was for their ease, not because the act itself is invalid for them. Thus, if they choose to perform it, it is accepted.

Key Terms
حرج (haraj): Hardship or difficulty that excuses an obligation.
مسافر (musafir): A traveler who has left his hometown with the intention of traveling a distance (approx. 48 miles or 3 days according to Hanafi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A sick person is excused from attending Friday prayer. If he decides to attend and prays Friday with the congregation, what is the ruling?
A) His Friday prayer is invalid because he was exempted.
B) His Friday prayer is valid and suffices for the obligatory Zuhr.
C) He must pray both Friday and Zuhr to be safe.
D) His prayer is valid only if he was not severely ill.

Key Takeaway
Exemption from Jumu'ah is based on hardship, but if the exempted choose to attend, their prayer is valid and fulfills the obligation.

Can an Exempted Person Lead Jumu'ah? – Hanafi View vs. Zufar
Ruling on who can lead Jumu'ah as imam; dispute with Zufar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a traveler, slave, or sick person leading Jumu'ah prayer and explain why Zufar's objection is rejected based on the distinction between rukhsah and legal capacity.

Core Idea
A concession (rukhsah) does not disqualify; legal capacity (ahliyyah) is the criterion for imamah.

The Hanafi school generally permits those excused from Friday attendance to lead it if they choose to come. This lesson examines the specific ruling for travelers, slaves, and the sick, and the objection raised by Imam Zufar. You will learn why the majority Hanafis differentiate between lack of obligation and lack of capacity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that a traveler, slave, or sick person may validly lead Friday prayer.
2
Identify Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that since Friday is not obligatory on them, they are like a boy or a woman, whose imamah is invalid.
3
Analyze Zufar's analogy (qiyas)
Zufar analogizes the exempted individuals to those permanently disqualified: a boy lacks legal capacity, a woman cannot lead men.
His illa (effective cause) is 'lack of obligation'.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The exemption is a concession (rukhsah), not a permanent disqualification. When they attend, the obligation attaches. Unlike boys (no capacity) and women (gender restriction), these individuals have legal capacity and are fit for imamah.
The Hanafi response distinguishes the illa.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, according to the majority, these individuals can lead; under Zufar's view, they cannot. The text sides with the majority.
This difference affects actual practice in mosques.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز للمسافر والعبد والمريض أن يؤم في الجمعة وقال زفر لا يجزيه لأنه لا فرض عليه فشبه الصبي والمرأة ولنا أن هذه رخصة فإذا حضروا يقع فرضا على ما بينا أما الصبي فمسلوب الأهلية والمرأة لا تصلح لإمامة الرجال وتنعقد بهم الجمعة لأنهم صلحوا للإمامة فيصلحون للاقتداء بطريق الأولى

ترجمہ: اور مسافر اور غلام اور بیمار کے لئے جمعہ میں امام بننا جائز ہے۔ اور امام زفر نے کہا ہے کہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس پر جمعہ فرض نہیں ہے۔ پس (ہر ایک) بچہ اور عورت کے مشابہ ہوگیا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ فرض نہ ہوتا رخصت ہے۔ لیکن جب یہ لوگ حاضر ہوگئے تو یہ نماز فرض واقع ہوگی جیسا کہ ہم نے بیان کیا ہے۔ رہا بچہ تو اس میں امامت کی اہلیت نہیں ہے۔ اور عورت مردوں کی امامت کی اہلیت نہیں رکھتی۔ اور مسافر غلام بیمار کے ساتھ جمعہ منعقد ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ یہ لوگ امامت کے لائق ہیں پس اقتداء کے لئے بطریق اولیٰ ہے۔
And it is permissible for a traveler, a slave, and a sick person to lead Friday prayer. Zufar said: It is not permissible, because Friday is not obligatory upon him, so he resembles a boy and a woman. Our proof is that this is a concession. So when they attend, it becomes obligatory upon them, as we have explained. As for the boy, he lacks legal capacity. And the woman is not fit to lead men in prayer. And Friday is valid with the presence of a traveler, slave, and sick, because they are fit for imamah, so by more reason they are fit for following (iqtida').
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage addresses who can serve as imam for Friday prayer. The ruling: a traveler, a slave, and a sick person are allowed to lead the Friday prayer. Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) disagreed, arguing that since Friday is not obligatory upon them, they are like a boy (who cannot be imam at all) or a woman (who cannot lead men). The Hanafi response is that their exemption from obligation is a concession (rukhsah) for their own attendance, not a disqualification from leadership. When they choose to attend, the prayer becomes obligatory upon them and they are valid as imams. A boy is excluded because he lacks legal capacity (ahliyyah) for imamah, and a woman is excluded because she cannot lead men. The text argues via a fortiori (bi tariq al-ula): if they are fit to be imams, they are certainly fit to be followers. The Friday prayer is valid with their presence as imam or follower.

Key Terms
امامت (imamah): The act of leading prayer as an imam.
رخصت (rukhsah): A concession or dispensation granted due to hardship, as opposed to the original ruling ('azimah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, it is permissible.
B) No, because Friday is not obligatory upon him.
C) Only if he is freed that day.
D) Only if he has permission from his master.

Key Takeaway
A traveler, slave, or sick person may lead Friday prayer because their exemption is a concession, not a disqualification; they have legal capacity.

Exemption from Jumu'ah and Validity of Attendance
Explaining exemption and validity of attendance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five categories exempt from Jumu'ah and explain why their attendance fulfills the obligation.

Core Idea
Exemption from Jumu'ah is a concession for hardship, but attendance still counts for the fard.

Friday prayer is wajib on every free, male, adult, resident Muslim who is healthy and sighted. However, Allah grants concessions (rukhsah) for those facing genuine hardship. This passage lists the exempted individuals and clarifies that their voluntary attendance is valid and fulfills the obligation, drawing a parallel to a traveler who chooses to fast in Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exempted categories
List the five types of people mentioned: traveler, woman, sick, blind, and slave. Note the reason given for each (e.g., slave busy serving master, woman serving husband, sick/blind face difficulty).
2
Understand the basis of exemption
The exemption is based on removing hardship (haraj) and harm (darar). This is a rukhsah (concession), not a negation of the general command. Jumu'ah remains wajib in principle, but these individuals are excused.
Hanafi usul: rukhsah does not imply the act is not praiseworthy.
3
Analyze the effect of attendance
If any exempted person attends Jumu'ah and prays with the congregation, it fulfills the fard of that time (Zuhr). This is because they voluntarily undertook the obligation, just as a traveler who fasts in Ramadan fulfills the duty.
The analogy (qiyas) with the traveler fasting highlights that voluntary assumption of obligation is valid.
4
Trace the underlying talil (legal reasoning)
The passage uses talil: the reason attendance is valid is that they undertook it (tahammulu). The principle: a concession does not bar the act from fulfilling the duty if performed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلواة الجمعة المريض والاعمى والعبد مشغول بخدمة المولى والمرأة بخدمة الزوج فعذر وادفعا للحرج والضرر فان حضروا فصلوا مع الناس اجزاهم عن فرض الوقت لانهم تحملوه فصاروا كا لمسافر اذا صاد
Chapter of Friday Prayer. The sick, the blind, and the slave are busy with the service of their master, and the woman with the service of her husband, so they are excused to remove hardship and harm. If they attend and pray with the people, it suffices them from the fard of the time because they undertook it, so they become like the traveler when he fasts.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on who is exempt from Friday prayer and what happens if they attend. The text first lists those on whom Jumu'ah is not wajib: the traveler, woman, sick, slave, and blind. The reason given is that these individuals face hardship in attending. The slave is occupied with his master's service, the woman with her husband's service, and the sick and blind face difficulty. Then the ruling: if they do attend and pray Jumu'ah with the congregation, it suffices for the fard prayer of that time (i.e., Zuhr). This is because they have voluntarily undertaken the hardship, similar to a traveler who chooses to fast in Ramadan despite being permitted not to. The underlying principle is that the obligation of Jumu'ah is lifted from them due to hardship (haraj), but if they choose to perform it, the obligation is fulfilled. This is based on the general command in Surah al-Jumu'ah (62:9) which is addressed to all believers, but the exemption is a concession (rukhsah) for those with valid excuses.

Key Terms
حرج (haraj): Hardship or difficulty that provides a valid excuse for exemption from an obligation.
رخصة (rukhsah): A concession granted due to necessity or hardship, allowing relaxation of a general ruling.
تحمل (tahammul): To undertake or bear a duty voluntarily.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He does not need to pray Zuhr; Jumu'ah suffices.
C) He must pray both Jumu'ah and Zuhr to be safe.
D) His Jumu'ah is invalid, so he must pray Zuhr.

Key Takeaway
Exemption from Jumu'ah due to hardship does not invalidate voluntary attendance; it fulfills the obligation.

Imamate of Traveler, Slave, and Sick Person in Jumu'ah
Hanafi ruling on imamate of exempted individuals with intra-school dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the imamate of travelers, slaves, and the sick in Jumu'ah, and explain the rebuttal of Zufar's objection using the distinction between rukhsah and inherent incapacity.

Core Idea
A concession (rukhsah) does not diminish capacity; thus, the exempted may lead Jumu'ah when they attend.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: can those who are exempt from Jumu'ah still lead it? Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn rule yes, while Zufar dissents. The underlying issue is whether the non-obligation of Jumu'ah on these individuals makes them unfit to be imams, similar to a child or a woman. The Hanafi response clarifies the nature of the exemption as a concession, not a defect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State clearly that according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, a traveler, slave, and sick person may lead Jumu'ah.
2
Pinpoint Zufar's objection and his analogy
Zufar argues that since Jumu'ah is not obligatory on these individuals, they are like a child or a woman who cannot lead.
Zufar's qiyas: non-obligation as the illa.
3
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis distinguish the non-obligation: for the traveler/slave/sick, it is a rukhsah (concession), not a defect. The child lacks capacity (salbul-ahliyyah) and the woman cannot lead men due to a textual prohibition.
Thus, the illa is not common; the analogy fails.
4
Apply the qiyas awwlawi argument
If they are fit to lead (since their prayer becomes fard upon attendance), they are even more fit to be followed.
This strengthens the Hanafi position.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: Zufar would require the imam to be one on whom Jumu'ah is obligatory; the Hanafi position allows a broader range. The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position.
This is the operative fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز للمسافر والعبد والمريض ان يؤم فى الجمعة وقال زفر لا يجزيه لانه لا فرض عليه فاشبه الصبى والمرأة ولنا ان هذه رخصة فاذا حضروا يقع فرضا على ما بينا اما الصبى فمسلوب الاهلية والمرأة لا تصلح لامامة الرجال وتنعقدبهم الجمعة لا نهم صلحوا للامامة فيصلحون للاقتداء بطريق الأولى
It is permissible for the traveler, the slave, and the sick person to lead in Friday prayer. Zufar said: It is not valid because Friday is not obligatory on him, so he resembles the boy and the woman. Our proof: This is a concession. When they attend, it becomes obligatory as we explained. As for the boy, he is lacking in capacity. The woman is not fit to lead men. And Friday prayer is valid with them because they are fit for leading, thus they are even more fit for following.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of who can serve as imam for Jumu'ah prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa and the majority of Hanafi scholars (including Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that a traveler, a slave, and a sick person may lead the Jumu'ah prayer if they attend. Zufar, a Hanafi scholar, disagreed, arguing that since Jumu'ah is not obligatory on them, they are like a child (who has no legal capacity) or a woman (who cannot lead men), and thus their imamate is invalid. The Hanafi response is that the non-obligation of Jumu'ah on them is a concession due to hardship, not a negation of their capacity. When they attend, the prayer becomes their obligatory prayer (fard). A child is completely without capacity (salbul-ahliyyah), and a woman cannot lead men because of the hadith 'A people will never prosper who appoint a woman over them.' Since these individuals are fit to lead (because they can perform a valid Jumu'ah that is fard for them), they are even more fit to be followed. This establishes their permissibility as imams.

Key Terms
إمامة (imamah): Leading the congregational prayer.
مسلوب الأهلية (maslub al-ahliyyah): Deprived of legal capacity; specifically a child who is not fully mukallaf.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Not permissible because Jumu'ah is not wajib on him
B) Permissible because his Jumu'ah becomes fard when he attends
C) Only if he is the only person present
D) Permissible only if he is not sick

Key Takeaway
A traveler, slave, or sick person may lead Jumu'ah because their attendance makes it fard, and the exemption is a concession, not a defect in capacity.

Zuhr Before Jumu'ah: Valid but Disliked
Ruling that praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse is makruh but valid, with response to Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi ruling on praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse and explain the dispute with Zufar, using the principle that obligation revolves around ability.

Core Idea
Zuhr remains the original fard; Jumu'ah is a command to drop it, not a replacement.

This passage addresses a common scenario: someone prays Zuhr at home on Friday before the Jumu'ah prayer and has no excuse. Is their prayer valid? The Hanafi school says it is valid but disliked, while a student of Abu Hanifa, Zufar, disagreed. We will explore the proofs and the key principle that obligation revolves around ability.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn: the Zuhr prayer is valid but makruh (disliked) if performed before Jumu'ah without a valid excuse.
Makruh in this context is makruh tanzihi (disliked, not sinful).
2
Identify the opposing view of Zufar
Zufar holds that the Zuhr prayer is invalid. Understand his reasoning: he considers Jumu'ah as the original fard on Friday and Zuhr merely as a substitute (badal), and one cannot resort to a substitute when able to perform the original.
Zufar was a prominent Hanafi student, but his view is not adopted in the madhhab.
3
Follow Zufar's proof
Examine Zufar's dalil: Jumu'ah replaces Zuhr as the primary obligation; therefore, when conditions for Jumu'ah are met, Zuhr is no longer an obligation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the original fard is still Zuhr for everyone. The command to perform Jumu'ah is a command to drop (isqat) the Zuhr obligation, not a substitution. The person can perform Zuhr alone because he has ability over it, but Jumu'ah depends on conditions beyond his individual control.
The key principle is that taklif (obligation) is based on ability (tamakkun).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Zufar, the person must still pray Jumu'ah or later repeat Zuhr; according to the Hanafi majority, his Zuhr prayer fulfills the obligation, though he should have attended Jumu'ah.
This difference affects whether qada is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن صلى الظهر فى منزله يوم الجمعة قبل صلوة الامام ولا عذر له كره له ذلك وجازت صلاته وقال زفر لايجزيه لان عنده الجمعة هى الفريضة اصالة والظهر كالبدل عنها ولا مصير الى البدل مع القدرة على الاصل ولنا اصل الفرض هو الظهر فى حق الكافة هذا هو الظاهر الا انه مامور باسقاطه بادا الجمعة وهذا لانه تمكن من ادا الظهر بنفسه دون الجمعة لتوقفها على شرائط لا تتم به وحده وعلى التكمن يدور التكليف
Whoever prays Zuhr in his house on Friday before the Imam's prayer and has no excuse, that is disliked (makruh) for him, but his prayer is valid. Zufar said: It is not valid, because in his view Jumu'ah is the original fard, and Zuhr is like a substitute for it, and one does not resort to the substitute when able to perform the original. Our proof: The original fard is Zuhr for everyone; this is apparent, except that one is commanded to drop it by performing Jumu'ah, and this is because he is able to perform Zuhr by himself without Jumu'ah, whereas Jumu'ah depends on conditions not complete by him alone, and obligation revolves around ability.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation of a person who prays Zuhr at home on Friday before the Imam leads Jumu'ah, without having any valid excuse (such as travel, sickness, etc.). According to Abu Hanifa and the majority, this action is makruh (disliked) but the Zuhr prayer is valid and fulfills the obligation of that time. Zufar disagrees, holding that the prayer is invalid. Zufar's reasoning is that Jumu'ah has replaced Zuhr as the original fard on Friday; Zuhr is merely a substitute (badal) that is only valid when Jumu'ah cannot be performed. Since this person had the ability to attend Jumu'ah, he cannot resort to the substitute. The Hanafi response is that the original fard for everyone on Friday is still Zuhr. The command to perform Jumu'ah is a command to drop (isqat) the obligation of Zuhr by performing Jumu'ah. However, Zuhr can be performed alone, while Jumu'ah depends on conditions (like congregation, khutbah, etc.) that are not all within his individual control. Since obligation is based on ability, the person has ability for Zuhr but not complete control over Jumu'ah conditions. Therefore, if he chooses to pray Zuhr alone before Jumu'ah, it is valid (though it is makruh because he abandoned the communal obligation unnecessarily). This principle highlights that in the Hanafi school, the primary obligation on Friday is Zuhr, but the community is collectively commanded to substitute it with Jumu'ah when conditions are met.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): A substitute or replacement for an original obligation.
أصل (asl): The original ruling or obligation.
تكليف (taklif): Legal obligation imposed on a mukallaf based on ability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if someone prays Zuhr at home on Friday before the Jumu'ah prayer and has no valid excuse?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
B) The prayer is valid but makruh
C) The prayer is valid and recommended
D) The prayer is invalid unless he also prays Jumu'ah

Key Takeaway
Praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse is valid because obligation is based on ability, but it is disliked due to leaving the communal duty.

The Permissibility of Travelers, Sick, and Slaves Leading Friday Prayer
Dispute on imamah of non-obligated individuals in Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a traveler, sick person, or slave leading Jumu'ah, explain the Hanafi proof from the Quran and the concept of concession, and evaluate the opposing views of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i.

Core Idea
When a traveler attends Jumu'ah, it becomes obligatory for him — thus he is fit to lead.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key dispute: can a person who is not originally obligated for Jumu'ah lead it? The Hanafi school says yes, but only when they attend and thereby assume the obligation. Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i have reservations. Let's unpack the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that it is permissible (jai'iz) for a traveler, sick person, or slave to lead the Friday prayer when they attend.
This is based on the general address of Quran 62:9.
2
Present Imam Zufar's objection
Imam Zufar argues that these individuals are like minors and women, who cannot lead, because Jumu'ah is not obligatory for them.
He uses qiyas (analogy) on the basis of non-obligation.
3
Present the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response distinguishes: their non-obligation is a concession (rukhsat) to remove hardship. When they attend, they voluntarily bear the hardship, so the prayer becomes obligatory for them.
Thus they are no longer like minors or women.
4
Distinguish from minors and women
Minors are not addressed by divine commands at all, so they lack capacity for imamah. Women have capacity to lead women but not men. Travelers, sick, and slaves are fully addressed and become obligated upon attendance.
The analogy fails because the illa (cause) is different.
5
Address Shafi'i's second issue
Imam Shafi'i agrees that such persons can lead, but he argues that Jumu'ah is not established if only they gather. The Hanafi response: if they are fit to lead (imamah), they are a fortiori fit to follow (iqtida'), so the congregation is valid.
This is based on the principle of 'awla (more fitting).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة الجمعة
سے حرج شرتی مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مسافر بیمار اور غلام پر اگر چہ معہ فرض نہیں ہے لیکن ان کو جمعہ میں امام بنانا جائز ہے۔ امام شافعی کا اصح قول بھی ہی ہے۔ امام زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ ان میں سے کسی کا امام جمعہ ہونا جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمعہ فرض نہ ہونے میں یہ تینوں تا ہے۔ ا بالغ بچہ اور عورت کے مشابہ ہیں پس جس طرح بچہ اور عورت کی امامت جمعہ جائز نہیں ہے اسی طرح ان کی امامت بھی جائز نہ ہوگی۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسافر غلام اور بیمار پر جمعہ کا فرض نہ ہونا بطور رخصت ہے یعنی جمعہ تو ہر ایک پر فرض عین ہے کیونکہ خطاب
دَانُودِيَ لِلصَّلوةِ مِنْ يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوا إلى ذكر الله عام ہے لیکن مسافر وغیرہ کو حرج دور کرنے کے لئے جمعہ میں حاضر نہ ہونے کی اجازت دیدی گئی ہے۔ مگر جب یہ لوگ ادا جمعہ کے لئے حاضر ہو گئے اور حرج ضرر کی مشقت برداشت کر لی تو یہ نماز فرض ہوگی نہ کر نفل جیسا کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ پس جب مسافر وغیرہ کی نماز جمعہ فرض واقع ہوئی تو ان کو امام بنانا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ رہا بچہ اور عورت پر نیاں تو وہ صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ نابالغ بچہ میں امامت کی اہلیت ہی نہیں ہے۔ اور امامت کی اہلیت اس لئے نہیں کہ خطاب باری اس کو شامل نہیں ہے پس جب بچہ امامت کی اہلیت ہی نہیں رکھتا تو اس کو امام بنانا کیسے درست ہو گا۔ اور رہی عورت تو اس میں عورتوں کی امامت کی ونکہ ان بیت تو ہے مگر مردوں کی امامت کی اہلیت نہیں ہے۔ اور جب مردوں کی امامت کی اہلیت نہیں تو عورت کو مردوں کی امامت کا حکم جواز بھی حاصل نہ ہو گا۔ حضرت امام شافعی کہتے ہیں کہ مسافر غلام اور بیمار کی امامت جمعہ تو درست ہے لیکن اگر جمعہ منعقد کرنے کے لئے فقط یہ لوگ تو ان کا اس تعداد کے مطابق بھی ہوں جس تعداد سے جمعہ منعقد ہو جاتا ہے۔ تو جمعہ منعقد نہیں ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے امام شافعی کے اس قول کو رد سے حرج کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ مسافر غلام اور بیمار کے جمع ہونے سے جماعت جمعہ منعقد ہو جائے گی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب یہ لوگ امامت کے کر کے لائق ہیں تو اقتداء کے لائق بدرجہ اولی ہوں گے۔
Chapter of Friday Prayer. The issue of difficulty [or condition?]: The traveler, sick person, and slave, even though Friday prayer is not obligatory upon them, it is permissible for them to lead the Friday prayer. Imam Shafi'i's soundest opinion is also this. Imam Zufar said that it is not permissible for any of them to be the imam of Friday prayer. Imam Zufar's proof is that in not being obligatory, these three are similar to a minor boy and a woman. So just as the imamah of a boy and a woman in Friday prayer is not permissible, similarly their imamah will not be permissible. Our proof is that the non-obligation of Friday upon the traveler, sick, and slave is by way of concession; that is, Friday prayer is obligatory upon everyone because the address (and call to prayer on Friday, so hasten to the remembrance of Allah) is general, but the traveler etc. are given permission not to attend Friday prayer to remove hardship. However, when these people attend to perform Friday prayer and bear the hardship and harm, then this prayer becomes obligatory, not supererogatory, as we have explained. So when the Friday prayer of the traveler etc. becomes obligatory, it is also permissible for them to be imam. As for the boy and woman, it is not correct because a minor boy does not have the qualification for imamah; and he does not have qualification because the divine address does not include him. So when the boy does not have the qualification for imamah, how can it be correct to make him imam? As for the woman, she has the qualification for imamah of women, but not for imamah of men. And when she does not have qualification for imamah of men, she does not obtain the ruling of permissibility for leading men. Hadrat Imam Shafi'i says that the imamah of the traveler, sick, and slave in Friday prayer is correct, but if only these people are present for the establishment of Friday prayer, even if they are in the number by which Friday prayer is established, then Friday prayer will not be established. The author of Hidayah, refuting and rejecting this statement of Imam Shafi'i, says that the congregation of Friday prayer will be established by the gathering of the traveler, sick, and slave. The proof is that when these people are fit to lead (imamah), then they are even more fit to follow (iqtida).
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a legal dispute (inter-madhhab) concerning the permissibility of a traveler (musafir), sick person (marid), or slave (ghulam) leading Friday prayer. The Hanafi position is that it is permissible for them to be imam when they attend, and the Friday congregation is valid with their presence. Imam Zufar forbids it, analogizing them to minors and women. Imam Shafi'i agrees on permissibility of imamah but denies the validity of the congregation if only such persons gather. The Hanafi response emphasizes that their non-obligation is a concession (rukhsat); when they attend, the prayer becomes obligatory for them, making them fit for imamah and iqtida'. Minors are not addressed by divine commands, and women lack capacity to lead men. The author of Hidayah affirms the Hanafi view, stating that those fit to lead are a fortiori fit to follow.

Key Terms
امامت (imamah): The act of leading congregational prayer.
مسافر (musafir): Traveler who is exempted from Jumu'ah due to journey.
حرج (haraj): Hardship or difficulty that qualifies a concession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a traveler (musafir) leading the Friday prayer?
A) It is not permissible; only residents may lead.
B) It is permissible (jai'iz) because when he attends, the prayer becomes obligatory for him.
C) It is obligatory upon him to lead if he is present.
D) It is makruh for him to lead.

Key Takeaway
A person not originally obligated for Jumu'ah may lead it if he attends, because the prayer becomes obligatory for him upon attendance.

The Validity of Zuhr Before Friday Prayer: A Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that Zuhr prayed before Jumu'ah without excuse is valid but makruh, and evaluate the opposing arguments.

Core Idea
Zuhr remains the original obligation on Friday; Jumu'ah is a means to drop it, not a replacement.

This passage addresses a critical dispute in Friday prayer: can a person validly pray Zuhr at home before attending Jumu'ah? The Hanafi school declares it valid yet makruh, while Imam Zufar, Shafi'i, and Maliki rule it invalid. Understanding the reasoning behind each position sharpens your ability to analyze obligation and substitution in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly does the Hanafi school rule regarding praying Zuhr at home on Friday before the imam's prayer? Identify both the validity and the level of dislike.
The ruling is 'jai'iz but makruh'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which scholars or schools oppose the Hanafi position? What do they rule instead? Note that Imam Zufar (within Hanafi) agrees with Shafi'i and Maliki.
Opponents say the Zuhr is invalid.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What is the basis of the opposing argument? They claim that Jumu'ah is the original obligation and Zuhr is a substitute. Explain the reasoning using the hadith and the principle of original vs substitute.
They argue: one cannot resort to the substitute when capable of the original.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut the opponent? Cite the hadith about Zuhr's time being general, and the principle that obligation is based on capability.
The Hanafi response emphasizes that Zuhr is the original fard for all days, and Jumu'ah is a mechanism to drop it.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence of this disagreement? How does the ruling differ in practice for a person who prayed Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse?
Hanafis consider it valid; others require the person to repeat Zuhr after Jumu'ah.

Source Text
