کسی نے جمعہ کے دن ظہر کی نماز امام سے پہلے پڑھ لی اور کوئی عذر مانع بھی نہیں تھا تو ایسا کرنا مکروہ ہے آیا ظہر کی نماز ہوئی یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء
ومن صلى الظهر فى منزله يوم الجمعة قبل صلوة الامام ولا عذر له كره له ذلك وجازت صلاته وقال زفر لايجزيه لان عنده الجمعة هى الفريضة اصالة والظهر كالبدل عنها ولا مصير الى البدل مع القدرة على الاصل ولنا اصل الفرض هو الظهر فى حق الكافة هذا هو الظاهر الا انه مامور باسقاطه بادا الجمعة وهذا لانه تمكن من ادا الظهر بنفسه دون الجمعة لتوقفها على شرائط لا تتم به وحده وعلى التكمن يدور التكليف
رجمہ اور جس شخص نے جمعہ کے روز اپنے مقام پر امام کی نماز سے پہلے ظہر پڑھ لی حالانکہ اس کو کوئی عذر بھی نہیں ہے تو اس کے حق میں یہ مکروہ ہے۔ اور نماز جائز ہوگئی ۔ اور امام زفر نے کہا ہے کہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ امام زفر کے نزدیک اصلی فرض تو جمعہ اور ظہر اس کے بدل کے مانند ہے اور اصل پر قدرت کرے رہتے ہوئے بدل کی طرف رجوع نہیں کیا جاتا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تمام کے حق میں
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے جمعہ کے دن امام کے نماز جمعہ پڑھانے سے پہلے اپنے گھر میں نماز ظہر پڑھی۔ حالانکہ اس کو کوئی عذر بھی نہیں ہے تو اس کی یہ نماز جائز تو ہوگئی لیکن مکروہ ہے۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ جائز نہیں ہوئی یہی امام مالک اور امام شافعی کا قول ہے۔ ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمعہ کے دن نماز جمعہ ہی اصلاً فرض ہے۔ اور ظہر اس کا بدل ہے کیونکہ نماز جمعہ کی طرف بھی کا امر کیا گیا ہے اور جب تک جمعہ فوت نہ ہو جائے ظہر پڑھنے سے منع کیا گیا ہے پس نماز جمعہ کا مامور بالا دا ء ہونا اور ظہر کا ممنوع ہونا نماز جمعہ کے فرض اصلی ہونے کی دلیل ہے اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ جب تک اصل پر قدرت ہو تو بدل کی طرف رجوع نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ لہذا انماز جمعہ پر قادر ہونے کی صورت میں ظہر کا ادا کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمعہ کے دن اصلا تو ظہر فرض ہے جیسا کہ دوسرے ایام میں ظہر فرض ہے۔ دلیل حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا قول اول وقت الظهر حين تزول الشمس ہے۔ بایں طور کہ حدیث مطلق ہے کسی دن کی تخصیص نہیں ہے۔ لہذا از وال شمس کے بعد تمام ایام میں بلا استثنا، ظہر کا وقت ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تکلیف بحسب القدرت ہوتی ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ربانی ہے لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا الأوسعها اور اس وقت کے اندر نماز کا مکلف بذات خود ظہر ادا کرنے پر قادر ہے نہ کہ جمعہ ادا کرنے پڑ کیونکہ جمعہ ایسی شرائط پر موقوف ہے جو تنہا ایک آدمی کے ساتھ پوری نہیں ہوتیں، مثلاً امام کا ہونا جماعت کا ہونا وغیرہ پس جمعہ کا مکلف بنانا تکلیف مالا يطاق کے قبیل سے ہوگا۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ جمعہ کے دن جمعہ ادا کر کے ظہر کی نماز ساقط کرنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے پس قدرت کے باوجود جمعہ سے اعراض برتر ہو۔ کر کے ظہر ادا کرنا جائز مگر مگر وہ ہوگا۔
Someone prayed Zuhr on Friday before the imam's prayer and there was no preventing excuse, so doing so is makruh; is the Zuhr prayer performed or not? Statements of jurists. And whoever prays Zuhr in his house on Friday before the imam's prayer and he has no excuse, it is makruh for him and his prayer is valid. Zufar said it is not valid because in his view Friday is the original obligation and Zuhr is like a substitute for it, and one does not resort to the substitute while able to perform the original. And our proof is that the original obligation is Zuhr for all people; this is apparent, except that he is commanded to drop it by performing Friday prayer, and this is because he is able to perform Zuhr by himself without Friday, because Friday depends on conditions not fulfilled by him alone, and obligation revolves around capability. And the person who prayed Zuhr at his place on the day of Friday before the imam's prayer while he has no excuse, then for him this is makruh, and the prayer is valid. Imam Zufar said it is not valid because according to him the original obligation is Friday and Zuhr is like its substitute, and one does not turn to the substitute while having power over the original. And our proof is that for all people the original obligation is Zuhr. Elaboration of the issue: If someone prayed Zuhr in his house on Friday before the imam leads the Friday prayer, and he has no excuse, then his prayer is valid but makruh. Imam Zufar said it is not valid, and this is the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i. Their proof is that on Friday, Friday prayer itself is originally obligatory, and Zuhr is its substitute because the command is given to Friday prayer and one is forbidden to pray Zuhr until Friday is missed. So the commandedness of Friday prayer and the prohibition of Zuhr indicate that Friday is the original obligation. And it is accepted that as long as one is able to perform the original, one does not resort to the substitute. Therefore, when able to pray Friday, performing Zuhr is not valid. Our proof is that on Friday, originally Zuhr is obligatory, as on other days. The proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The time of Zuhr begins when the sun passes the meridian.' Thus, the hadith is absolute, not specifying any day. So after the sun passes the meridian, on all days without exception, it is the time of Zuhr. The second proof is that obligation is according to capability, as the divine saying: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' And at that time, the person obligated is able to perform Zuhr himself, not to perform Friday, because Friday depends on conditions not fulfilled by one person alone, such as the presence of an imam and congregation. Thus, obligating Friday would be a kind of impossible obligation. However, it is necessary that on Friday, by performing Friday prayer, the obligation of Zuhr is dropped. So, despite being able to pray Friday, deliberately turning away from it and praying Zuhr is permissible but makruh.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on a person who prays Zuhr at home on Friday before the imam's Jumu'ah prayer without a valid excuse. The Hanafi school holds that this Zuhr is valid (because the original obligation for the day is Zuhr), but it is makruh because it involves abandoning the superior Jumu'ah. Imam Zufar, along with Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i, considers the Zuhr invalid, arguing that Jumu'ah is the primary obligation and Zuhr is merely a substitute; one cannot resort to the substitute when capable of the original. The Hanafi response cites the hadith that the time for Zuhr begins at zawal, which is general for all days, and the principle that obligation is based on capability. Since a person is capable of praying Zuhr individually but not Jumu'ah on his own, the original obligation remains Zuhr. Jumu'ah is a means to drop the Zuhr obligation when conditions are met. Therefore, praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah is valid but disliked.

Key Terms
ظہر (zuhr): The noon prayer, considered the original daily obligation.
بدل (badal): Substitute; here, Zuhr is considered a substitute for Jumu'ah by opponents.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; an action that is not sinful but contrary to what is better.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a person prays Zuhr at home on Friday before the imam prays Jumu'ah and has no excuse, his Zuhr is:
A) Invalid and must be repeated after Jumu'ah.
B) Valid but makruh.
C) Valid and recommended (mustahab).
D) Invalid unless he attends Jumu'ah.

Key Takeaway
Zuhr on Friday remains the original fard; praying it before Jumu'ah is valid but makruh because Jumu'ah is the superior obligation.

Invalidation of Zuhr When Setting Out for Jumu'ah After Praying It
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether starting to walk to Jumu'ah invalidates earlier Zuhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether walking to Jumu'ah invalidates an earlier Zuhr, and state the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Walking to Jumu'ah: for Abu Hanifa it voids Zuhr; for Sahibayn only joining the imam does.

Imagine you have already performed Zuhr individually, then decide to attend Jumu'ah. What happens to your Zuhr? This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the act of walking (sa'y) towards Jumu'ah, while the imam is still in prayer, invalidates the earlier Zuhr out of precaution. His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree, arguing that only actually joining the Jumu'ah congregation can break the completed Zuhr. Understanding this ikhtilaf illuminates how Hanafi jurists weigh the specific characteristics of an act (sa'y) against general analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two conflicting rulings from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. According to Abu Hanifa, when does the Zuhr become invalid? According to the Sahibayn, when does it become invalid?
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, so both positions are within the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing views and their evidence
Write the proofs of each side. The Sahibayn use qiyas: sa'y is inferior to Zuhr, so it cannot break it; only Jumu'ah itself is superior. Abu Hanifa uses the specific characteristic of sa'y as a distinctive element of Jumu'ah, so out of precaution (ihtiyat) it is treated like Jumu'ah itself.
Abu Hanifa's proof is dalil 'aqli based on the special nature of sa'y.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain why Abu Hanifa rejects the analogy of attending after the imam finishes. He distinguishes between walking while the imam is in prayer (sa'y during Jumu'ah) and walking after it (sa'y not specific to Jumu'ah). The former takes the rank of Jumu'ah due to its connection.
The key is the timing and the ongoing Jumu'ah.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: According to Abu Hanifa, if the person walks, his Zuhr is void and he must pray Jumu'ah. According to the Sahibayn, his Zuhr remains valid unless he actually joins the Jumu'ah congregation.
This affects whether the person needs to repeat Zuhr if he changes his mind.

Source Text

فان بدا له ان يحضرها فتوجه اليها والامام فيها بطل ظهره عند ابي حنيفة بالسعى وقالا لا يبطل حتى يدخل مع الامام لان السعى دون الظهر فلا ينقضه بعد تمامه والجمعة فوقها فينقضها وصار كما اذا توجه بعد فراغ الامام وله ان السعى الى الجمعة من خصائص الجمعة فينزل منزلتها فى حق ارتقاض الظهر احتياطا بخلاف ما بعد الفراغ منها لانه ليس بسعى اليها
ترجمہ پھر اگر اس کی رائے میں ظاہر ہوا کہ جمعہ میں حاضر ہو جائے پس جمعہ کی طرف متوجہ ہوا حال یہ کہ امام نماز جمعہ میں ہے تو ام ہونے کے ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک چلنے کے ساتھ ہی اس کی ظہر باطل ہو جائے گی اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ ظہر باطل نہ ہوگی یہاں تک کہ امام کے ساتھ داخل ہو جائے کیونکہ سعی ظہر سے کمتر ہے تو ظہر مکمل ہونے کے بعد سعی اس کو نہ توڑے گی۔ اور جمعہ ظہر سے بڑھ کر ہے۔ لہذا جمعہ جمعہ کی طرح ظہر کو توڑ دے گا اور ایسا ہو گیا جیسے امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد جمعہ کی طرف متوجہ ہوا۔ اور امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سمعی الی الجمعہ جمعہ کی خصوصیات میں سے ہے پس ظہر توڑنے کے حق میں احتیاطاً سعی کو جمعہ کے مرتبہ میں اتار لیا جائے گا بر خلاف اس کے کہ امام جمعہ
Then if it becomes apparent to him to attend it (Jumu'ah), so he goes towards it while the imam is in it, then according to Abu Hanifa, his Zuhr becomes invalid by (his) walking, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It does not become invalid until he enters with the imam, because walking is inferior to Zuhr, so it does not break it after its completion. And Jumu'ah is superior to it, so it breaks it. And it becomes as if he went after the imam finished. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that walking to Jumu'ah is from the specific characteristics of Jumu'ah, so it is placed in the rank of Jumu'ah in respect of overturning Zuhr as a precaution, unlike after its completion because it is not walking towards it. Translation: Then if it appears to him that he should attend Jumu'ah, so he heads towards it while the imam is in the Friday prayer, then according to Abu Hanifa, his Zuhr becomes invalid by the mere walking, and the two (Sahibayn) said it does not become invalid until he enters with the imam, because walking is inferior to Zuhr, so it does not break it after its completion. And Jumu'ah is superior to it, so it breaks it, and it becomes similar to when he goes after the imam has finished. And Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that walking to Jumu'ah is among the specific characteristics of Jumu'ah, so it is given the rank of Jumu'ah in the matter of invalidating Zuhr as a precaution, contrary to after its completion because it is not walking towards it.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding the effect of setting out for Jumu'ah after one has already prayed Zuhr. According to Abu Hanifa, as soon as the person starts walking towards the mosque while the imam is still engaged in the Friday prayer, his earlier Zuhr becomes invalid. The Sahibayn hold that the Zuhr remains valid until the person actually joins the congregation with the imam. The Sahibayn reason that walking (sa'y) is an act inferior to the completed Zuhr prayer, so it cannot nullify it; only the superior act of Jumu'ah itself can break it. Abu Hanifa, however, argues that walking to Jumu'ah is a specific characteristic of Jumu'ah itself, and thus, out of precaution, it is given the same legal effect as the prayer itself in terms of invalidating the Zuhr. This difference affects the obligation of the person: if he walks, according to Abu Hanifa he must pray Jumu'ah and his Zuhr is void; according to the Sahibayn, his Zuhr remains valid unless he actually joins.

Key Terms
سعی (sa'y): Walking or rushing towards the Jumu'ah prayer.
بطل (batala): To become invalid or void.
احتیاط (ihtiyat): Precaution; a principle to prefer the more cautious ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, at what point does a person's earlier Zuhr become invalidated if he decides to attend Jumu'ah?
A) When he makes the intention to attend.
B) When he starts walking towards the mosque.
C) When he enters the mosque.
D) When he joins the imam in prayer.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue hinges on whether walking to Jumu'ah carries the same legal effect as the prayer itself out of precaution, or whether only the actual joining of the congregation can overturn a completed Zuhr.

Friday Prayer vs Zuhr: Original Obligation and Ruling on Praying Zuhr Before Friday
Inter-madhhab dispute on the relationship between Zuhr and Friday prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that Zuhr is the original fard on Friday and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i/Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
Zuhr is the original fard on every day; Friday prayer is a substitute that cancels Zuhr, not replaces it.

The Friday prayer is a weekly communal obligation, but what is its relationship to the daily Zuhr prayer? The Hanafi school maintains a distinctive position: Zuhr remains the original fard, and Friday is a dispensation to lift it. This lesson examines the inter-madhhab dispute on whether one may pray Zuhr before the Friday prayer without an excuse.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi view: Zuhr is the original fard on Friday; Friday prayer is a substitute. Praying Zuhr before Friday without excuse is valid but makruh.
The key term is 'fard asli' (original obligation).
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Imam Zufar, Imam Malik, and Imam Shafi'i hold that Friday prayer is the original fard, and Zuhr is only a substitute. Their evidence: the command is for Friday, and Zuhr is forbidden until Friday is missed.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf in usul.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds with two proofs: (1) The hadith 'The first time of Zuhr is when the sun declines' is absolute, applying to all days including Friday. (2) Obligation is based on capability (Quran: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity'), and an individual cannot fulfill the conditions of Friday alone.
These proofs show that Zuhr is the original obligation.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi says Zuhr before Friday is valid but makruh; opponents say it is invalid and must be repeated as Zuhr later or as Friday if time remains.
This affects whether one needs to repeat the prayer.
5
Note the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position (valid but makruh) is the relied-upon view for fatwa, despite the intra-Hanafi dissent of Imam Zufar.
The majority of Hanafi scholars follow Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة الجمعة

فرض اصلی تو ظہر ہے۔ یہی ظاہر ہے مگر جمعہ ادا کر کے اس کو ساقط کر دینے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے اور ظہر کا اصل ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ ہر شخص ظہر ادا کرنے پر بذات خود قادر ہے نہ کہ ادائے جمعہ پر کیونکہ جمعہ ایسی شرائط پر موقوف ہے جو تنہا آدمی کے ساتھ پوری نہیں ہوتیں۔ حالانکہ قدرت ہی پر مکلف ہونے کا مدار ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے جمعہ کے دن امام کے نماز جمعہ پڑھانے سے پہلے اپنے گھر میں نماز ظہر پڑھی۔ حالانکہ اس کو کوئی عذر بھی نہیں ہے تو اس کی یہ نماز جائز تو ہوگئی لیکن مکروہ ہے۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ جائز نہیں ہوئی یہی امام مالک اور امام شافعی کا قول ہے۔ ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمعہ کے دن نماز جمعہ ہی اصلاً فرض ہے۔ اور ظہر اس کا بدل ہے کیونکہ نماز جمعہ کی طرف امر کیا گیا ہے اور جب تک جمعہ فوت نہ ہو جائے ظہر پڑھنے سے منع کیا گیا ہے پس نماز جمعہ کا مامور بہ ہونا اور ظہر کا ممنوع ہونا نماز جمعہ کے فرض اصلی ہونے کی دلیل ہے اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ جب تک اصل پر قدرت ہو تو بدل کی طرف رجوع نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ لہذا نماز جمعہ پر قادر ہونے کی صورت میں ظہر کا ادا کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔

ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمعہ کے دن اصلا تو ظہر فرض ہے جیسا کہ دوسرے ایام میں ظہر فرض ہے۔ دلیل حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا قول أول وقت الظهر حين تزول الشمس ہے۔ بایں طور کہ حدیث مطلق ہے کسی دن کی تخصیص نہیں ہے۔ لہذا از وال شمس کے بعد تمام ایام میں بلا استثنا، ظہر کا وقت ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تکلیف بحسب القدرت ہوتی ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ربانی ہے لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا اور اس وقت کے اندر نماز کا مکلف بذات خود ظہر ادا کرنے پر قادر ہے نہ کہ جمعہ ادا کرنے پر کیونکہ جمعہ ایسی شرائط پر موقوف ہے جو تنہا ایک آدمی کے ساتھ پوری نہیں ہوتیں، مثلاً امام کا ہونا جماعت کا ہونا وغیرہ پس جمعہ کا مکلف بنانا تکلیف مالا يطاق کے قبیل سے ہوگا۔ ہاں اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ جمعہ کے دن جمعہ ادا کر کے ظہر کی نماز ساقط کرنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے پس قدرت کے باوجود جمعہ سے اعراض کر کے ظہر ادا کرنا جائز مگر مکروہ ہوگا۔
Chapter of Friday Prayer. The original obligation is Zuhr. This is apparent, but it is commanded that by performing Friday prayer, Zuhr is cancelled. And Zuhr being the original is because every person is inherently capable of performing Zuhr by himself, not of performing Friday prayer, because Friday prayer depends on conditions that are not fulfilled by one person alone, whereas capability is the basis of being obligated. Explanation of the ruling: If someone on Friday, before the imam leads the Friday prayer, prayed Zuhr in his home while he had no excuse, then his prayer is valid but makruh (disliked). Imam Zufar said it is not valid, and this is the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i. Their proof: On Friday, Friday prayer is originally fard, and Zuhr is its substitute, because the command is for Friday prayer, and it is forbidden to pray Zuhr until Friday is missed. Thus Friday prayer being commanded and Zuhr being forbidden proves that Friday prayer is the original fard. And it is agreed that as long as one has ability to perform the original, one does not resort to the substitute. Therefore, when able to perform Friday, performing Zuhr would not be correct. Our proof: On Friday, originally Zuhr is fard, just as on other days. Proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The first time of Zuhr is when the sun declines.' The hadith is absolute, not specifying any day. Hence after the decline of the sun, on all days without exception, the time of Zuhr applies. Second proof: Obligation is according to ability, as Allah says: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' And within this time, the obligatee is able to perform Zuhr by himself, not Friday, because Friday depends on conditions such as the presence of an imam and congregation. So obligating Friday would be like an impossible obligation. However, it is essential that on Friday, the command is to cancel Zuhr by performing Friday. So avoiding Friday despite ability and performing Zuhr is valid but makruh.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage states a fundamental Hanafi principle regarding the Friday (Jumu'ah) prayer. The author begins by clarifying that the original fard (obligation) on Friday is the Zuhr prayer, just as on other days. The Friday prayer is a substitute that, when performed, cancels the obligation of Zuhr. The reasoning is that a Muslim is always capable of performing Zuhr individually, but Friday prayer requires conditions (imam, congregation) that one person alone cannot fulfill. The ruling is: if a person prays Zuhr at home before the Friday prayer without any excuse (such as being a traveler or sick), the prayer is valid (jā'iz) but makruh (disliked). The author then presents the opposing view of Imam Zufar, Imam Malik, and Imam Shafi'i: they hold that Friday prayer itself is the original fard, and Zuhr is only a substitute when Friday is missed. Their evidence is that the command is to perform Friday, and Zuhr is forbidden until Friday is missed, indicating the primacy of Friday. The Hanafi response provides two proofs: (1) The hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) fixing the time of Zuhr is general to all days, so Friday is included in that obligation. (2) The principle of taklīf (obligation) is based on capability (qudra); since Friday cannot be performed by an individual without conditions, obligating it as original would be imposing an undue burden (taklīf mā lā yuṭāq). Thus, Zuhr remains the original fard, and Friday is a means to lift its obligation. The passage ends by reiterating that performing Zuhr while capable of Friday is valid but makruh.

Key Terms
فرض اصلی (fard aṣlī): The original obligation (Zuhr) that is independently obligated based on capability.
مکروہ (makrūh): Disliked but valid; in this context, performing Zuhr before Friday without excuse is permissible but discouraged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person prays Zuhr at home on Friday before the Friday prayer without any excuse?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but makruh.
C) The prayer is valid and recommended.
D) The prayer is invalid unless he is a traveler.

Key Takeaway
Zuhr remains the original fard obligation on Friday; Friday prayer is a substitute that, when performed, lifts that obligation.

Dispute on Whether Sa'y to Jumu'ah Invalidates Zuhr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of sa'y on Zuhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding invalidation of Zuhr due to sa'y, identify the thamarah al-khilaf, and apply the rule to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Setting out for Friday prayer invalidates Zuhr for Abu Hanifa but not the Sahibayn—the dispute hinges on whether sa'y shares the rank of Friday.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on a subtle point: if a person prays Zuhr at home on Friday and then sets out for the Friday congregation while the imam is still praying, but arrives after the imam has finished, is his Zuhr invalidated? Imam Abu Hanifa says yes; his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn), say no. The disagreement arises from differing views on whether the act of proceeding to Friday (sa'y) has the same legal rank as Friday itself. Understanding this dispute helps sharpen your ability to trace a ruling back to its underlying principle (ta'lil) and to appreciate how a difference in conceptual framing leads to different practical outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two possibilities
Read the description: a person prays Zuhr at home on Friday before the Friday prayer, then decides to attend Friday. Two outcomes: either he catches the prayer (Zuhr invalidated by consensus) or he does not (the point of dispute). Focus on the second case.
2
State the position of Imam Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa holds that the moment one sets out (sa'y) towards the mosque while the imam is still engaged in Friday prayer, the Zuhr becomes invalid, even if one misses the prayer. Thus, one must repeat Zuhr.
His key concept: sa'y is a khassa (distinctive feature) of Friday, so it shares Friday's rank and can invalidate the lower (Zuhr).
3
State the position of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn hold that only actual participation in Friday prayer invalidates Zuhr. Merely setting out does not, because sa'y is a means, not an end. Therefore, if one arrives after the imam finishes, the Zuhr remains valid and no repetition is needed.
Their principle: the higher (Friday) invalidates the lower (Zuhr) only when actually performed, not by mere intention.
4
Analyze the proofs (istidlal) of each side
Abu Hanifa argues that sa'y is among the special characteristics of Friday (khasa'is) because Friday requires a specific location, making sa'y integral. The Sahibayn argue that sa'y is merely a cause (sabab) to reach Friday, and a cause does not carry the ruling of the effect. Identify the underlying usul principle: for Abu Hanifa, what is necessary for an act (sa'y) can share its legal status; for Sahibayn, ends and means are distinct.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Apply the two rulings to the scenario: a person sets out while imam is praying but arrives after imam finishes. Under Abu Hanifa: Zuhr is invalid → must repeat Zuhr. Under Sahibayn: Zuhr is valid → no need to repeat. This is the concrete difference.

Source Text

سے فارغ ہو گیا ہے اس لئے کہ یہ جمعہ کی طرف بھی کرنا نہیں ہے۔
باب صلوة الجمعة
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص جس نے جمعہ کے دن اپنے گھر میں ظہر پڑھی درانحالیکہ ابھی تک نماز جمعہ ادا نہیں کی گئی ہے پھر اس کو خیال آیا کہ نماز جمعہ میں شرکت کرنی چاہئے۔ اس ارادہ کے ساتھ یہ شخص جامع مسجد کی طرف چلدیا تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ یا تو یہ امام کی ساتھ نماز جمعہ میں شریک ہو جائے گا یا شریک نہ ہو سکے گا۔ اگر اس نے امام کے ساتھ نماز جمعہ کو پالیا تو اس کی نماز ظہر باطل ہو جائے گی اور نفل میں تبدیل ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اگر یہ شخص جمعہ کے لئے روانہ تو اس وقت ہوا تھا جبکہ امام نماز جمعہ میں تھا لیکن اس کے پہنچتے پہنچتے امام نماز جمعہ سے فارغ ہو گیا اور یہ شخص نماز جمعہ کو امام کے ساتھ نہیں پاس کا تو اس بارے میں امام الہمام قدوۃ الا نام امام اعظم کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ گھر سے چلنے کے ساتھ ہی اس کی نماز ظہر باطل ہو گئی اب چونکہ اس کو نماز جمعہ تو مل نہیں سکی اور ادا کی ہوئی ظہر باطل ہو گئی اس لئے نماز ظہر اعادہ کرے۔ اور صاحبین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ محض چلنے سے ظہر باطل نہ ہوگی بلکہ نماز جمعہ میں شرکت کرنے سے باطل ہو گی ۔ یعنی اس شخص کے پہنچنے سے پہلے ہی اگر امام نماز جمعہ سے فارغ ہو گیا تو اس کی ظہر باطل نہ ہوگی۔ ہاں اگر امام کے ساتھ نماز جمعہ کے کسی حصہ میں شریک ہو گیا تو اس کی ظہر باطل ہو جائے گی۔
صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سعی الی الجمعہ چونکہ بذاتہ مقصود نہیں ہے بلکہ ادا جمعہ کا وسیلہ ہے اور ظہر فرض مقصود ہے۔ اس لئے سعی الی الجمعه به نسبت ظہر کے ادنی اور کمتر ہے۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ اعلی ادنی کی وجہت باطل نہیں ہوتا اسلئے محض سعی الی الجمعہ سے ظہر باطل نہیں ہوگی اور جمعہ چونکہ ظہر سے اعلی اور برتر ہے اس لئے جمعہ کی نماز ظہر کو باطل کر دے گی۔ رہا یہ کہ جمعہ اعلیٰ کیوں ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہم کو شریعت اسلام نے یہ حکم دیا ہے کہ جمعہ کے دن ظہر کو ساقط کر کے جمعہ ادا کیا جائے، پس جمعہ کی وجہ سے ظہر کا ساقط ہونا جمعہ کے اعلیٰ اور برتر ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے امام کے نماز جمعہ سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد جمعہ کی طرف متوجہ ہوا کہ اس صورت میں بالاتفاق سعی ظہر کو باطل نہیں کرتی۔ کیونکہ یہ بیکار سعی ہے اسی طرح سعی الی الجمعہ ظہر کو اس صورت میں باطل نہیں کرے گی جبکہ سعی الی الجمعہ کرتے وقت امام نماز جمعہ میں تھا لیکن اس کے پہنچنے تک امام نماز جمعہ سے فارغ ہو گیا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سعی یعنی جمعہ کے لئے چلنا جمعہ کے خصائص میں سے ہے۔ کیونکہ جمعہ ایسی نماز ہے جس کو ہر جگہ ادا نہیں کیا جا سکتا بلکہ اس کے واسطے مخصوص مکان کا ہونا ضروری ہے لہذا بغیر سعی الی الجمعہ کے جمعہ کا ادا کرنا ممکن نہیں ہوگا۔ پس ثابت . ہو گیا کہ سعی الی الجمعہ، جمعہ کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ اور جب سعی جمعہ کے خصائص میں سے ہے تو سعی الی الجمعہ، جمعہ کے مرتبہ میں ہو گی ۔ پس جس طرح ظہر ادا کرنے کے بعد نماز جمعہ میں شریک ہونا ظہر کو باطل کر دیتا ہے۔ اسی طرح نماز جمعہ کی طرف سعی کرنا بھی ظہر کو باطل کر دے گا۔ بشرطیکہ جس وقت سعی کی ہے اس وقت امام نماز جمعہ میں ہو ۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر امام کے نماز جمعہ سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد سعی کی تو یہ بھی ظہر کو باطل نہیں کرے گی ۔ کیونکہ یہ کی جمعہ کے مرتبہ میں نہیں ہے اور جمعہ کے مرتبہ میں اس لئے نہیں کہ یہ جمعہ کی طرف سعی نہیں ہے۔ امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے درمیان ثمرہ اختلاف اس مثال میں ظاہر ہو گا کہ ایک شخص اپنے گھر میں ظہر ادا کرنے کے بعد جمعہ کے لئے اس وقت چلا جبکہ امام نماز جمعہ میں مشغول ہے لیکن اس کے پہونچنے تک امام نماز جمعہ سے فارغ ہو گیا۔ تو امام صاحب کے نزد یک چونکہ سعی الی الجمعہ سے ظہر باطل ہو گئی ہے اس لئے ظہر کا اعادہ کرے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ ظہر باطل نہیں ہوئی اس لئے 
ظہر کا اعادہ نہ کرے۔
He has become free from it because he is not going towards Friday. Chapter of Friday Prayer. Explanation: The scenario is that a person prayed Zuhr in his house on Friday while the Friday prayer had not yet been performed. Then he thought he should attend Friday prayer. With this intention he set out towards the Friday mosque. There are two possibilities: either he will join the imam in Friday prayer or he will not join. If he catches the Friday prayer with the imam, his Zuhr prayer becomes invalid and changes into a supererogatory prayer. And if he set out for Friday when the imam was in the Friday prayer but by the time he arrived the imam had finished the Friday prayer and he did not catch the Friday prayer with the imam, then regarding this, the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa is that from the moment he left his house his Zuhr prayer became invalid. Now since he did not get the Friday prayer and his performed Zuhr became invalid, he must repeat Zuhr. The opinion of the Sahibayn is that merely walking does not invalidate Zuhr; rather, it is invalidated by participating in Friday prayer. That is, if before his arrival the imam had finished Friday prayer, his Zuhr is not invalidated. Yes, if he joins the imam in any part of Friday prayer, his Zuhr becomes invalid. The proof of the Sahibayn is that walking towards Friday (sa'y ila al-jumu'ah) is not an end in itself but a means to perform Friday, while Zuhr is an obligatory end. Therefore, sa'y is lower and lesser in status compared to Zuhr. The principle is that the higher is not invalidated by the lower, so mere sa'y does not invalidate Zuhr. And because Friday is higher and superior to Zuhr, Friday prayer will invalidate Zuhr. As for why Friday is superior, the answer is that Islamic law commands us to drop Zuhr on Friday and perform Friday instead; thus the dropping of Zuhr due to Friday proves Friday's superiority. The author of Hidayah said: This is like a person who turns towards Friday after the imam has finished Friday prayer; in that case by consensus sa'y does not invalidate Zuhr because it is futile. Similarly, sa'y towards Friday will not invalidate Zuhr when at the time of sa'y the imam was in Friday prayer but by the time he arrives the imam has finished. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that walking for Friday is among the special characteristics (khasa'is) of Friday. Because Friday is a prayer that cannot be performed everywhere; rather, it requires a specific place. Therefore, without sa'y, performing Friday is impossible. So it is established that sa'y is specific to Friday. And when sa'y is among the characteristics of Friday, it will be in the rank of Friday. Just as participating in Friday prayer after performing Zuhr invalidates Zuhr, similarly walking towards Friday will invalidate Zuhr, provided that at the time of walking the imam is in Friday prayer. Contrary to this, if one walks after the imam has finished Friday prayer, that does not invalidate Zuhr because it is not in the rank of Friday; it is not considered sa'y towards Friday. The practical difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn appears in this example: a person, after praying Zuhr at home, walks for Friday while the imam is engaged in Friday prayer, but by the time he arrives the imam has finished. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, since sa'y invalidated his Zuhr, he must repeat Zuhr. According to the Sahibayn, since Zuhr was not invalidated, he does not repeat Zuhr.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of proceeding to the Friday congregational prayer (sa'y ila al-jumu'ah) on a previously performed Zuhr prayer. The scenario: a person prays Zuhr at home on Friday before the Friday prayer has begun, then decides to attend Friday prayer. If he catches the Friday prayer with the imam, his Zuhr is invalidated and becomes nafl. The dispute arises when he sets out while the imam is still in the prayer but arrives after the imam has finished. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that merely setting out with the intention of joining Friday (sa'y) invalidates the Zuhr, so he must repeat Zuhr. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that only actual participation in Friday invalidates Zuhr; if he misses the prayer, his Zuhr remains valid. The Sahibayn argue that sa'y is a means, not an end, and the principle is that a higher act (Friday) can invalidate a lower one (Zuhr) only when actually performed, not by mere intention or movement. Abu Hanifa argues that sa'y is a distinctive feature of Friday (khasa'is), because Friday requires travel to a specific location; therefore sa'y shares the rank of Friday and thus can invalidate Zuhr, provided it occurs while the imam is still engaged in prayer. The practical difference (thamarah al-ikhtilaf) is that in the described scenario, Abu Hanifa requires repetition of Zuhr, while the Sahibayn do not. The commentator (Ashraf al-Hadaya) presents both arguments and then cites the author of Hidayah's clarification using the analogy of setting out after the imam has finished, which is futile by consensus.

Key Terms
سعی الی الجمعہ (sa'y ilā al-jumu‘ah): The act of walking or proceeding to attend the Friday congregational prayer, considered a necessary means to perform Friday prayer.
ثمرہ اختلاف (thamarah al-ikhtilāf): The practical consequence or outcome of a legal disagreement between scholars.
صاحبین (al-Ṣāḥibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, whose views often differ from his.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what invalidates a Zuhr prayer performed at home on Friday?
A) Setting out (sa'y) towards the Friday mosque while the imam is praying.
B) Actual participation in any part of the Friday prayer.
C) The intention to attend Friday prayer.
D) Arriving at the mosque before the imam finishes.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether sa'y alone invalidates Zuhr, with the later mufta bihi position following the Sahibayn that only actual participation in Friday invalidates the earlier Zuhr.

Ruling on Congregational Zuhr for Excused Persons on Friday
First ruling on karahah of Zuhr in congregation for excused persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that it is makruh tanzihi for excused persons (ma'dhur) to pray Zuhr in congregation on Friday in the city, and explain the two different rationales (deficiency vs. apparent opposition) given in the text.

Core Idea
Excused persons may not break the Friday congregation; their Zuhr in congregation is disliked.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from al-Hidayah: excused persons (e.g., sick, travelers, slaves) are discouraged from performing Zuhr in congregation on Friday in the city. The original rationale of causing deficiency is critiqued by the commentator, who offers a refined reason. Understanding this refinement helps you grasp the legal reasoning process within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday in the city by those who are excused from Friday prayer (ma'dhur). The ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not haram).
The prayer itself is valid if performed, but the manner is discouraged.
2
Define the person (ma'dhur) and context
Ma'dhur includes slaves, travelers, and the sick. The context is a city (misr) where Friday is established. Different from villages where Friday is not obligatory.
The ruling applies only in the city, not in rural areas.
3
Examine the original proof (dalil)
The original proof cited in al-Hidayah is that congregational Zuhr causes deficiency (ikhlal) in Friday by dividing the congregation, since Friday gathers all congregations.
This rationale implies that multiple Friday prayers are not allowed.
4
Analyze the commentator's critique
The commentator (Ashraf al-Hadayah) argues that this proof is weak because multiple Friday prayers are permitted in a city according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. He suggests a better reason: apparent opposition (mu'aradah) to Friday.
The ruling remains the same, but the reasoning is refined.
5
Conclude and apply
The dislike stands, but it is due to the appearance of competing with Friday, not actual deficiency. Al-Quduri confirms that if done, the prayer is valid.
This shows how Hanafi jurists refine proofs without changing the established ruling.

Source Text

ویکره ان يصلى المعذورون الظهر بجماعة يوم الجمعة في المصر وكذا اهل السجن لما فيه من الاخلال بالجمعة اذهى جامعة للجماعات والمعذور قد يقتدى به غیره بخلاف اهل السواد لانه لا جمعة عليهم ولو صلى قوم اجزأهم لاستجماع شرائطه
ترجمہ اور معذور لوگوں کا جمعہ کے دن شہر کے اندر جماعت کے ساتھ ظہر ادا کرنا مکروہ ہے اسی طرح قیدیوں کا ۔ کیونکہ اس عمل میں جمعہ کے اندر خلل پیدا کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ جمعہ تو تمام جماعتوں کو جمع کرنے والا ہے ۔ اور معذور کے ساتھ کبھی غیر معذور بھی اقتدا کر لیتا ہے۔ برخلاف گاؤں والوں کے کہ ان پر جمعہ نہیں ہے اور اگر کسی قوم نے اس دن ظہر جماعت سے پڑھ لی تو ان کو کافی ہوگئی۔ کیونکہ اس کی تمام شرطیں جمع ہو گئیں۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ معذور لوگ مثلاً غلام ، مسافر، بیمار جمعہ کے دن شہر کے اندر جمعہ کی نماز سے پہلے یا بعد میں اگر باجماعت ظہر ادا کر لیں تو یہ عمل مکروہ ہے۔ یوں ہی قیدیوں کا جمعہ کے دن باجماعت ظہر ادا کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس عمل میں جمعہ کے اندر خلل واقع ہوگا۔ خلل یہ ہے کہ جمعہ تمام جماعتوں کا جامع ہے پس جب کچھ لوگوں نے ظہر کو جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کیا تو جمعہ جامعۃ الجماعات نہ رہا۔ اس دلیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک شہر میں متعدد جمعے جائز نہیں ہیں۔ حالانکہ ایک شہر میں کئی جگہ جمعہ ادا کرنا امام صاحب اور امام محمد کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ پس صاحب ہدایہ کا کراہت جماعت کی دلیل میں اخلال بالجمعہ بیان کرنا غیر معقول ہے۔ مناسب یہ ہے کہ کراہت کی دلیل یہ بیان کی جائے کہ جمعہ کے دن ظہر کو باجماعت ادا کرنے میں ظاہری صورت میں جمعہ کا معارضہ اور مقابلہ معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ والمعذور الخ سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال: یہ ہے کہ جب معذورین پر جمعہ فرض نہیں ہے تو ان کے ظہر کو با جماعت ادا کرنے میں جمعہ کے اندر خلل کا کیا سوال ہے۔ جواب: معذور کے ساتھ بھی غیر معذور بھی اقتدا کر لیتا ہے لہذا غیر معذور کے اقتدا کرنے سے جمعہ میں خلل ہوگا۔ اس کے برخلاف گاؤں کے لوگ اگر باجماعت ظہر ادا کریں تو اس میں کوئی کراہت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ گاؤں والوں پر سرے سے جمعہ فرض نہیں ہوا ہے اور معذور پر جمعہ فرض تھا مگر عذر کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو گیا۔ صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ جمعہ کے دن ظہر کی جماعت مکروہ ہونے کے باوجود اگر کچھ لوگوں نے ظہر کو جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کر لیا تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ نماز اپنی شرطوں کے ساتھ پائی گئی۔ رہی کراہت تو وہ اس کی ذات سے خارج حق جمعہ کی وجہ سے تھی سو وہ اب بھی ہے۔
جس نے امام کو جمعہ کی نماز میں پالیا نماز پڑھے اور جمعہ کی بنا کرے
و من ادرك الامام يوم الجمعة صلى معه ما ادركه وبنى عليها الجمعة لقوله عليه السلام ما ادركتم فصلو او ما فاتكم فاقضوا
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے امام کو جمعہ کے دن پایا تو اس کے ساتھ اس کو پڑھے جس کو اس نے پایا ہے اور اسی پر جمعہ کی بناء کرے۔ کیونکہ
Ruling for excused persons to pray Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday. It is disliked (makruh) for excused persons to pray Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday, and also for prisoners, because it causes deficiency in the Friday prayer, since Friday gathers all congregations. And the excused person may be followed by others (in prayer). Unlike the villagers, because Friday is not obligatory upon them. And if a group prays (Zuhr in congregation), it suffices them because all its conditions are fulfilled. Explanation: Excused persons such as slaves, travelers, and sick people, if they pray Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday before or after the Friday prayer, this act is disliked. Similarly, prisoners praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday is disliked. The proof is that this act causes deficiency in Friday prayer. The deficiency is that Friday is a gathering of all congregations; when some people pray Zuhr in congregation, Friday ceases to be a comprehensive gathering. From this proof it is understood that multiple Friday prayers in one city are not permissible—although according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, multiple Friday prayers in one city are permissible. Therefore the author of Hidayah's mention of deficiency as a proof for dislike is unreasonable. It is more appropriate to give the proof that praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday outwardly appears as opposition and rivalry to Friday. From 'and the excused person...' is an answer to a question. The question is: Since Friday is not obligatory upon the excused, what does deficiency have to do with it? The answer: Non-excused persons might follow the excused, so through their following, deficiency occurs in Friday. Contrary to villagers: if they pray Zuhr in congregation, there is no dislike because Friday is not at all obligatory upon them; whereas Friday was obligatory upon the excused but dropped due to the excuse. Al-Quduri says: Even though congregational Zuhr on Friday is disliked, if some people perform it in congregation, it is permissible because the prayer is found with all its conditions. As for the dislike, it was due to compromise of the right of Friday, and that still remains. Whoever catches the imam on Friday, he prays with him what he caught and builds upon it the Friday prayer, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'What you have caught, pray it, and what you have missed, complete it.'
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage presents two related rulings within the chapter of Friday prayer. First, the ruling on excused persons (ma'dhur: slaves, travelers, sick) performing Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday. According to the matn of al-Hidayah, it is makruh for them because it creates a deficiency in the Friday prayer—Friday is meant to gather all congregations, and if some pray in separate congregations, that unity is undermined. The commentator, Ashraf al-Hadaya, criticizes this reasoning: if multiple Friday prayers are allowed in a city (as per Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad), then this deficiency argument is illogical. He suggests a better reason: that praying Zuhr in congregation outwardly appears as competing with or opposing the Friday prayer. The text then addresses an objection: since excused persons are not required to pray Friday, why would their congregational Zuhr cause deficiency? The answer is that non-excused persons might follow the excused imam, thus diverting attendance from Friday. Villagers, on whom Friday is not obligatory at all, may pray Zuhr in congregation without dislike. Al-Quduri clarifies that if such a congregational Zuhr is performed, it is valid (jaez) but remains makruh due to disrespecting Friday's right. The second ruling: whoever catches the imam in the Friday prayer (even a single rakah) prays what he caught with the imam and then completes the remainder as Friday, based on the hadith 'Whatever you have caught, pray, and whatever you have missed, complete.' This is a general principle applicable to all prayers, specifically applied here to Friday.

Key Terms
معذور (ma‘dhūr): A person with a valid excuse (sickness, travel, slavery) that exempts them from the obligation of Friday prayer.
کراہت (karāhah): Dislike; an act that is discouraged but not forbidden. Here, it is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful).
اخلال بالجمعہ (ikhlāl bi al-jumu‘ah): Causing deficiency or harm to the Friday prayer by undermining its congregational nature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Quduri as cited in the text, if a group of excused persons prays Zuhr in congregation on Friday in the city, what is the ruling?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is permissible but still disliked (makruh).
C) It is commendable because they are following the sunnah.
D) It becomes nafl instead of fard.

Key Takeaway
The ruling that it is makruh for excused persons to pray Zuhr in congregation on Friday is established, but the original proof (deficiency) is flawed; the correct rationale is apparent opposition to Friday.

Catching Part of the Friday Prayer
Second ruling on catching part of Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a latecomer who catches the imam in any part of the Friday prayer (at least one rak'ah) prays what he caught and then completes the remainder as Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
Catch one rak'ah of Jumu'ah with the imam and you have caught the entire Friday prayer.

This lesson covers a practical scenario: a person arrives late for Friday prayer and finds the imam already in salah. The hadith provides a general principle that whatever you catch with the imam, you pray, and whatever you miss, you complete. Applied to Jumu'ah, it means that if you catch at least one rak'ah, you pray the remaining as part of Jumu'ah. If you catch less than a rak'ah, you treat it as Zuhr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person arrives late for Jumu'ah and finds the imam already in prayer. He joins immediately.
This is a common occurrence in congregational prayers.
2
State the ruling from the text
Whoever catches the imam on Friday prays with him what he caught and then builds upon it the Friday prayer.
The phrase 'builds upon it' (bana 'alayha) means he continues the same prayer as Jumu'ah.
3
Cite the proof (hadith)
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'What you have caught, pray it, and what you have missed, complete it.' This is a general rule for all prayers, applied here to Friday.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Clarify the condition of 'catching'
'Catching' (idrak) means performing at least one complete rak'ah with the imam. If one catches less than a rak'ah (e.g., after ruku'), then he does not count that rak'ah and prays four rak'ahs of Zuhr instead.
This is the standard Hanafi position.
5
Explain the completion
After the imam says salam, the latecomer stands and completes the remaining rak'ahs (one if he caught one rak'ah, two if he caught no rak'ah? Actually if he caught one, he completes two total, so he prays one more. If he caught two, he already completed Friday). The intention remains for Jumu'ah.
The prayer is valid as Jumu'ah only if he caught at least one rak'ah with the imam.

Source Text

معذورین کے لئے جمعہ کے دن شہر میں ظہر کی نماز جماعت سے پڑھنے کا حکم
ویکره ان يصلى المعذورون الظهر بجماعة يوم الجمعة في المصر وكذا اهل السجن لما فيه من الاخلال بالجمعة اذهى جامعة للجماعات والمعذور قد يقتدى به غیره بخلاف اهل السواد لانه لا جمعة عليهم ولو صلى قوم اجزأهم لاستجماع شرائطه
ترجمہ اور معذور لوگوں کا جمعہ کے دن شہر کے اندر جماعت کے ساتھ ظہر ادا کرنا مکروہ ہے اسی طرح قیدیوں کا ۔ کیونکہ اس عمل میں جمعہ کے اندر خلل پیدا کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ جمعہ تو تمام جماعتوں کو جمع کرنے والا ہے ۔ اور معذور کے ساتھ کبھی غیر معذور بھی اقتدا کر لیتا ہے۔ برخلاف گاؤں والوں کے کہ ان پر جمعہ نہیں ہے اور اگر کسی قوم نے اس دن ظہر جماعت سے پڑھ لی تو ان کو کافی ہوگئی۔ کیونکہ اس کی تمام شرطیں جمع ہو گئیں۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ معذور لوگ مثلاً غلام ، مسافر، بیمار جمعہ کے دن شہر کے اندر جمعہ کی نماز سے پہلے یا بعد میں اگر باجماعت ظہر ادا کر لیں تو یہ عمل مکروہ ہے۔ یوں ہی قیدیوں کا جمعہ کے دن باجماعت ظہر ادا کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس عمل میں جمعہ کے اندر خلل واقع ہوگا۔ خلل یہ ہے کہ جمعہ تمام جماعتوں کا جامع ہے پس جب کچھ لوگوں نے ظہر کو جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کیا تو جمعہ جامعۃ الجماعات نہ رہا۔ اس دلیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک شہر میں متعدد جمعے جائز نہیں ہیں۔ حالانکہ ایک شہر میں کئی جگہ جمعہ ادا کرنا امام صاحب اور امام محمد کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ پس صاحب ہدایہ کا کراہت جماعت کی دلیل میں اخلال بالجمعہ بیان کرنا غیر معقول ہے۔ مناسب یہ ہے کہ کراہت کی دلیل یہ بیان کی جائے کہ جمعہ کے دن ظہر کو باجماعت ادا کرنے میں ظاہری صورت میں جمعہ کا معارضہ اور مقابلہ معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ والمعذور الخ سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال: یہ ہے کہ جب معذورین پر جمعہ فرض نہیں ہے تو ان کے ظہر کو با جماعت ادا کرنے میں جمعہ کے اندر خلل کا کیا سوال ہے۔ جواب: معذور کے ساتھ بھی غیر معذور بھی اقتدا کر لیتا ہے لہذا غیر معذور کے اقتدا کرنے سے جمعہ میں خلل ہوگا۔ اس کے برخلاف گاؤں کے لوگ اگر باجماعت ظہر ادا کریں تو اس میں کوئی کراہت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ گاؤں والوں پر سرے سے جمعہ فرض نہیں ہوا ہے اور معذور پر جمعہ فرض تھا مگر عذر کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو گیا۔ صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ جمعہ کے دن ظہر کی جماعت مکروہ ہونے کے باوجود اگر کچھ لوگوں نے ظہر کو جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کر لیا تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ نماز اپنی شرطوں کے ساتھ پائی گئی۔ رہی کراہت تو وہ اس کی ذات سے خارج حق جمعہ کی وجہ سے تھی سو وہ اب بھی ہے۔
جس نے امام کو جمعہ کی نماز میں پالیا نماز پڑھے اور جمعہ کی بنا کرے
و من ادرك الامام يوم الجمعة صلى معه ما ادركه وبنى عليها الجمعة لقوله عليه السلام ما ادركتم فصلو او ما فاتكم فاقضوا
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے امام کو جمعہ کے دن پایا تو اس کے ساتھ اس کو پڑھے جس کو اس نے پایا ہے اور اسی پر جمعہ کی بناء کرے۔ کیونکہ
Ruling for excused persons to pray Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday. It is disliked (makruh) for excused persons to pray Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday, and also for prisoners, because it causes deficiency in the Friday prayer, since Friday gathers all congregations. And the excused person may be followed by others (in prayer). Unlike the villagers, because Friday is not obligatory upon them. And if a group prays (Zuhr in congregation), it suffices them because all its conditions are fulfilled. Explanation: Excused persons such as slaves, travelers, and sick people, if they pray Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday before or after the Friday prayer, this act is disliked. Similarly, prisoners praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday is disliked. The proof is that this act causes deficiency in Friday prayer. The deficiency is that Friday is a gathering of all congregations; when some people pray Zuhr in congregation, Friday ceases to be a comprehensive gathering. From this proof it is understood that multiple Friday prayers in one city are not permissible—although according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, multiple Friday prayers in one city are permissible. Therefore the author of Hidayah's mention of deficiency as a proof for dislike is unreasonable. It is more appropriate to give the proof that praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday outwardly appears as opposition and rivalry to Friday. From 'and the excused person...' is an answer to a question. The question is: Since Friday is not obligatory upon the excused, what does deficiency have to do with it? The answer: Non-excused persons might follow the excused, so through their following, deficiency occurs in Friday. Contrary to villagers: if they pray Zuhr in congregation, there is no dislike because Friday is not at all obligatory upon them; whereas Friday was obligatory upon the excused but dropped due to the excuse. Al-Quduri says: Even though congregational Zuhr on Friday is disliked, if some people perform it in congregation, it is permissible because the prayer is found with all its conditions. As for the dislike, it was due to compromise of the right of Friday, and that still remains. Whoever catches the imam on Friday, he prays with him what he caught and builds upon it the Friday prayer, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'What you have caught, pray it, and what you have missed, complete it.'
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage presents two related rulings within the chapter of Friday prayer. First, the ruling on excused persons (ma'dhur: slaves, travelers, sick) performing Zuhr in congregation in the city on Friday. According to the matn of al-Hidayah, it is makruh for them because it creates a deficiency in the Friday prayer—Friday is meant to gather all congregations, and if some pray in separate congregations, that unity is undermined. The commentator, Ashraf al-Hadaya, criticizes this reasoning: if multiple Friday prayers are allowed in a city (as per Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad), then this deficiency argument is illogical. He suggests a better reason: that praying Zuhr in congregation outwardly appears as competing with or opposing the Friday prayer. The text then addresses an objection: since excused persons are not required to pray Friday, why would their congregational Zuhr cause deficiency? The answer is that non-excused persons might follow the excused imam, thus diverting attendance from Friday. Villagers, on whom Friday is not obligatory at all, may pray Zuhr in congregation without dislike. Al-Quduri clarifies that if such a congregational Zuhr is performed, it is valid (jaez) but remains makruh due to disrespecting Friday's right. The second ruling: whoever catches the imam in the Friday prayer (even a single rakah) prays what he caught with the imam and then completes the remainder as Friday, based on the hadith 'Whatever you have caught, pray, and whatever you have missed, complete.' This is a general principle applicable to all prayers, specifically applied here to Friday.

Key Terms
ادراک (idrāk): The act of catching a rak'ah with the imam, which requires performing at least one full rak'ah including qiyam, ruku', and sujud.
بناء (binā'): Building upon; continuing the prayer after the imam's salam by completing the missed rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person joins the Jumu'ah prayer during the tashahhud of the second rak'ah. What should he do?
A) He prays two rak'ahs with the imam and completes no more.
B) He prays the tashahhud with the imam and then stands to complete one rak'ah.
C) He has missed both rak'ahs, so he must pray four rak'ahs of Zuhr.
D) He leaves the prayer and repeats it.

Key Takeaway
Catching at least one rak'ah of Jumu'ah with the imam makes your entire prayer valid as Jumu'ah; otherwise, you pray Zuhr.

Ruling on Excused Persons Praying Zuhr in Congregation on Friday
Ruling and reasoning for ma'dhur's Zuhr congregation on Friday

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a ma'dhur praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday in a city and explain the Hanafi reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
For excused persons, praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday is valid but disliked because it undermines Jumu'ah's unifying purpose.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from al-Hidayah regarding Friday prayer. While Jumu'ah is a wajib congregation, some individuals are excused. What happens when they gather for Zuhr instead? The passage provides a nuanced answer: it is valid but disliked. Understanding the reasoning helps us appreciate the legal weight of communal worship and the importance of not disrupting the prescribed Friday congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Who is the subject? What is the hukm (legal classification)?
The act is praying Zuhr in congregation; the subject is the ma'dhur (excused persons) and likewise prisoners; the ruling is makruh (disliked) but valid.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
What reasoning does the author provide for this ruling? What type of proof is it?
The proof is istihsan: 'لما فيه من الاخلال بالجمعة اذهى جامعة للجماعات' (because it disrupts Friday prayer, which unites the congregations).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does this reasoning specifically support the ruling? What is the logical link?
The unifying aspect of Jumu'ah is compromised if a separate congregation for Zuhr is held simultaneously. Additionally, the ma'dhur might be followed by others who are not excused, causing neglect of Jumu'ah.
4
Identify exceptions and boundaries
Are there cases where this ruling does not apply? What distinguishes them?
The exception is 'اهل السواد' (people of the countryside/villages) because Jumu'ah is not obligatory on them. Also, if the ma'dhur prays individually or outside the city, no karahah.
5
Confirm validity despite karahah
Why is the prayer still valid? What does this tell us about the nature of karahah in this context?
The text says 'ولو صلى قوم اجزأهم لاستجماع شرائطه' (and if a group prayed, it suffices them due to fulfillment of its conditions). The karahah is not due to a deficiency in the prayer itself but due to an external factor (disruption of Jumu'ah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره ان يصلى المعذورون الظهر بجماعة يوم الجمعة في المصر وكذا اهل السجن لما فيه من الاخلال بالجمعة اذهى جامعة للجماعات والمعذور قد يقتدى به غیره بخلاف اهل السواد لانه لا جمعة عليهم ولو صلى قوم اجزأهم لاستجماع شرائطه
And it is disliked that those excused pray Zuhr in congregation on Friday in the city, and likewise the prisoners, because of the disruption it causes to the Friday prayer, for it gathers the congregations. And the excused person may be followed by others. Unlike the people of the countryside, for Friday prayer is not obligatory upon them. And if a group prayed, it suffices them due to the fulfillment of its conditions.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on excused persons (e.g., slaves, travelers, sick) praying Zuhr in congregation on Friday within a city (misr). The ruling is makruh (disliked). The reason given is that it undermines the purpose of Jumu'ah, which is to unite the community in one congregation. Additionally, an excused person might be followed by someone who is not excused, thus causing neglect of Jumu'ah. Villagers (ahl al-sawad) are exempt because Jumu'ah is not obligatory on them. If the excused do perform Zuhr in congregation, their prayer is valid because all conditions of Zuhr are met; the karahah is due to external factors. The text also implies that multiple Jumu'ah in one city would be problematic, but the commentator notes that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad permit multiple Jumu'ahs, so the better explanation for karahah is that it appears to compete with Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
معذور (ma'dhur): A person excused from Jumu'ah due to a legitimate reason such as illness, travel, or being a slave.
مصر (misr): A large city or town where Jumu'ah is validly held.
اهل السواد (ahl al-sawad): People of the countryside or rural areas where Jumu'ah is not held.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it disliked for an excused person to pray Zuhr in congregation on Friday in the city?
A) Because Zuhr prayer is not valid on Friday.
B) Because it disrupts the unity of Jumu'ah and may lead non-excused persons to follow them.
C) Because the excused person must pray Jumu'ah instead.
D) Because it is only allowed in the countryside.

Key Takeaway
Excused persons should avoid congregating for Zuhr on Friday in a city to preserve the unity of Jumu'ah, though their prayer is valid if performed.

Latecomer Catching Imam in Tashahhud or Sajda Sahw in Jumu'ah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on building Jumu'ah when catching only tashahhud or sajda sahw.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ikhtilaf between the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad regarding a latecomer who catches Jumu'ah only in tashahhud or sajda sahw, and state the mufta bihi position with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
A latecomer catching tashahhud is mudrik—builds on Jumu'ah and prays two rak'ahs (two shaykhs); Imam Muhammad splits based on catching most of second rak'ah.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: when a latecomer joins Jumu'ah and finds the imam only in the final tashahhud or in the prostration of forgetfulness, does he complete Jumu'ah as two rak'ahs or revert to Zuhr? The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) maintain he is mudrik and builds on Jumu'ah, while Imam Muhammad introduces a distinction based on how much of the second rak'ah he caught. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your grasp of the concept of 'mudrik' and the rules of building (bina') in congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the exact scenario: a latecomer joins Jumu'ah and finds the imam in tashahhud or sajda sahw. The question is whether he builds on Jumu'ah or on Zuhr.
2
Identify the two positions
State the ruling of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) and the ruling of Imam Muhammad. Note the condition Imam Muhammad attaches.
3
Analyze the proofs
For each position, extract the dalil (proof) from the text. The two shaykhs argue he is mudrik and Jumu'ah is two rak'ahs. Imam Muhammad argues missed congregation condition, so it is Jumu'ah in one aspect and Zuhr in another.
4
Identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the two shaykhs: pray 2 rak'ahs. Under Imam Muhammad: pray 4 rak'ahs with a sitting after two and recitation in the last two.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is the position of the two shaykhs. Note the tarjih authority (al-Hidayah) and why Imam Muhammad's view is not adopted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان ادركه فى التشهد او فى سجود السهو بني عليها الجمعة عندهما وقال محمد ان ادرک معه اکثر الركعة الثانية بنى عليها الجمعة وان ادرك اقلها بنى عليها الظهر لانه جمعة من وجه ظهر من وجه لقوات بعض الشرائط في حقه فيصلى اربعا اعتبارا للظهر ويقعد لا محالة على رأس الركعتين اعتبارا للجمعة ويقرأ فى الاخريين لا حتمال النفلية ولهما انه مدرك للجمعة في هذه الحالة حتى يشترط نية الجمعة وهى ركعتان ولاوجه لـمـاذكر لانهما مختلفان فلايبني أحدهما على تحريمة الآخر
And if he caught him in the tashahhud or in the prostration of forgetfulness, he builds Jumu'ah upon it according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: If he caught with him most of the second rak'ah, he builds Jumu'ah upon it; if he caught less than that, he builds Zuhr upon it, because it is Jumu'ah in one respect and Zuhr in another due to the loss of some conditions regarding him. So he prays four rak'ahs considering Zuhr, and he sits inevitably at the end of two rak'ahs considering Jumu'ah, and he recites in the last two due to the possibility of supererogatory. And for them (the two), he is a person who catches Jumu'ah in this situation, even if the intention of Jumu'ah is required, and it is two rak'ahs. There is no basis for what he mentioned because they are different, so one cannot be built upon the other's beginning.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage addresses a latecomer who catches the imam during Jumu'ah only in the tashahhud (final sitting) or in sajda sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs), the latecomer builds his prayer on Jumu'ah: he completes the prayer as two rak'ahs, because he is considered to have caught Jumu'ah. Imam Muhammad disagrees and distinguishes: if the latecomer caught most of the second rak'ah (e.g., joined in ruku'), he builds on Jumu'ah; if he caught only the tashahhud or sajda sahw (less than most of the second rak'ah), then his prayer is both Jumu'ah (from one aspect) and Zuhr (from another). To reconcile, Imam Muhammad rules that he prays four rak'ahs (considering it Zuhr) but must sit after two rak'ahs (considering Jumu'ah) and recite in the last two (as if it were nafl). The two shaykhs argue that he is a 'mudrik' (one who catches the prayer) and thus follows the imam's intention of Jumu'ah, which is two rak'ahs. They reject Imam Muhammad's view because the two prayers (Jumu'ah and Zuhr) are fundamentally different and cannot be built upon each other's starting intention.

Key Terms
مدرك (mudrik): One who catches the imam while the imam is still in prayer, even if only in the final sitting.
بناء (bina'): To build one's prayer upon what one caught with the imam, considering it as part of one's own prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf for a person who catches the imam only in the tashahhud of Jumu'ah?
A) He must pray Zuhr completely.
B) He builds on Jumu'ah and prays two rak'ahs.
C) He prays four rak'ahs sitting after two.
D) His prayer is invalid and he must repeat.

Key Takeaway
A latecomer who catches the imam in Jumu'ah in tashahhud or sajda sahw is considered mudrik and builds on Jumu'ah, praying two rak'ahs—this is the mufta bihi Hanafi view.

Latecomer Joining Jumu'ah in Tashahhud or Sajda Sahw
Hanafi internal dispute on latecomer's prayer type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi internal dispute on whether a latecomer who catches the Imam in tashahhud or sajda sahw prays Jumu'ah or Zuhr, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Catching the Imam in any part of Jumu'ah makes one a catcher of Jumu'ah itself.

When a person arrives late for Jumu'ah and finds the Imam in the final sitting or in the prostration of forgetfulness, a question arises: has he caught the Jumu'ah prayer or must he pray Zuhr? The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad disagree. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical consequence of each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the disagreement
Understand the factual situation: a latecomer catches the Imam in tashahhud or sajda sahw. The two shaykhs say he builds Jumu'ah upon it; Imam Muhammad distinguishes based on catching the majority of the second rak'ah.
The disagreement is intra-Hanafi; Imam Muhammad's view aligns with Malik and Shafi'i.
2
Analyze the proof of the two shaykhs
They argue the latecomer is a mudrik (catcher) of Jumu'ah because he joined the congregation while the Imam was still in prayer. Intending Jumu'ah is required, and Jumu'ah is only two rak'ahs.
They cite the general hadith: 'Whatever you catch, pray; whatever you miss, complete.'
3
Analyze Imam Muhammad's proof and cautious approach
Imam Muhammad considers the prayer hybrid: from one aspect Jumu'ah (due to intention), from another Zuhr (due to missing congregation). He recommends praying four rak'ahs with a sitting after two and recitation in the last two.
He relies on a hadith of Abu Hurairah about catching the ruku' of the last rak'ah.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response and tarjih
The two shaykhs reject mixing because the prayers are fundamentally different; one cannot be built upon the other's tahrimah. The hadith supporting Imam Muhammad is declared weak by muhaddithun.
The mufta bihi position is that of the two shaykhs: the latecomer prays Jumu'ah as two rak'ahs.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to the two shaykhs: pray 2 rak'ahs Jumu'ah. According to Imam Muhammad: if caught majority of second rak'ah, pray 2 rak'ahs Jumu'ah; if caught lesser part, pray 4 rak'ahs with a sitting at two and recitation in the last two.
The mufta bihi is the simpler ruling: all latecomers to Jumu'ah pray two rak'ahs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان ادركه في التشهد او فى سجود السهو بني عليها الجمعة عندهما وقال محمد ان ادرک معه اکثر الركعة الثانية بنى عليها الجمعة وان ادرك اقلها بنى عليها الظهر لانه جمعة من وجه ظهر من وجه لقوات بعض الشرائط في حقه فيصلى اربعا اعتبارا للظهر ويقعد لا محالة على رأس الركعتين اعتبارا للجمعة ويقرأ فى الاخريين لا حتمال النفلية ولهما انه مدرك للجمعة في هذه الحالة حتى يشترط نية الجمعة وهى ركعتان ولاوجه لـمــاذكر لانهما مختلفان فلايبني أحدهما على تحريمة الآخر ترجمہ اور اگر امام کو شہد یا سجدہ سہو میں پایا تو شیخین کے نزدیک اس پر جمعہ کی بنا کرے اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر امام کے ساتھ دوسری رکعت کا اکثر حصہ پالیا ہے تو اس پر جمعہ کی بناء کرے۔ اور اگر دوسری رکعت کا کم حصہ پایا تو اس پر ظہر کی بناء کرے۔ کیونکہ اس کی یہ نماز من وجہ جمعہ ہے اور من وجہ ظہر ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کے حق میں بعض شرطیں فوت ہو گئیں ۔ پس ظہر کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے چار رکعت پڑھے اور جمعہ کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے دو رکعت پر بالیقین بیٹھے اور آخر کی دورکعتوں میں قرآت کرے نفل کا احتمال ہونے کی وجہ سے اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس حالت میں وہ جمعہ کا پانے والا ہے حتی کہ اس پر جمعہ کی نیت کرنا شرط قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ اور جمعہ دوہی رکعت ہے۔ اور جو امام محمد نے ذکر کیا ہے اس کی کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ دونوں نمازیں مختلف ہیں اس لئے ایک کو دوسرے کے تحریمہ پرمبنی نہیں کر سکتے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے امام کو نماز جمعہ کے تشہد میں پایا یا سجدہ سہو میں پایا تو شیخین کے نزدیک یہ شخص جمعہ کی نماز پوری کرے۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ اگر اس نے اکثر رکعت ثانیہ کو پالیا مثلاً دوسری رکعت کے رکوع میں امام کے ساتھ شریک ہو گیا تو جمعہ کی نماز پوری کرے اور اگر دوسری رکعت کا اکثر حصہ نہیں پایا مثلاً رکوع کے بعد امام کے ساتھ شریک ہوا تو ظہر کی نماز پوری کرے۔ یہی قول امام مالک اور امام شافعی کا ہے۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تشہد یا سجدہ سہو میں امام کے ساتھ شریک ہونے والے کی یہ نماز من وجہ جمعہ ہے اور من وجہ ظہر ہے جمعہ تو اس لئے ہے کہ جمعہ کی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے اور ظہر اس لئے کہ اس کے حق میں جمعہ کی بعض شرطیں مثلاً جماعت فوت ہو چکی ہے کیونکہ امام کے سلام پھیرنے کے بعد یہ شخص تنہا نماز جمعہ ادا کرے گا۔ پس اس شخص کی نماز جب ایک اعتبار سے جمعہ ہے اور ایک اعتبار سے ظہر۔ تو ظہر کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے چار رکعت پڑھے اور جمعہ کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے دو رکعت پر بالیقین بیٹھے ۔ اور چونکہ آخر کی دو رکعتوں میں نفل ہونے کا احتمال ہے اس لئے ان میں سورۃ فاتحہ کے علاوہ سورت کی قبرأت بھی کرے۔ امام محمد کے مذہب کی تائید شارح نقایہ ملاعلی قاری کی پیش کردہ حدیث ابوہریرہ سے بھی ہوتی ہے حدیث کے الفاظ ہیں:۔ من ادرك الركوع من الركعة الاخيرة يوم الجمعة فليضف اليها أخرى ومن لم يدرك الركوع من ركعة الاخيرة فليصل الظهر اربعاً یعنی جس نے جمعہ کے دن دوسری رکعت کا رکوع پالیا تو اس کے ساتھ دوسری رکعت ملالے اور جس نے دوسری رکعت کا رکوع نہیں پایا تو ظہر کی چار رکعت پڑھے۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص اس حالت میں جمعہ کا پانے والا ہے حتی کہ اس کے لئے جمعہ کی نیت کرنا شرط ہے۔ اگر جمعہ کی نیت نہ کی تو اس کی اقتداء صحیح نہ ہوگی۔ حاصل یہ کہ تشہد یا سجدہ سہو میں امام کے ساتھ شریک ہو کر اس نے جمعہ کو پالیا ہے اور جمعہ پانے والا جمعہ ہی ادا کرے گا نہ کہ ظہر اور جمعہ کی چونکہ دورکعت ہیں۔ اس لئے یہ شخص دو رکعت پڑھے گا نہ کہ چار رکعتیں۔ رہا امام محمد کا بنظر احتیاط جمعہ اور ظہر دونوں پر عمل کرنا سو وہ غلط ہے۔ کیونکہ جمعہ اور ظہر دو مختلف نمازیں ہیں۔ لہذا ان میں سے ایک کا دوسرے کی تحریمہ پر بنا کر نا کس طرح درست ہوگا۔ شیخین کے مذہب کی تائید ابو ہریرہ کی اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا اقيمت الصلوة فلانا توها تسعون، واتوها وعليكم السكينة فما ادركتم فصلوا وما فاتكم فاتمو اوفى لفظ فاقضوا یعنی جب نماز جمعہ قائم کی جائے تو اس کی طرف دوڑ کر مت آؤ بلکہ وقار اور سکون کے ساتھ آؤ پس جو تم نے (امام کے ساتھ ) پالیا اس کو پڑھ لو اور جو فوت ہو گیا اس کی قضاء کر لو یعنی امام کے سلام پھیرنے کے بعد اس کو پورا کر لو۔ رہا امام محمد کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث ابو ہریرہ کا جواب تو اس کو محدثین نے ضعیف کہا ہے۔ (عنایہ )
And if he catches him in the tashahhud or in the sajda sahw, he builds Jumu'ah upon it according to them (the two shaykhs). And Muhammad said: If he catches with him the majority of the second rak'ah, he builds Jumu'ah upon it; and if he catches the lesser part, he builds Zuhr upon it, because it is from one aspect Jumu'ah and from one aspect Zuhr due to the loss of some conditions in his case. So he prays four rak'ahs considering Zuhr, and he sits necessarily at the end of two rak'ahs considering Jumu'ah, and he recites in the last two due to the possibility of nafl. And for them (the two shaykhs), he is a person who has caught Jumu'ah in this situation, so much so that the intention of Jumu'ah is required of him, and it is two rak'ahs. And there is no justification for what he (Muhammad) mentioned because they are different, so one cannot be built upon the tahrimah of the other. Translation: And if he catches the Imam in tashahhud or sajda sahw, then according to the two shaykhs, he builds Jumu'ah upon it. And Imam Muhammad said: If he catches the majority of the second rak'ah with the Imam, then he builds Jumu'ah upon it; and if he catches the lesser part of the second rak'ah, then he builds Zuhr upon it. Because his prayer is from one aspect Jumu'ah and from one aspect Zuhr, because some conditions are lost in his case. So considering Zuhr he prays four rak'ahs, and considering Jumu'ah he sits necessarily at the end of two rak'ahs, and he recites in the last two due to the possibility of it being nafl. And the proof of the two shaykhs is that in this state he is a person who has caught Jumu'ah, so much so that intending Jumu'ah is made a condition for him, and Jumu'ah is only two rak'ahs. And what Imam Muhammad mentioned has no basis, because these two prayers are different, so one cannot be built upon the tahrimah of the other. Explanation: The scenario is that if someone catches the Imam in the tashahhud of Jumu'ah prayer or in sajda sahw, then according to the two shaykhs this person should complete Jumu'ah prayer. And Imam Muhammad said: If he caught the majority of the second rak'ah, for example he joined the Imam in the ruku' of the second rak'ah, then he should complete Jumu'ah; and if he did not catch the majority of the second rak'ah, for example he joined the Imam after ruku', then he should complete Zuhr prayer. This is also the opinion of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i. Imam Muhammad's proof is that the prayer of the one joining in tashahhud or sajda sahw is from one aspect Jumu'ah and from one aspect Zuhr. It is Jumu'ah because intending Jumu'ah is necessary, and it is Zuhr because some conditions of Jumu'ah, such as congregation, are lost in his case, because after the Imam says salam, this person will pray Jumu'ah alone. So since his prayer is from one aspect Jumu'ah and from one aspect Zuhr, considering Zuhr he prays four rak'ahs, and considering Jumu'ah he sits necessarily at two rak'ahs. And because there is a possibility that the last two rak'ahs are nafl, he recites a surah in them in addition to Surah al-Fatihah. Imam Muhammad's madhhab is also supported by the hadith of Abu Hurairah presented by the commentator of Niqayah, Mulla Ali Qari; the wording is: 'Whoever catches the ruku' of the last rak'ah on Friday, let him add another to it, and whoever does not catch the ruku' of the last rak'ah, let him pray Zuhr four rak'ahs.' That is, whoever catches the ruku' of the second rak'ah on Friday should add another rak'ah to it, and whoever does not catch the ruku' of the second rak'ah should pray Zuhr four rak'ahs. The proof of the two shaykhs is that this person in this state is a person who has caught Jumu'ah, so much so that intending Jumu'ah is a condition for him. If he does not intend Jumu'ah, his following is not valid. The conclusion is that by catching the Imam in tashahhud or sajda sahw, he has caught Jumu'ah, and the one who catches Jumu'ah should perform Jumu'ah, not Zuhr; and since Jumu'ah is two rak'ahs, this person should pray two rak'ahs, not four. As for Imam Muhammad's acting upon both Jumu'ah and Zuhr out of caution, that is wrong because Jumu'ah and Zuhr are two different prayers, so how can one be built upon the tahrimah of the other? The opinion of the two shaykhs is also supported by the hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'When the prayer is established, do not come running, but come with tranquility, and whatever you catch, pray, and whatever you miss, complete' (or in another wording 'make up'). That is, when the Jumu'ah prayer is established, do not come running to it, but come with dignity and tranquility; so whatever you catch with the Imam, pray, and whatever you miss, make it up after the Imam says salam. As for the response to the hadith presented by Imam Muhammad, the muhaddithun have declared it weak (from al-Inayah).
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a latecomer to Jumu'ah who catches the Imam in the final tashahhud or in sajda sahw. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that such a person has caught Jumu'ah in its entirety (as he joined the congregation while the Imam was still in prayer) and therefore must complete Jumu'ah as two rak'ahs, intending Jumu'ah. Imam Muhammad, however, distinguishes between catching the majority of the second rak'ah (e.g., joining in ruku') versus the lesser part (after ruku'). In the former, he prays Jumu'ah; in the latter, he prays Zuhr four rak'ahs. Imam Muhammad argues that the latecomer's prayer is hybrid: from one aspect it is Jumu'ah (due to intention), from another Zuhr (due to missing congregation). He therefore recommends a cautious approach: pray four rak'ahs with a sitting after two (like Jumu'ah) and recitation in the last two (like nafl). The two shaykhs reject this, asserting that the prayer is unequivocally Jumu'ah because the latecomer has caught the Imam in prayer; building one prayer upon another's tahrimah is invalid because the prayers are fundamentally different. The text also notes that Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i agree with Imam Muhammad. The commentary then provides supporting hadiths for both sides, but notes that Imam Muhammad's hadith is considered weak by muhaddithun. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the two shaykhs: the latecomer prays Jumu'ah as two rak'ahs.

Key Terms
تشهد (tashahhud): The sitting of the prayer in which the supplication of tashahhud is recited, typically in the final rak'ah.
سجود السهو (sajda al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to correct errors in prayer.
بناء (bina'): To build upon a prior prayer; here, meaning to consider oneself as having caught Jumu'ah and to continue from where the Imam is.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The initial takbir that renders the prayer sacred and prohibits worldly actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if a person catches the Imam in tashahhud of Jumu'ah, how many rak'ahs does he pray?
A) Four rak'ahs of Zuhr
B) Two rak'ahs of Jumu'ah
C) Four rak'ahs as a combination of Jumu'ah and Zuhr
D) He must repeat the prayer later

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position is that catching the Imam in any part of Jumu'ah makes one a catcher of the prayer; the latecomer prays two rak'ahs of Jumu'ah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
