Eid Prayer: Wajib or Sunnah? Resolving the Hanafi Dispute
Resolves the dispute whether Eid prayer is wajib or sunnah with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on Eid prayer (wajib vs sunnah), identify the evidence for each, and explain why the relied-upon view is Sunnah mu'akkadah.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is Sunnah mu'akkadah – obligatory in practice, but its proof is from the Sunnah, not the Quran.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: Is Eid prayer wajib (obligatory) or Sunnah (recommended)? The text presents both views, weighs the evidence, and settles on the position that Eid prayer is Sunnah mu'akkadah – an emphasized sunnah that carries practical weight but is not at the level of fard. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi technical distinction between fard, wajib, and sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and initial ruling
The passage begins with a general statement: Eid prayer is wajib upon those upon whom Friday prayer is wajib. Note that this is the initial claim, but it is later qualified.
This sets the scope: conditions for jumu'ah (free, male, resident, etc.) also apply to Eid prayer.
2
Examine the internal Hanafi disagreement
The text quotes al-Jami' al-Saghir: If two Eids coincide, the first is Sunnah and the second is fard. The commentator explains that this nass (clear text) supports the Sunnah view, while the earlier part (wajib) is a narration from Abu Hanifa. Thus, there are two positions within the school.
Imam Muhammad's text is Zahir al-Riwayah and is the basis for the relied-upon view.
3
Analyze the evidence for each position
Two 'faces' (wajh) are presented: Face 1 (Sunnah) relies on the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah) and the hadith of the Bedouin where the Prophet said only five prayers are obligatory, implying no other obligatory prayer. Face 2 (Wajib) relies on the fact that Eid prayer is mandated on the same conditions as Jumu'ah, and on the general command to pray.
The Bedouin hadith is a key dalil for the Sunnah view: 'Are there any others? He said: No, unless you volunteer.'
4
Identify the tarjih (preference)
The text states 'al-awwal asahh' (the first is more correct), meaning the Sunnah view is preferred. This tarjih is based on the strength of the Bedouin hadith and the clear text from al-Jami' al-Saghir.
This tarjih aligns with Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and is the mufta bihi position.
5
Understand the terminological nuance
The passage ends by explaining why Eid prayer is called 'Sunnah' even though it is binding: 'tasmiiatuhu sunnatan li wujubihi bi al-sunnah' – it is called Sunnah because its obligation is established by the Sunnah (prophetic practice), not by a definitive Quranic text.
This is a Hanafi technicality: something obligatory by Sunnah is termed 'Sunnah' in legal classification, indicating a lower level than fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نماز عید کی شرعی حیثیت
(المصالح العقلیہ )
و تجب صلواة العيد على كل من تجب عليه صلواة الجمعة و فى الجامع الصغير عيدان اجتمعا في يوم واحد فالاول سنة والثانى فريضة ولايترك واحد منها قال وهذا اتنصيص على السنة والاول على الوجوب وهو رواية عن ابي حنيفة وجه الاول مواظبة النبى الله ووجه الثاني قوله في حديث الاعرابی عقیب سؤاله هل على غيرهن قال لا الا ان تطوع والاول اصح و تسميته سنة لوجوبه بالسنة
ترجمہ اور عید کی نماز واجب ہوتی ہے ہر اس شخص پر جس پر جمعہ کی نماز واجب ہوتی ہے اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ ایک روز میں دو عیدیں جمع ہوئیں تو پہلی نسبت ہے۔ اور دوسری فرض ہے اور دونوں میں سے کسی کو نہ چھوڑا جائے۔ فاضل مصنف نے کہا کہ یہ عید کی نماز کے سنت ہونے کا صریحی بیان ہے اور ادل واجب ہونے کا صریحی بیان ہے اور یہی ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے۔ قول اول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ
Legal status of Eid prayer (the rational considerations). The Eid prayer is obligatory upon everyone upon whom Friday prayer is obligatory. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: If two Eids coincide on one day, the first (Eid) is Sunnah and the second is fard, and neither should be left. The author (of al-Hidayah) said: This is a clear text (nass) that (the first) is Sunnah, and the first (part of the quote) indicates obligation (wajib), and that is a narration from Abu Hanifa. The first face (wijs) is the Prophet's constancy (in performing it). The second face is his saying in the hadith of the Bedouin after his question: 'Are there any others besides them?' He said: 'No, unless you volunteer (extra).' And the first (face) is correct (asahh). And calling it Sunnah is because its obligation is established by the Sunnah. Translation: And Eid prayer is obligatory upon everyone upon whom Friday prayer is obligatory. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Two Eids have gathered on one day, so the first is Sunnah and the second is fard, and neither should be omitted. The author said: This is a clear statement that (the first) is Sunnah, and the first (part) indicates obligation, and that is a narration from Abu Hanifa. The first face (reason) is the Prophet's constancy. The second face is his saying in the hadith of the Bedouin after his question: 'Are there any others besides them?' He said: 'No, unless you volunteer.' The first face is correct. And calling it Sunnah is because its obligation is by the Sunnah. The first face (reason) is that...
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage addresses the legal status of Eid prayer within the Hanafi school. The text begins with a general ruling: Eid prayer is obligatory (wajib) for those on whom Jumu'ah is obligatory. However, a quote from al-Jami' al-Saghir (by Imam Muhammad) states that if two Eids coincide, the first is Sunnah and the second is fard. The commentator (likely from al-Hidayah) notes that this is a clear text indicating Sunnah, while the first part of the quote (about obligation) indicates a different view (wajib), and this second view is a narration from Abu Hanifa. The dispute is between two 'faces' (wajh): the first face argues that Eid prayer is Sunnah because the Prophet constantly performed it. The second face argues it is wajib based on the hadith of the Bedouin, where the Prophet listed only five daily prayers as obligatory, but then said 'unless you volunteer extra', implying no other obligatory prayers beyond those five, which would make Eid non-obligatory (but the text says the first face is correct). The term 'sunnah' here means it is obligatory but its obligation is established by the Sunnah (i.e., through prophetic practice and hadith, not through the Quran), hence it is called Sunnah. The Urdu commentary begins to explain the first face but cuts off.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): Here, a legally binding practice established by the Prophet's Sunnah, which is obligatory (wajib) in the sense that it must be fulfilled, but not at the level of fard. Often termed Sunnah mu'akkadah.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation; here it refers to the claim that Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory) according to the narration from Abu Hanifa.
تسميته سنة لوجوبه بالسنة (tasmiyyatu sunnatan li wujubihi bi al-sunnah): Calling (the prayer) 'Sunnah' because its obligation is established by the Sunnah (prophetic practice) rather than by a definitive Quranic text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the text say Eid prayer is called 'sunnah' even though it is wajib?
A) Because it is optional
B) Because its obligation is established by the Sunnah, not the Quran
C) Because it is only recommended for men
D) Because it is a voluntary prayer

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is Sunnah mu'akkadah in the relied-upon Hanafi view; its obligation is proven by the Sunnah, not the Quran, so it is not fard but carries a binding recommendation.

Salah — Prayer

Eid Prayer: Wajib or Sunnah? The Hanafi Position
Presents proofs and responses in the dispute over Eid prayer's legal status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Eid prayer (wajib), explain why the Prophet's muwāẓabah indicates wujūb, and critique the Bedouin hadith objection using the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib; the term 'sunnah' in al-Jami' al-Saghir refers to its evidentiary source, not its legal category.

This passage examines a classic dispute over whether the Eid prayer is obligatory or recommended. While the Hanafi school holds it is wajib based on the Prophet's consistent practice, other schools and even some Hanafi texts seem to label it sunnah. The key is understanding the technical meaning of 'sunnah' in this context and the strength of different proofs. Let us unpack the arguments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the explicit ruling in the matn: Eid prayer is wajib upon those on whom Jumu'ah is wajib. Note that this is a narration from Abu Hanifa and the relied-upon view.
The text says 'wa huwa riwayatun 'an Abi Hanifah' and 'al-awṣaḥ'.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Recognize that the opposing view (ascribed to Malik, Shafi'i, and some Hanafis) considers Eid prayer sunnah. Their evidence includes the hadith of the Bedouin where the Prophet said there are only five obligatory prayers, and the statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir that when Eid and Jumu'ah coincide, the Eid prayer is sunnah.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the opponent's dalil: the Bedouin asked if there are any obligatory prayers beyond the five, and the Prophet replied 'No, unless you do voluntary acts' (lā illā an tatawwa‘). This seems to exclude Eid prayer from obligation.
Also the use of 'sunnah' in al-Jami' al-Saghir appears to contradict the wajib claim.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the two Hanafi rebuttals: (1) The Bedouin was a villager, and Eid prayer is not wajib on villagers, so the answer was tailored to him. (2) The conversation may have occurred before the obligation of Eid prayer was revealed. Additionally, the imperative in the Quranic verse (li-tukabbirū) indicates obligation when interpreted as the Eid prayer takbīr.
The commentator further explains that 'sunnah' in al-Jami' al-Saghir means 'obligation proven by the Sunnah,' not that the prayer itself is sunnah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Recognize the practical consequence: according to the wajib view, missing Eid prayer without excuse is a sin; according to the sunnah view, it is not a sin but one loses reward. The Hanafi school adopts the first view as mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نماز عید کی شرعی حیثیت
(المصالح العقلیہ)
و تجب صلواة العيد على كل من تجب عليه صلواة الجمعة و فى الجامع الصغير عيدان اجتمعا في يوم واحد فالاول سنة والثانى فريضة ولايترك واحد منها قال وهذا اتنصيص على السنة والاول على الوجوب وهو رواية عن ابي حنيفة وجه الاول مواظبة النبى الله ووجه الثاني قوله في حديث الاعرابی عقیب سؤاله هل على غير قال لا الا ان تطوع والاول اصح و تسميته سنة لوجوبه بالسنة
ترجمہ اور عید کی نماز واجب ہوتی ہے ہر اس شخص پر جس پر جمعہ کی نماز واجب ہوتی ہے اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ ایک روز میں دو عیدیں جمع ہوئیں تو پہلی نسبت ہے۔ اور دوسری فرض ہے اور دونوں میں سے کسی کو نہ چھوڑا جائے۔ فاضل مصنف نے کہا کہ یہ عید کی نماز کے سنت ہونے کا صریحی بیان ہے اور ادل واجب ہونے کا صریحی بیان ہے اور یہی ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے۔ قول اول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس پر مواظبت فرمائی ہے۔ اور قول ثانی کی وجہ حدیث اعرابی میں اس کے دوال کرنے کے بعد کہ کیا مجھ پر ان کے علاوہ بھی کوئی نماز ہے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہ قول ہے کہ نہیں مگر یہ کہ اپنی طرف سے نیک کام کے طور پر کرے۔ اور قول اول اصح ہے اور اس کا سنت نام رکھنا اس لئے ہے کہ اس کا وجوب سنت سے ثابت ہے۔ تشریح قدوری کے بیان کے مطابق نماز عید واجب ہے کیونکہ قدوری نے فرمایا کہ نماز عید اس شخص پر واجب ہوتی ہے جس پر نماز جمعہ واجب ہوتی ہے جامع صغیر کے بیان کے مطابق عید کی نماز سنت ہے۔ کیونکہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں کہا ہے کہ اگر ایک دن میں دو عید میں جمع ہو جائیں یعنی جمعہ کے دن عید الفطر یا عید الاضحی کا دن پڑ جائے تو اول یعنی عید کی نماز مسنون اور جمعہ کی نماز فرض ہے۔ شارح انقایه لاعلی قاری نے تحریر فر مایا ہے کہ اصح قول کے مطابق ہمارے نزدیک عید کی نماز واجب ہے۔ یہی ابو حنیفہ سے مروی ہے امام مالک امام شافعی اور بعض احناف کے نزدیک عید کی نماز سنت ہے ۔ امام احمد فرض کفایہ کے قائل ہیں۔
صلوۃ عیدین کے واجب ہونے کی دلیل عیدین کی نماز پر آنحضرت صلے اللہ علیہ وسلم کا بغیر ترک کئے مواظبت اور ہمیشگی فرمانا ہے۔ کیونکہ نبی کریم صلے اللہ علیہ وسلم کی مواظبت دلیل وجوب ہوتی ہے۔ قول ثانی یعنی مسنون ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اہل نجد میں سے ایک اعرابی شخص پریشان حال آیا۔ اس کا مقصد سفر اسلام کے بارے میں معلومات حاصل کرنا تھا چنانچہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اسلام کے ایک جز کو بیان کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ دن رات میں پانچ نمازیں ہیں۔ یہ سن کر اس نے کہا ھل علی غیر من کیا مجھ پر ان پانچ نمازوں کے سواء بھی کوئی نماز ہے۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جواب میں ارشاد فر مایالا الا ان تطوع نہیں مگر یہ کہ بطور نفل پڑھے اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ پانچ نمازوں کے علاوہ باقی تمام نمازیں غیر فرض ہیں یعنی نفل ہیں پس عیدین کی نماز کا واجب نہ ہونا ثابت ہو گیا، ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب تو یہ ہے کہ سائل گاؤں کا باشندہ تھا اور گاؤں والوں پر عید کی نماز واجب نہیں ہوتی اس لئے آنحضرت صلے اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اس کے حسب حال جواب ارشاد فر مایا۔ دوسرا جواب یہ دیا گیا کہ بہت ممکن ہے کہ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی یہ گفتگو نماز عید کے واجب ہونے سے پہلے کی ہو نماز عید کے وجوب پر باری تعالیٰ کا قول و لِتُكَبِّرُ وا اللهَ عَلَى مَا هَدَاكُمْ بھی دلالت کرتا ہے کیونکہ و لتكبر وااللہ کی تفسیر صلوٰۃ عید کے ساتھ کی گئی ہے اور یہ امر کا صیغہ ہے جس کا موجب وجوب ہے۔ رہا امام محم کا جامع صغیر میں صلوۃ عید کوسنت کہنا تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ عید کی نماز کا وجوب سنت سے ثابت ہے یہ مطلب ہر گز نہیں کہ عید کی نماز سنت ہے۔
The legal status of Eid prayer (Rational benefits). The Eid prayer is wajib upon every person upon whom the Friday prayer is wajib. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: if two Eids coincide in one day, the first is sunnah and the second is fard, and neither should be left. The author said: This is an explicit statement on it being sunnah, and the first (statement) on obligation, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa. The basis of the first (obligation view) is the Prophet's continuous practice. The basis of the second (sunnah view) is his statement in the hadith of the Bedouin following his question: 'Are there any others besides them?' He said: 'No, unless you do voluntary acts.' And the first is more correct, and calling it 'sunnah' is because its obligation is established by the Sunnah. Translation: The Eid prayer is wajib upon every person upon whom the Friday prayer is wajib. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is said: if two Eids coincide in one day, the first is sunnah and the second is fard, and neither should be left. The author said that this is an explicit statement on it being sunnah, and the first emphasizes obligation, and this is a narration from Abu Hanifa. The basis of the first view is that the Prophet continuously performed it. The basis of the second view is the hadith of the Bedouin after asking 'Are there any other prayers besides these?' The Prophet said: 'No, unless you do it as a voluntary act.' And the first view is more correct, and calling it 'sunnah' is because its obligation is proven by the Sunnah. Explanation: According to Quduri, the Eid prayer is wajib because he said it is wajib on those upon whom Jumu'ah is wajib. According to the statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is sunnah. Because Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir that if two Eids coincide in one day – i.e., Eid al-Fitr or Eid al-Adha falls on Friday – then the first (Eid) is sunnah and the Jumu'ah is fard. The commentator 'Ali al-Qari wrote in Sharh al-Nuqayah that according to the more correct view, in our school the Eid prayer is wajib. This is narrated from Abu Hanifa. Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and some Hanafis hold that Eid prayer is sunnah. Imam Ahmad holds it is fard kifaya. The proof for the obligation of Eid prayers is the Prophet's continuous and uninterrupted performance of them, because the Prophet's continuous practice is proof of obligation. The proof for the second view (sunnah) is that a Bedouin from Najd came in a distressed state; his aim was to get information about Islam. So the Prophet, while explaining a part of Islam, said: There are five prayers day and night. Hearing this, he said: 'Are there any other prayers besides these five on me?' The Prophet replied: 'No, except that you pray voluntarily.' From this hadith, it is known that all prayers besides the five are non-obligatory, i.e., nafl. Thus it is established that the Eid prayer is not wajib. Our response to this is that the questioner was a villager, and on villagers the Eid prayer is not wajib, so the Prophet answered according to his situation. A second response: it is very possible that this conversation of the Prophet took place before the Eid prayer was made obligatory. The obligation of Eid prayer is also indicated by the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And that you may glorify Allah for His guidance' because 'that you may glorify Allah' has been interpreted as the Eid prayer, and this is an imperative form which indicates obligation. As for Imam Muhammad calling the Eid prayer 'sunnah' in al-Jami' al-Saghir, its meaning is that the obligation of Eid prayer is proven by the Sunnah; it does not ever mean that the Eid prayer is sunnah (i.e., non-obligatory).
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal status of the Eid prayer. The author first quotes the matn stating that the Eid prayer is wajib for those on whom Jumu'ah is wajib. Then he references a difference in al-Jami' al-Saghir where Imam Muhammad stated that if two Eids (Eid and Jumu'ah) coincide, the first (Eid) is sunnah and the second (Jumu'ah) is fard. The commentator explains that this indicates the Eid prayer is sunnah in one sense but the word 'sunnah' here refers to the fact that its obligation is proven by the Sunnah, not that it is non-obligatory. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that it is wajib, based on the Prophet's continuous practice. The opposing view cites the hadith of the Bedouin where the Prophet said there are only five obligatory prayers, implying no other obligatory prayers. The Hanafi response is that the Bedouin was from the village where Eid prayer is not wajib, or that the conversation occurred before Eid prayer was made obligatory. Additionally, the Quranic verse 'And that you may glorify Allah for His guidance' is interpreted as the Eid prayer, and the imperative form indicates obligation.

Key Terms
مواظبت (Muwāẓabat): The Prophet's continuous and consistent practice of an act without leaving it.
وجوب (Wujūb): Obligation; an act whose omission incurs sin.
سنت (Sunnah): In this context, it is used to mean the obligation is proven by the Sunnah (i.e., by a hadith that is not mutawatir), not that the act is non-obligatory.
أمر (Amr): Imperative form in Arabic grammar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the relied-upon ruling for Eid prayer?
A) Sunnah muakkadah
B) Fard kifaya
C) Wajib
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
The Eid prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school due to the Prophet's continuous practice, and the term 'sunnah' in al-Jami' al-Saghir refers to its proof source, not its legal category.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Recommended Acts for the Two Eids
Lists the mustahabb acts before Eid prayer with their proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five mustahabb acts for Eid al-Fitr and state the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Eid sunnah acts: eat, ghusl, miswak, perfume, best clothes — all mustahabb, not wajib.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hadayah outlines the recommended acts (mustahabb) for the day of Eid al-Fitr. Understanding these acts helps you follow the Prophetic practice and distinguish between what is obligatory and what is commendable. The author provides both direct hadith evidence and analogy with Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Recall the occasion
Eid al-Fitr morning, before leaving for the prayer ground (musalla).
2
List the five acts
Eating something, performing ghusl, using miswak, applying perfume, wearing the best clothes.
Some scholars add other acts, but these are the core from this passage.
3
Identify the evidence
Direct hadith for eating (the Prophet ate before Fitr) and for ghusl (he performed ghusl on Eids). Ghusl and perfume also supported by qiyas on Jumu'ah.
Qiyas: 'because it is a day of gathering, so ghusl and perfume are prescribed as on Jumu'ah'.
4
Note the hukm
These acts are mustahabb (sunnah ghayr muakkadah), not wajib. Omitting them is not sinful but loses reward.
This is the established Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Apply in practice
Plan your Eid morning to include these acts. Remember that the prayer itself is valid without them, but following the sunnah brings barakah.

عیدین میں مسنون اعمال
ويستجب في يوم الفطر ان يطعم قبل الخروج الى المصلى ويغتسل ویستاک و يتطيب لما روى انه كان يطعم في يوم الفطر قبل ان يخرج الى المصلى وكان يغتسل فى العيدين ولانه يوم اجتماع فيسن فيه الغسل والتطيب كما فى الجمعة ويلبس احسن ثيابه لان النبي كان له جبة فنك اوصوف يلبسها في الاعياد
ترجمہ مستحب یہ ہے کہ عید الفطر کے دن مصلی عید گاہ جانے سے پہلے کچھ کھالے اور غسل کرئے مسواک کرے، خوشبو لگائے
Chapter on the recommended acts of the two Eids. It is mustahabb on the day of Fitr to eat before going out to the prayer place, to perform ghusl, use miswak, apply perfume, because it is narrated that he (the Prophet) used to eat on Fitr before going out to the prayer place, and he used to perform ghusl on the two Eids, and because it is a day of gathering, so ghusl and perfume are prescribed as on Jumu'ah. And to wear his best clothes because the Prophet had a cloak of [؟] which he wore on the Eids. Translation: It is mustahabb that on the day of Eid al-Fitr, before going out to the prayer place (musalla), he should eat something, perform ghusl, use miswak, apply perfume, ...
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage enumerates the recommended acts (mustahabb) for the two Eids. The author mentions five acts for the day of Eid al-Fitr: eating before leaving for the prayer, performing ghusl (ritual bath), using miswak (tooth stick), applying perfume, and wearing the best clothes. These acts are established by the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and also by analogy with Jumu'ah, as both are congregational days of celebration. The proof for eating is the hadith that the Prophet used to eat on Eid al-Fitr before the prayer. The other acts are also proven by his practice and by qiyas on the day of Jumu'ah. These acts are mustahabb, meaning they are recommended but not obligatory; leaving them is not sinful but one loses the reward of following the sunnah.

Key Terms
مستحب (Mustahabb): An act that is recommended; doing it is rewarded, omitting it is not sinful.
غسل (Ghusl): A full ritual bath with water covering the entire body; recommended for Eid.
مصلی (Muṣallā): The open area where the Eid prayer is performed; originally the prayer place outside the mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT mentioned as a recommended act for Eid al-Fitr?
A) Eating before the prayer
B) Performing ghusl
C) Giving charity before the prayer
D) Wearing one's best clothes

Key Takeaway
The five mustahabb acts for Eid al-Fitr are eating before prayer, ghusl, miswak, perfume, and wearing best clothes—all sunnah, not obligatory.

Recommended Acts (Mustahabbat) on 'Eid Day
Listing mustahabbat for 'Eid days with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five mustahab acts for 'Eid days, identify their hadith proofs, and distinguish the eating-related sunnah between 'Eid al-Fitr and 'Eid al-Adha.

Core Idea
The Prophet's sunnah for 'Eid includes distinctive acts: eat before Fitr prayer, postpone eating after Adha prayer, perform ghusl, use perfume, and wear best clothes.

The 'Eid day is a celebration and congregation. The Hanafi school, based on prophetic practice and rational analogy, recommends specific acts to enhance the spirit of gratitude and joy. This lesson presents these acts with their evidences, helping you incorporate them into your 'Eid practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
List all the mustahab acts mentioned in the passage for 'Eid al-Fitr and 'Eid al-Adha. Note that some acts apply to both Eids, while one (eating timing) differs.
There are five core acts: eating before Fitr prayer, ghusl, miswak, perfume, and wearing best clothes. For Adha, eating is after prayer.
2
Locate the hadith proof for each act
For each mustahab act, find the specific hadith cited in the passage. Distinguish between the primary hadith (Bukhari, Ibn Majah) and the additional narrations (Tirmidhi, Jabir).
The passage provides explicit citations: Bukhari for eating dates on Fitr, Ibn Majah for ghusl on both Eids and 'Arafah, etc.
3
Understand the rational analogy (qiyas)
Note the author's argument that 'Eid is a day of congregation like Jumu'ah, thus ghusl and perfume are sunnah by analogy. Consider how this qiyas strengthens the ruling.
This qiyas is based on the shared illah (effective cause) of public gathering.
4
Distinguish between 'Eid al-Fitr and 'Eid al-Adha
Observe the specific difference: on Fitr, the sunnah is to eat before the prayer; on Adha, the sunnah is to wait until after the prayer. Identify the hadith evidence for each.
Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah report that the Prophet would not eat on Adha until after prayer.

باب العيدين
کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم عید گاہ جانے سے پہلے عید الفطر کے دن کھاتے تھے اور آپ عیدین کے دن غسل کرتے تھے۔ اور اس لئے کہ عید مجتمع ہونے کا دن ہے اس لئے اس میں بھی غسل کرنا اور خوشبو لگانا مسنون ہوگا۔ جیسے جمعہ میں ہے اور اپنے کپڑوں میں سے اچھے کپڑے پہنے کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے پاس فنک یا صوف کا جبہ تھا آپ اس کو عیدوں میں پہنا کرتے تھے۔ تشریح عید کے دن کے مستحبات میں سے ایک یہ ہے کہ عید گاہ جانے سے پہلے کوئی میٹھی چیز تناول کرے۔ امام بخاری نے حضرت ان سے روایت کیا ہے قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يغد ويوم الفطر حتى يا كل ثمرات ويا كلهن انسرا حضرت انسؓ نے فرمایا ہے کہ رسول صلے اللہ علیہ وسلم عید الفطر کے دن نماز عید کے لئے ) تشریف نہ لیجاتے یہاں تک کہ طاق عدد چھوہارے نہ کھا لیتے ۔ اور ترمذی اور ابن ماجہ میں ہے ان رسول الله صلے الله عليه وسلم كان لا يخرج يوم الفطر حتى اكل وكان لا يـاكـل يـوم النحر حتى يصلی یعنی عید الفطر کے دن بغیر کچھ کھائے نہ نکلتے۔ اور عید الاضحی کے دن بغیر نماز پڑھے نہ کھاتے تھے۔ دوسرا مستحب عمل غسل ہے۔ چنانچہ ابن ماجہ نے فاکہہ بن سعد کی حدیث روایت کی ہے۔ ان رسول اللہ صلے اللہ عليه وسلم كان يغتسل يوم الفطر ويوم لنحر و يوم العرفة یعنی رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم عید الفطر کے دن عید الاضحی کے دن اور عرفہ کے دن غسل فرمایا کرتے تھے عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عیدین کا دن لوگوں کے جمع ہونے کا دن ہے اس لئے اس میں غسل کرنا خوشبو لگانا مسنون ہے جیسا کہ جمعہ کے دن یہ دونوں عمل مسنون ہیں۔ تیسرا مستحب عمل یہ ہے کہ اپنے موجودہ کپڑوں میں سے جو کپڑے عمدہ اور اچھے ہوں ان کو زیب تن کرئے کیونکہ نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پاس فنک یا صوف کا جبہ تھا عید وغیرہ کے موقعہ پر آپ اس کو پہنا کرتے تھے فنک ایک جانور ہے جس کی کھال کی پوستین بہت عمدہ ہوتی ہے۔ ایک دوسری روایت میں ہے عن جابر بن عبدالله قال كان للنبي الله عليه وسلم برد احمر يلبسه في الجمعة و العيد جابر بن عبد اللہ کہتے ہیں کہ حضور صل اللہ علیہ وسلم کے پاس سرخ ھاری دار یمنی چادر تھی جس کو آپ جمعہ اور عید میں پہنتے تھے۔
Recommended acts of the two Eids: It is mustahab on the day of Fitr to eat something before going out to the musalla, to perform ghusl, to use miswak, and to apply perfume, because it is narrated that he used to eat on the day of Fitr before going out to the musalla, and he used to perform ghusl on the two Eids. And because it is a day of gathering, so ghusl and perfume are sunnah, just as on Jumu'ah. And he should wear his best clothes, because the Prophet had a jubbah of fank (a type of fur) or wool that he used to wear on the Eids. Translation: It is mustahab to eat something before going to the Eidgah, perform ghusl, use miswak, apply perfume. Commentary: One of the mustahabbat of 'Eid day is to eat something sweet before going to the Eidgah. Imam Bukhari narrated from Anas that the Messenger of Allah would not go out on the day of Fitr until he had eaten some dates, and he would eat an odd number. And in Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah: that the Messenger of Allah would not go out on the day of Fitr until he ate, and he would not eat on the day of Nahr until he prayed. The second mustahab act is ghusl. Ibn Majah narrated from Fakih ibn Sa'd: that the Messenger of Allah used to perform ghusl on the day of Fitr, the day of Nahr, and the day of Arafah. The rational proof is that the day of 'Eid is a day of gathering, so ghusl and perfume are sunnah, just as on Jumu'ah. The third mustahab act is to wear one's best clothes, because the Prophet had a jubbah of fank or wool that he wore on Eids. Fank is an animal whose skin makes excellent fur. In another narration from Jabir: the Prophet had a red garment (burd) that he wore on Jumu'ah and 'Eid.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah details the sunan (recommended acts) for the day of 'Eid, particularly 'Eid al-Fitr. The author states that it is mustahab (recommended) to eat before going to the prayer ground, to perform ghusl (full ablution), to use miswak (tooth stick), to apply perfume, and to wear one's best clothes. The commentary provides hadith proofs: for eating, the Prophet would eat an odd number of dates before 'Eid al-Fitr prayer (Bukhari), and on 'Eid al-Adha he would not eat until after the prayer (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah). For ghusl, the Prophet performed it on both Eids and on the day of Arafah (Ibn Majah). The rational analogy is that 'Eid is a day of congregation, similar to Jumu'ah, so these acts are sunnah. For clothing, the Prophet wore a special jubbah of fur or wool on Eids, and also a red garment (burd) from Yemen. These acts are all mustahab, meaning they are recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahab): Recommended but not obligatory; synonymous with mandub; skipping it without reason is not sinful but losing reward.
غسل (ghusl): Full body wash, a recommended act on 'Eid days.
مسواک (miswak): Tooth cleaning stick, recommended for oral hygiene and sunnah.
تطيب (tatayyub): Applying perfume; recommended on 'Eid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a mustahab act specifically for 'Eid al-Adha according to the text?
A) Eating before prayer
B) Not eating until after prayer
C) Wearing new clothes
D) Applying perfume

Key Takeaway
The recommended acts for 'Eid are sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah, rooted in the Prophet's practice, and differ between Fitr and Adha regarding eating timing.

Sadaqat al-Fitr Timing and Takbir Dispute
Ruling on paying sadaqat al-fitr before 'Eid prayer and the dispute about takbir on the way

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred time for paying sadaqat al-fitr and explain the Hanafi position on takbir for 'Eid al-Fitr, including the intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
Sadaqat al-fitr before prayer; takbir aloud not sunnah for Fitr according to Abu Hanifah.

This lesson covers two important practices for 'Eid al-Fitr: the timing of sadaqat al-fitr and whether to recite takbir loudly on the way to prayer. The text presents a clear ruling on the first and details an intra-Hanafi dispute on the second, highlighting Abu Hanifah's reliance on the principle of concealment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the passage
Read the passage and note that it covers two separate but related 'Eid practices: when to pay sadaqat al-fitr and whether to say takbir aloud on the way to the prayer ground.
The passage is from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah.
2
Determine the ruling on sadaqat al-fitr timing
Find the statement that sadaqat al-fitr should be paid before the 'Eid prayer, and identify the evidence (hadith of Ibn Umar).
The text says 'it is wajib' in the commentary, but the primary ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
3
Identify the dispute on takbir for 'Eid al-Fitr
Locate the different positions: Abu Hanifah says no loud takbir; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say yes by analogy with 'Eid al-Adha.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifah's proof
Understand his reasoning: the original principle in remembrance is concealment; loud takbir was only prescribed for 'Eid al-Adha because it is the 'day of takbir'.
Thus, the specification for Adha prevents analogical extension to Fitr.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The author sides with Abu Hanifah, so the relied-upon view is that it is not sunnah (or makruh tanzih) to recite takbir loudly on the way to 'Eid al-Fitr prayer.
This is the position for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤدي صدقة الفطر اغناء للفقير ليتفرغ قلبه للصلواة ويتوجه الى المصلى ولا يكبر عند ابي حنيفة في طريق المصلى وعندهما يكبر اعتبارا بالاضحى وله ان الاصل فى الثناء الاخفاء والشرع ورد به في الاضحى لانه يوم تكبير ولا كذلك الفطر
ترجمہ اور محتاج کو بے نیاز کرنے کے لئے صدقہ فطر ادا کرے تاکہ نماز کے لئے اس کا دل فارغ ہو جائے اور عید گاہ کی طرف متوجہ ہو۔ اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک عید گاہ کے راستہ میں تکبیر نہ کہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک عیدالاضحی پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے تکبیر کہے۔ امام ابو خفیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ثناء اور ذکر میں اصل اخفاء ہے اور جبر کے ساتھ شریعت عید الاضحی میں دار ود ہوئی ہے کیونکہ عیدالانی تکبیر کا دن ہے اور عید الفطر ایسا نہیں ہے۔ تشریح نماز عید سے پہلے صدقہ فطر ادا کرنا واجب ہے کیونکہ صحیحین میں ابن عمر کی حدیث ہے۔ ان النبی صلے الله عليه وسلم امريز كوة الفطر ان يؤدى قبل خروج الناس الى الصلوة وكان هویؤ ديها قبل ذالک بیوم او بیو مين (رواه ابوداؤد)
And he should pay sadaqat al-fitr to enrich the poor so that his heart may be free for prayer and he may proceed to the musalla. And according to Abu Hanifah, he should not say takbir on the way to the musalla, but according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he should say takbir, analogy with al-Adha. And for him (Abu Hanifah), the principle is that in praise and remembrance, concealment is the original; and the shari'ah came with loudness on al-Adha because it is the day of takbir, and not so for Fitr. Commentary: It is wajib to pay sadaqat al-fitr before the 'Eid prayer, because in the two Sahihs the hadith of Ibn Umar: that the Prophet ordered zakat al-fitr to be paid before the people go out to prayer. And he used to pay it a day or two before. (Narrated by Abu Dawud)
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage covers two topics related to 'Eid al-Fitr. First, the timing of sadaqat al-fitr: it is recommended (or in some views wajib according to the commentary) to pay it before the 'Eid prayer, so that the poor can also participate in the festivities with a free heart. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet ordered sadaqat al-fitr to be paid before people go out to prayer. Second, the issue of saying takbir (Allahu Akbar) on the way to the prayer ground: According to Imam Abu Hanifah, one should not say it loudly on the way to 'Eid al-Fitr prayer, because takbir is a form of remembrance and the original principle is to keep it concealed (silent). The Shari'ah prescribed aloud takbir only for 'Eid al-Adha because it is the 'day of takbir', not for 'Eid al-Fitr. However, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) analogize from 'Eid al-Adha and say that takbir should be said aloud on the way for both Eids. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifah for 'Eid al-Fitr, as explained by the author.

Key Terms
تکبیر (takbir): Uttering 'Allahu Akbar'. Here specifically about saying it loudly on the way to 'Eid prayer.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two chief disciples of Abu Hanifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifah, what is the ruling on saying takbir loudly on the way to 'Eid al-Fitr prayer?
A) It is sunnah muakkadah
B) It is not sunnah
C) It is wajib
D) It is haram

Key Takeaway
Sadaqat al-fitr should be paid before 'Eid prayer; takbir aloud on the way to Fitr prayer is not sunnah according to Abu Hanifah, contrary to the Sahibayn.

The Three Sunnan Before 'Eid Prayer
Explains the sunan before 'Eid prayer with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three recommended acts before 'Eid prayer, cite the Hanafi proofs from hadith and qiyas, and distinguish between the rulings for 'Eid al-Fitr and 'Eid al-Adha regarding eating.

Core Idea
Eating, ghusl, perfume, and best clothes before 'Eid prayer are sunnah muakkadah—recommended, not obligatory.

Before heading to the 'Eid prayer, the Prophet ﷺ consistently performed certain acts. These acts are not obligatory but are strongly recommended (sunnah muakkadah). In this lesson, we examine the three main sunan: eating something sweet before 'Eid al-Fitr, performing ghusl and applying perfume, and wearing one's best clothes. We will study the hadith evidence and the Hanafi reasoning that establishes these as sunnah rather than wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sunan
From the passage, list the recommended acts before the 'Eid prayer: (1) eating before 'Eid al-Fitr, (2) performing ghusl and applying perfume, (3) wearing the best clothes. Note the specific distinction between 'Eid al-Fitr (eat before prayer) and 'Eid al-Adha (eat after prayer).
The acts for both Eids are similar except the timing of eating.
2
Examine the hadith proofs
For each sunnah, locate the hadith cited in the passage. For eating: Bukhari (odd dates), Tirmidhi/Ibn Majah (eats before Fitr, eats after Nahr). For ghusl: Ibn Majah from Fakih ibn Sa'd. For clothing: the Prophet's fannak cloak and a red striped cloak worn on 'Eid and Friday.
The hadiths are all ahad, zanni al-thubut, but consistent action indicates sunnah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi wajh al-dalalah
Apply the Hanafi principle that the Prophet's habitual actions (fi'l) indicate sunnah unless a qarina shows wujub. Since no such qarina exists, these acts are sunnah muakkadah. The rational analogy (qiyas) to Friday further supports ghush and perfume being sunnah due to the shared illa of 'day of gathering'.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider ghusl for 'Eid as wajib based on analogy to Friday. The Hanafi school maintains it is sunnah because the analogy is not perfect; the Prophet's action is consistent with sunnah, not obligation. The mufta bihi is sunnah.
This difference has practical implications: omitting ghusl is not sinful in Hanafi but is discouraged.

Source Text

باب العيدين کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم عید گاہ جانے سے پہلے عید الفطر کے دن کھاتے تھے اور آپ عیدین کے دن غسل کرتے تھے۔ اور اس لئے کہ عید مجتمع ہونے کا دن ہے اس لئے اس میں بھی غسل کرنا اور خوشبو لگانا مسنون ہوگا۔ جیسے جمعہ میں ہے اور اپنے کپڑوں میں سے اچھے کپڑے پہنے کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے پاس فنک یا صوف کا جبہ تھا آپ اس کو عیدوں میں پہنا کرتے تھے۔ تشریح عید کے دن کے مستحبات میں سے ایک یہ ہے کہ عید گاہ جانے سے پہلے کوئی میٹھی چیز تناول کرے۔ امام بخاری نے حضرت انس سے روایت کیا ہے قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يغد ويوم الفطر حتى يا كل ثمرات ويا كلهن انسرا حضرت انسؓ نے فرمایا ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم عید الفطر کے دن نماز عید کے لئے تشریف نہ لے جاتے یہاں تک کہ طاق عدد چھوہارے نہ کھا لیتے ۔ اور ترمذی اور ابن ماجہ میں ہے ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان لا يخرج يوم الفطر حتى اكل وكان لا ياكل يوم النحر حتى يصلی یعنی عید الفطر کےدن بغیر کچھ کھائے نہ نکلتے۔ اور عید الاضحی کے دن بغیر نماز پڑھے نہ کھاتے تھے۔ دوسرا مستحب عمل غسل ہے۔ چنانچہ ابن ماجہ نے فاکہہ بن سعد کی حدیث روایت کی ہے۔ ان رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يغتسل يوم الفطر ويوم النحر و يوم العرفة یعنی رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم عید الفطر کے دن عید الاضحی کے دن اور عرفہ کے دن غسل فرمایا کرتے تھے عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عیدین کا دن لوگوں کے جمع ہونے کا دن ہے اس لئے اس میں غسل کرنا خوشبو لگانا مسنون ہے جیسا کہ جمعہ کے دن یہ دونوں عمل مسنون ہیں۔ تیسرا مستحب عمل یہ ہے کہ اپنے موجودہ کپڑوں میں سے جو کپڑے عمدہ اور اچھے ہوں ان کو زیب تن کرئے کیونکہ نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پاس فنک یا صوف کا جبہ تھا عید وغیرہ کے موقعہ پر آپ اس کو پہنا کرتے تھے فنک ایک جانور ہے جس کی کھال کی پوستین بہت عمدہ ہوتی ہے۔ ایک دوسری روایت میں ہے عن جابر بن عبدالله قال كان للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم برد احمر يلبسه في الجمعة و العيد جابر بن عبد اللہ کہتے ہیں کہ حضور صلى اللہ علیہ وسلم کے پاس سرخ دھاری دار یمنی چادر تھی جس کو آپ جمعہ اور عید میں پہنتے تھے۔
Chapter of the Two 'Eids. Because it is narrated that the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, used to eat on the day of 'Eid al-Fitr before going to the prayer ground, and he used to perform ghusl on the two 'Eids. And because the 'Eid is a day of gathering, therefore performing ghusl and applying perfume is sunnah in it, just as on Friday. And wear the best of your clothes because the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, had a cloak of fannak or wool, which he used to wear on the 'Eids. Explanation: Among the recommended acts of the day of 'Eid is to eat something sweet before going to the prayer ground. Imam Bukhari narrated from Anas, he said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, would not go out on the day of 'Eid al-Fitr until he had eaten some dates, and he would eat them individually. Anas said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, would not go out for the 'Eid prayer on the day of 'Eid al-Fitr until he had eaten an odd number of dates. And in Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, would not go out on the day of 'Eid al-Fitr until he had eaten, and he would not eat on the day of al-Nahr until he had prayed. That is, on 'Eid al-Fitr he would not go out without eating something, and on 'Eid al-Adha he would not eat until after prayer. The second recommended act is ghusl. Ibn Majah narrated from Fakih ibn Sa'd: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, used to perform ghusl on the day of 'Eid al-Fitr, the day of al-Nahr, and the day of 'Arafah. The rational proof is that the day of the two 'Eids is a day of gathering, so performing ghusl and applying perfume is sunnah, just as it is sunnah on Friday. The third recommended act is to wear the best and finest clothes from among one's available garments, because the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, had a cloak of fannak or wool, and he would wear it on the 'Eids and other occasions. Fannak is an animal whose skin makes a very fine fur coat. In another narration: Jabir ibn 'Abdullah said: The Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, had a red Yemeni cloak with stripes which he wore on Friday and on the 'Eid.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the sunan (recommended acts) before the 'Eid prayer. The author first states the general principle: because the Prophet used to eat before 'Eid al-Fitr and perform ghusl on both 'Eids, these acts are sunnah. The reasoning is that 'Eid is a day of gathering, similar to Friday, so ghusl and perfume are recommended. Then the author expands with detailed proofs. For eating before 'Eid al-Fitr, he cites a hadith from Bukhari that the Prophet would not go out until he ate an odd number of dates. A second hadith from Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah distinguishes ‘Eid al-Fitr (eat before prayer) from ‘Eid al-Adha (eat after prayer). For ghusl, he cites Ibn Majah’s hadith that the Prophet performed ghusl on both 'Eids and on the day of 'Arafa, and adds a rational analogy to Friday. For clothing, he mentions the Prophet’s fannak cloak and a red cloak worn on 'Eid and Friday. All three acts are sunnah, meaning they are recommended but not obligatory; omission does not invalidate the prayer but is contrary to the ideal.

Key Terms
مسنون (masnūn): An act established by the Prophet's consistent practice, recommended but not obligatory.
عیدین (‘īdayn): The two festivals: Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.
فنک (fannak): A type of animal (probably sable or marten) whose fur is used for high-quality cloaks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is eating before the 'Eid prayer considered sunnah for 'Eid al-Fitr but not for 'Eid al-Adha?
A) Because the Prophet ate dates before 'Eid al-Fitr but ate only after prayer on 'Eid al-Adha, as established in hadith.
B) Because 'Eid al-Fitr breaks the fast of Ramadan, so eating is wajib.
C) Because 'Eid al-Adha involves sacrifice, so one must wait.
D) Because the Prophet was hungry on 'Eid al-Fitr but not on 'Eid al-Adha.

Key Takeaway
The three sunan before 'Eid prayer—eating (for Fitr), ghusl/perfume, and best clothes—are sunnah muakkadah, confirmed by the Prophet's practice and analogy to Friday.

Walking to Eid Prayer Ground and the Exception for the Weak
Ruling on walking to Eid and exception for the weak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on walking to the Eid prayer ground and identify the exception for the weak who cannot attend the musalla.

Core Idea
Walking to the Eid musalla is mustahabb, but the weak may pray in the mosque with a deputy imam.

This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on walking to the Eid prayer ground. While it is highly recommended (mustahabb) to walk to the musalla, the school provides an accommodation for those who are weak or unable to go. The imam of the time may appoint a deputy to lead the Eid prayer inside the city mosque for such individuals, based on the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is walking to the Eid prayer ground. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended) according to the Hanafi school, based on the statement of Sayyiduna Umar that it is sunnah.
This is not obligatory; one may ride with a valid excuse.
2
Recognize the evidence
The evidence comes from the narration of Sayyiduna Umar and the practice of Sayyiduna Ali. Ali appointed a deputy to lead the weak in the mosque while walking to the musalla himself.
The narration demonstrates that walking is the preferred practice and that the exception is established.
3
Understand the exception for the weak
If some people are excused from going to the musalla due to weakness, the imam should appoint someone to lead them in the Eid prayer inside the city mosque. This shows the school's flexibility.
The deputy imam leads the full Eid prayer; those unable to attend the musalla thus fulfill the sunnah in the mosque.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the sunnah of walking to the Eid prayer ground and the permissibility of appointing a deputy imam for those unable to go to the musalla. The Hanafi school considers walking to the Eid prayer ground as mustahabb, based on the practice of the Prophet and the early Caliphs. The exception for the weak demonstrates flexibility in the school. The narration of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) is used as evidence: he appointed a deputy to lead the weak in the mosque while he himself went to the musalla with others.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustaḥabb): Recommended action, not obligatory.
سنت (sunnah): Act established by the Prophet's practice, carrying reward for doing and no sin for leaving.

Reciting Takbir on the Way to Eid al-Fitr: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on takbir on way to Eid al-Fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi Hanafi position on reciting takbir loudly on the way to Eid al-Fitr, explain the arguments of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the tarjih mechanism to resolve the intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
On Eid al-Fitr, takbir is recited softly; only Eid al-Adha has a specific text for loud takbir.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the takbir should be recited loudly or softly on the way to Eid al-Fitr prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it should be recited softly, while his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), argue for loud recitation by analogy to Eid al-Adha. We will examine the proofs, the objection, and the Hanafi response that leads to the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Positions
State clearly what Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn rule regarding takbir on the way to Eid al-Fitr. Abu Hanifa says softly (sirri); Sahibayn say loudly (jihri).
2
Examine the Sahibayn's Proof
The Sahibayn use qiyas (analogy) to Eid al-Adha. They argue that since both are Eid prayers, the same rule of loud takbir applies. Identify the illa (legal cause) they assume: commonality of 'Eid'.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's Proof
Abu Hanifa relies on the general principle that dhikr is best concealed (Quran 7:205 and hadith). He also notes that loud takbir on Eid al-Adha is an exception based on a specific text (Surah al-Hajj 22:28 or al-Baqarah 2:203), and Eid al-Fitr does not share the same ila because it is not tied to Hajj.
Note the usul point: qiyas is invalid when the far' (Eid al-Fitr) does not share the effective cause (illa) of the asl (Eid al-Adha).
4
Consider the Objection and Response
An objection is raised citing the verse 'to complete the number and magnify Allah' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:185) and a hadith of Ibn Umar. The response explains that the verse refers to takbir within the prayer, not on the way, and the hadith is weak due to a matruk narrator (Walid ibn Muhammad).
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view: takbir on the way to Eid al-Fitr is recited softly. The practical consequence: one should not raise the voice when reciting takbir on the way to Eid al-Fitr prayer.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس مسئلہ میں اختلاف ہے کہ عید الفطر کے دن عید گاہ جاتے وقت راستہ میں تکبیر بآواز بلند پڑھنے یا آہستہ سے حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ یہ آواز بلند نہ پڑھئے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ بہ آواز بلند پڑھے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل عید الاضحی پر قیاس ہے یعنی جس طرح عیدالانی میں تکبیر یہ آواز بلند مشروع ہے اسی طرح عید الفطر میں بھی یہ آواز بلند مشروع ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ذکر کے اندر اصل تو اخفاء ہے چنانچہ ارشاد باری تعالی ہے وَاذْكُرُرَبَّكَ فِي نَفْسِكَ تَضَرُّعًا وَخِيفَةً وَدُونَ الْجَهْرِ مِنَ الْقَوْل اور حضور سال اللہ علیہ وسلم کا ارشاد ہے خیر الذكر الخفی و خیر الرزق ما يكفی عمدہ ذکر ذکر خفی ہے اور عمدہ رزق تقدر کفایت ہے نہ ضرورت سے زائد اور نہ کم ہو ایک اردو شاعر کہتا ہے مجھے جو بھی دے وہ قبول ہے مگر التجا یہ ضرور ہے میرے ظرف سے بھی سواء نہ دے میری آرزو سے بھی کم نہ دے بہر حال ذکر کے اندراصل اخفاء ہے مک عید الاضحی کے ایام میں بالجبر تکبیر پر خلاف قیاس نص وارد ہوئی ہے اللہ نے فرمایا۔ وَاذْكُرُ اللَّهَ فِي أَيَّامٍ مَّعْدُودَاتٍ، مفسرین نے کہا ہے کہ یہاں عید قرباں کے ایام میں تکبیر جہری مراد ہے اور عید الفطر عید الاضحی کےہم معنی بھی نہیں کیونکہ عیدالاضحی ارکان حج میں سے ایک رکن کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے یعنی اس دن میں بعض ارکان حج ادا کئے جاتے ہیں اور عید الفطر میں یہ بات نہیں پائی جاتی پس جب عید الفطر عید الاضحی کے معنی میں نہیں ہے۔ تو عید الفطر کوعیدالاضحی پر قیاس کرنا بھی مناسب نہ ہوگا۔ اس جگہ ایک اعتراض کیا جا سکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ حضرت امام صاحب کا یہ فرمانا کہ عید الفطر میں تکبیر جہری پر شریعت وارد نہیں ہوئی یہ بات تسلیم نہیں ہے اس لئے خدائے لم یزل ولا یزال نے فرمایا ہے وَلِتُكْمِلُوا الْعِدَّةَ وَلِتُكَبِّرُوا اللَّهَ عَلَى مَا هَدَاكُمْ اس آیت میں رمضان المبارک کے صوته بالتكبير من رسول خدا عید الفطر اور عید قربان کے دن تکبیر کے ساتھ اپنی آواز کو بلند کرتے ہوئے نکلتے تھے پس ثابت ہوگیا کہ عید الفطر کے دن بھی تکبیر جر کی پر نص موجود ہے۔ جواب آیت میں نماز کے اندر کی تکبیر مراد ہے آیت کے معنی یہ ہوں گے صلوا صلوة العيد وكبروا الله فيها ، يعنى عيد الفطر کی نماز ادا کرو اور اس میں یہ یہ آواز بلند تکبیر کہور ہی حدیث ابن عمر تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث کی سند میں ولید بن محمد عن الز ہری ہے۔ اور ولید متروک الحدیث ہے۔ اس لئے یہ حدیث قابل استدلال نہ ہوگی۔
There is a dispute in this matter: on the day of Eid al-Fitr, when going to the prayer ground, should one recite the takbir loudly or softly? Imam Abu Hanifa said: Do not recite it loudly. And the two Sahibayn said: Recite it loudly. The proof of the two Sahibayn is analogy (qiyas) on Eid al-Adha: just as loud takbir is prescribed on Eid al-Adha, so also it is prescribed on Eid al-Fitr. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the original principle in dhikr (remembrance) is concealment. As Allah says: 'And remember your Lord within yourself in humility and fear and without loudness of speech.' And the Prophet said: 'The best remembrance is the hidden one, and the best provision is that which suffices.' In any case, the principle in remembrance is concealment. However, on the days of Eid al-Adha, a text (nass) has come that is contrary to analogy for loud takbir. Allah said: 'And remember Allah during [specific] numbered days.' The commentators said that here loud takbir is intended for the days of Eid al-Adha. And Eid al-Fitr does not share the same meaning as Eid al-Adha, because Eid al-Adha is associated with the rites of Hajj, which are not present in Eid al-Fitr. So when Eid al-Fitr is not equivalent in meaning to Eid al-Adha, analogizing Eid al-Fitr to Eid al-Adha is not appropriate. At this point, an objection can be raised: Imam Abu Hanifa's statement that no text has come for loud takbir on Eid al-Fitr is not accepted, because Allah says: 'That you may complete the number and magnify Allah for that He has guided you.' In this verse, after completing the fasts of Ramadan, takbir has been informed, and takbir becomes known only when it is said loudly. And from Ibn Umar it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah used to go out on Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha raising his voice with takbir. So it is established that there is a text for takbir on Eid al-Fitr (jihri). The answer: In the verse, the takbir inside the prayer is meant. The meaning of the verse is: 'Pray the Eid prayer and say takbir in it aloud.' As for the hadith of Ibn Umar, the answer is that in its chain there is Walid ibn Muhammad from al-Zuhri, and Walid is abandoned (matruk) in hadith. Therefore this hadith is not acceptable as evidence.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) regarding whether the takbir should be recited loudly or softly on the way to the Eid al-Fitr prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the takbir should be recited softly, based on the general principle that dhikr is best done secretly, as indicated by the Quranic verse (Surah al-A'raf 7:205) and the hadith 'The best remembrance is the hidden one'. He argues that the loud takbir on Eid al-Adha is an exception established by a specific text (Surah al-Hajj 22:28 or al-Baqarah 2:203) and that Eid al-Fitr does not share the same significance as Eid al-Adha (which is tied to Hajj rites), so analogy is invalid. The two Sahibayn analogize Eid al-Fitr to Eid al-Adha, claiming that both are Eids, so loud takbir should be prescribed. An objection is raised against Abu Hanifa's position, citing the Quranic verse (Surah al-Baqarah 2:185) and a hadith of Ibn Umar. The response explains that the verse refers to takbir within the prayer, not on the way, and the hadith of Ibn Umar has a weak chain (Walid ibn Muhammad is matruk). The Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa's position as the relied-upon view (mufta bihi), with the condition that the takbir is said softly on Eid al-Fitr.

Key Terms
تکبیر (takbīr): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' as a form of remembrance on the way to Eid prayer.
صاحبین (al-Ṣāḥibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa reject the analogy (qiyas) between Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha regarding loud takbir?
A) Because both Eids are the same in every respect.
B) Because Eid al-Adha is associated with Hajj rites, while Eid al-Fitr is not.
C) Because the hadith of Ibn Umar is authentic and overrides the analogy.
D) Because the Quran commands silence on both Eids.

Key Takeaway
According to the Hanafi school, takbir on the way to Eid al-Fitr is recited softly, based on the general principle of concealed dhikr and the absence of a specific text for loud recitation on this Eid.

Prohibition of Nafl Before Eid Prayer in the Musalla
Ruling on karahah of nafl before Eid prayer in musalla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing nafl before the Eid prayer, identify the basis for the karahah, and distinguish between the musalla and home regarding post-Eid nafl.

Core Idea
Performing voluntary prayers before Eid prayer in the musalla is makruh — the Prophet's practice sets the rule.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling about supererogatory prayers (nafl) in connection with the Eid prayer. The source passage explains that it is disliked (makruh) to pray nafl before the Eid prayer in the musalla, based on the Prophet's practice. However, there is a nuance: the dislike applies primarily in the musalla, while after returning home, it is recommended to pray two rak'ahs. Understanding this distinction helps avoid confusion about what is permitted on Eid day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What act is being ruled upon? (Performing nafl before the Eid prayer in the musalla.) What is the hukm? (Makruh tanzih, i.e., lightly disliked but not sinful.)
The ruling is based on the Prophet's omission despite his eagerness for prayer.
2
Locate the evidence
The primary evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, showing that the Prophet did not pray before the Eid prayer in the musalla. This omission is taken as evidence of karahah.
The Hanafi principle: the Prophet's persistent omission in the presence of motivation indicates prohibition or dislike.
3
Note the internal ikhtilaf
The passage mentions two opinions: one restricts karahah to the musalla; the other extends it to all locations before the Eid prayer. Understand the basis for each.
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that karahah is specific to the musalla, because the Prophet prayed nafl after returning home.
4
Apply to different scenarios
Consider: praying nafl before Eid in the musalla (makruh), praying nafl after Eid in the musalla (makruh), praying nafl after returning home (permissible, even recommended).
The hadith of Abu Sa'id confirms that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs after returning home.

ولا يتنفل في المصلى قبل صلوة العيد لان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يفعل ذلك مع حرصه على الصلواة ثم قيل الكراهة في المصلى خاصة وقيل فيه وفى غيره عامة لانه لم يفعله ترجمہ اور عید کی نماز سے پہلے عیدگاہ میں نفل نہ پڑھے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایسا نہیں کیا باوجود یکہ آپ نماز کے حریص تھے پھر کہا گیا کہ کراہت مخصوص طور پر عید گاہ میں ہے۔ اور کہا گیا کہ عید گاہ اور اس کے علاوہ میں عام ہے کیونکہ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے اس کو نہیں کیا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، نماز عید سے پہلے نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے عید گاہ میں بھی اور عید گاہ کے علاوہ بھی امام کے واسطے بھی مکروہ ہے اور مقتدی کے واسطے بھی ابن عباس کا قول ہے ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم خرج فصلى بهم العيد لم يصل قبلها ولا بعدها ، یعنی حضور صلى الله علیہ وسلم نے گھر سے نکل کر لوگوں کو عید کی نماز پڑھائی آپ نے نہ عید سے پہلے کوئی نفل نماز پڑھی اور نہ عید کے بعد حالانکہ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کو نماز کی بے پناہ حرض تھی ۔ اگر عید سے پہلے یا بعد میں نفل پڑھنے کی اجازت ہوتی تو اللہ کے رسول ضرور پڑھتے ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا ہے کہ بعض مشائخ کے نزدیک عید گاہ اور گھر دونوں جگہ کراہت عام ہے اور بعض نے فرمایا کہ عید کی نماز کے بعد عید گاہ کے اندر بلاشبہ نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ لیکن گھر آ کر نفل پڑھنا بلا کراہت جائز ہے۔ ابوسعید خدری کی حدیث ہے قال کان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يصلى قبل العيد شيئاً فاذا رجع الى منزله صلى رکعتین ۔ یعنی رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم عید سے پہلے کچھ نہیں پڑھتے تھے۔ لیکن جب اپنے گھر واپس آ جاتے تو دورکعت نفل ادا کرتے ۔
And one should not perform supererogatory prayer (nafl) in the musalla before the Eid prayer, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not do that despite his eagerness for prayer. Then it was said: The karahah is specifically in the musalla. And it was said: It is general in the musalla and elsewhere, because he did not do it. Translation: And one should not perform nafl before the Eid prayer in the Eid prayer ground, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not do that, despite his eagerness for prayer. Then it was said that the karahah is specifically in the Eid prayer ground. And it was said that it is general in the Eid prayer ground and elsewhere, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not do it. Explanation of the issue: Performing nafl before the Eid prayer is makruh, both in the musalla and elsewhere, for both the imam and the follower. The statement of Ibn Abbas: 'The Messenger of Allah went out and led them in the Eid prayer, he did not pray before it nor after it.' That is, the Prophet came out of his house and led the people in the Eid prayer; he prayed neither nafl before it nor after it, even though he had great eagerness for prayer. If there were permission to pray nafl before or after, the Messenger would have certainly done so. The author of al-Hidayah said: According to some mashayikh, the karahah is general both in the musalla and at home. And some said that after the Eid prayer, it is definitely makruh to pray nafl inside the musalla, but to pray nafl at home after returning is permissible without karahah. The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'The Messenger of Allah used not to pray anything before the Eid prayer, but when he returned to his house, he would pray two rak'ahs.'
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the karahah (dislike) of performing supererogatory prayers before the Eid prayer in the musalla. The primary evidence is the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who did not pray any nafl before or after the Eid prayer in the musalla, despite his love for prayer. Two opinions are mentioned: one restricts the karahah to the musalla only, and another extends it to any location (including home) before the Eid prayer. However, the relied-upon view is that it is makruh to pray nafl before the Eid prayer in the musalla, but it is permissible to pray nafl at home after returning. The hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri is cited to support this: the Prophet would pray two rak'ahs after returning home. The Hanafi school thus distinguishes between praying before the Eid prayer (which is not done) and praying after returning home (which is recommended).

Key Terms
مصلی (muṣallā): The open prayer ground outside the city used for Eid prayers.
کراہت (karāhah): Dislike; an act that is better to avoid but not sinful.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer, voluntary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying nafl before the Eid prayer in the musalla?
A) Sunnah
B) Wajib
C) Makruh
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
It is makruh tanzih to pray any voluntary prayer before the Eid prayer in the musalla, but permissible to pray nafl at home after the Eid prayer.

Time of Eid Prayer: From Sunrise to Zawal
Ruling on the time for Eid prayer from sunrise to zawal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time for Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school, identify the evidence from the Prophet's practice, and explain the ruling when the crescent is sighted after zawal.

Core Idea
Eid prayer time is from sunrise (one spear height) until zawal; after zawal, it is not valid.

The Eid prayer is a unique act of worship with a specific time window. This lesson clarifies when the time begins and ends according to the Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). You will also learn an important detail: if the crescent of Eid is sighted after zawal, the prayer is delayed to the next day. Understanding this timing ensures the prayer is performed correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the Eid prayer (salat al-Eid). According to the Hanafi school, it is wajib, but its time is specified as from sunrise to zawal.
The ruling on the time is independent of the debate on whether the prayer itself is wajib or sunnah.
2
State the time window
The time begins when the sun rises to the height of one or two spears (approximately 15-20 minutes after sunrise) and ends at zawal (when the sun passes the meridian).
This is derived from the Prophet's practice and is specific to Eid prayer, not general prayer times.
3
Note the evidence
The passage cites that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would pray Eid when the sun was at the height of one or two spears. This establishes the beginning time. The end at zawal is derived from the general principle that after zawal, the prayer time exits.
The evidence is a hadith indicating the Prophet's practice; it is considered a proof (dalil) for the Hanafi position.
4
Identify the exception
If the crescent for Eid al-Fitr is sighted after zawal, the prayer is delayed to the next day. This is to avoid praying on a day of doubt (yawm al-shakk).
This exception is specific to Eid al-Fitr and shows the school's caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا حلت الصلوة بارتفاع الشمس دخل وقتها الى الزوال او ذا زالت الشمس خرخ وقتها لانني كان يصلى العيد والشمس على قيد رمح او رمحين ولما شهدوا با لهلال بعد الزوال امر بالخروج الى المصلى من الغد ترجمہ اور جب سورج کے بلند ہونے سے نماز حلال ہوگئی تو نماز عید کا وقت داخل ہو گیا زوال آفتاب تک اور جب سورج ڈھل گیا تو عید کی نماز کا وقت نکل گیا۔ اس لئے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم عید کی نماز اس وقت پڑھتے جب سورج ایک نیزہ یا دو نیزہ بلند ہوتا۔ اور جب زوال کے
And when prayer becomes permissible at the rising of the sun, its time enters and extends to zawal (decline). And when the sun declines, its time exits. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray the Eid prayer when the sun was at the height of one or two spears. And when they testified to the crescent after zawal, he ordered them to go out to the musalla the next day. Translation: And when the prayer becomes permissible with the rising of the sun, the time for Eid prayer enters and remains until zawal. And when the sun declines, the time for Eid prayer has left. Because the Prophet used to pray the Eid prayer when the sun was at the height of one or two spears. And when they witnessed the crescent after zawal, he ordered them to go out to the musalla the next day.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the time for Eid prayer. The Hanafi school holds that the time for both Eid prayers begins after sunrise (when the sun has risen to the height of a spear or two, approximately 15-20 minutes after sunrise) and continues until zawal (when the sun passes the meridian). The evidence is the practice of the Prophet, who would pray at that time. A secondary point is mentioned: if the crescent for Eid al-Fitr is sighted after zawal, the prayer is delayed to the next day. This is a specific ruling in Hanafi fiqh to avoid praying on the day of doubt.

Key Terms
زوال (zawāl): The decline of the sun from its zenith; the end of the time for Eid prayer.
رمح (rumḥ): A spear; used as a measure of sun's height above horizon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ending time for Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) At sunrise
B) At zawal (when the sun declines)
C) At mid-afternoon
D) At sunset

Key Takeaway
The time for Eid prayer begins at sunrise (spear height) and ends at zawal; after that, it cannot be performed.

Ruling on Nafl Before Eid Prayer in the Musalla
States the ruling of karaha for nafl before Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafl before Eid prayer in the musalla and identify the dalil and the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Nafl before Eid in the musalla is makruh because the Prophet abandoned it despite his eagerness.

This lesson examines a specific ruling regarding voluntary prayer before the Eid prayer. While many assume extra prayers are always commendable, the Hanafi school holds that in the musalla (Eid prayer ground) it is makruh. We will explore the evidence from the Prophet's practice and an internal disagreement about the scope of the karaha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (Nafl prayer before Eid in the musalla). What is the hukm? (Makruh).
The act is specifically voluntary prayer, not the Eid prayer itself.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's (ﷺ) practice: he did not pray nafl before Eid despite his well-known eagerness for prayer. This is recorded in hadith.
The dalil is a fi'li (action-based) Sunnah, categorized as ahad and zanni al-dalala.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Why does the Prophet's abandonment prove karaha? Because his eagerness for prayer normally leads him to perform voluntary prayers, so his omitting it here indicates that it is not legislated and is therefore discouraged.
This reasoning combines the absence of action with the known motive to pray.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some scholars restrict the karaha to the musalla only; others extend it generally (including at home). The text mentions both views.
This ikhtilaf is among later Hanafi mashayikh, not the founding imams.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that the karaha is specific to the musalla, as favored by Imam al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah. Praying nafl at home after the Eid prayer is not makruh.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يتنفل في المصلى قبل صلوة العيد لان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يفعل ذلك مع حرصه على الصلواة ثم قيل الكراهة في المصلى خاصة وقيل فيه وفى غيره عامة لانه لم يفعله
And he should not pray nafl in the musalla before the Eid prayer, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not do that despite his eagerness for prayer. Then it was said: the karaha is specific to the musalla, and it was said: it is general in it and elsewhere, because he did not do it.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof. It addresses whether one may pray voluntary (nafl) prayers in the musalla (prayer ground) before the Eid prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that it is makruh (reprehensible) to do so. The proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not do it, despite his well-known eagerness for prayer. The text then notes a disagreement among the mashayikh: some say the karaha is specific to the musalla, others say it is general (including at home). The preferred opinion, as supported by the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, is that nafl before Eid is makruh in the musalla but permissible at home after Eid. The passage clarifies that the karaha applies to both imam and ma'mum.

Key Terms
المصلى (al-musalla): The place designated for Eid prayer, usually an open ground outside the city.
الكراهة (al-karahah): Legal reprehension; an act that is discouraged but not sinful if done.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying nafl in the musalla before the Eid prayer?
A) It is mustahab
B) It is makruh
C) It is haram
D) It is mubah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, praying nafl before Eid prayer in the musalla is makruh, based on the Prophet's abandonment despite his eagerness for prayer.

Time for Eid Prayer from Sunrise to Zawal
Establishes the beginning and end time for Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time for Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the proof from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Eid prayer time is from sunrise (spear's height) to zawal – a limited window derived from Prophetic practice.

This passage from Al-Hidayah defines the time for Eid prayer, a wajib act. It provides both a direct ruling and a proof from the Sunnah, illustrating how the Hanafi school derives time boundaries from the Prophet's actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the Eid prayer. According to the Hanafi school, it is wajib. The passage focuses on its time, not the ruling itself.
The time is a condition for the prayer's validity.
2
Note the time boundary
The passage states that the time begins when the sun rises (to a spear's height, approximately 15-20 minutes after sunrise) and ends at zawal (when the sun passes the meridian).
Zawal is the same as the start of Zuhr time.
3
Examine the first proof
The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray Eid when the sun was at the height of a spear or two. This indicates the preferred and normative time.
The hadith is from the practice of the Prophet, not a verbal command.
4
Examine the second proof
When witnesses sighted the crescent after zawal, the Prophet delayed the Eid prayer to the next day. This shows that the time had passed after zawal.
This incident (related in hadith) demonstrates the end of the time.
5
Understand the Hanafi reliance
The Hanafi school uses these actions of the Prophet to establish a fixed time window. The time is not discretionary but defined by clear natural markers.
This is a dalil naqli (textual evidence) with zanni thubut and dalala.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا حلت الصلوة بارتفاع الشمس دخل وقتها الى الزوال او اذا زالت الشمس خرج وقتها لانه كان يصلى العيد والشمس على قيد رمح او رمحين ولما شهدوا بالهلال بعد الزوال امر بالخروج الى المصلى من الغد
And when prayer becomes permissible with the rising of the sun, its time enters until zawal. And when the sun passes the meridian, its time exits. Because he (peace be upon him) used to pray Eid when the sun was at the height of a spear or two, and when they testified to the sighting of the crescent after zawal, he ordered going out to the musalla on the next day.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof concerning the time of Eid prayer. The passage defines the time as from sunrise (when the sun has risen approximately a spear's height, i.e., about 15-20 minutes after sunrise) until zawal (when the sun begins to decline from its zenith). Two proofs are given: first, the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who would pray Eid when the sun was a spear or two high; second, an incident where witnesses came after zawal to testify about the crescent, and the Prophet delayed the Eid prayer to the next day, indicating that the time had passed. The commentary adds that the beginning time is when the sun is one or two spears high, and the end time is zawal. This is the Hanafi position, and it is derived from the Prophet's actions and the prohibition of prayer at sunrise.

Key Terms
الزوال (al-zawal): The moment when the sun passes its zenith and begins to decline.
رمح (rumh): A spear; used as a measure of the sun's height above the horizon (approx. 7-8 degrees).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the sun reaches its zenith
B) When the sun sets
C) At midday exactly
D) At the time of Duha prayer

Key Takeaway
The time for Eid prayer is strictly bounded by the rising and zenith of the sun, based on the Prophet's practice.
