Method of Eid Prayer: Takbirs and Recitation
Details the Hanafi method of Eid prayer takbirs and responds to opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of takbirs in Eid prayer and explain the reasoning for preferring the lesser number over the opposing view.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school adds three extra takbirs after the opening in the first rak'ah and three after recitation in the second — taking the lesser when custom is broken.

Eid prayer has extra takbirs that distinguish it from regular prayers. But how many? The Hanafi school, based on Ibn Mas'ud, prescribes a specific number. This lesson unpacks that ruling and the reasoning behind it, contrasting with the view of Ibn Abbas and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact sequence of takbirs in both rak'ahs as held by the Hanafi school.
The first rak'ah: opening takbir, then 3 extra, then recitation, then ruku takbir. Second rak'ah: recitation, then 3 extra, then ruku takbir.
2
Identify the opposing view
What did Ibn Abbas and al-Shafi'i hold regarding the number and placement of takbirs?
Ibn Abbas reports 5 extra after opening in each rak'ah (or 4 in one narration). Al-Shafi'i interprets all narrations as additions, totaling 15-16 takbirs.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Understand the evidence from Ibn Mas'ud and the legal principle of 'taking the lesser' when an act breaks the norm.
The Hanafi school relies on the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and the idea that increasing takbirs is contrary to usual prayer, so the minimal established number is chosen.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school respond to the opposing proof? Consider the principle of joining the extra takbirs to the stronger takbirs.
In the first rak'ah, the extra takbirs are joined to the opening takbir (due to its strength as fard and precedence); in the second, to the ruku takbir.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in the number of takbirs in the prayer?
Hanafi: 9 total (including opening and ruku takbirs). Shafi'i: 15-16 total.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصلى الامام بالناس ركعتين يكبر فى الاولى للافتتاح و ثلثا بعدها ثم يقرأ الفاتحة وسورة ويكبر تكبيرة يركع بها ثم يبتدى في الركعة الثانية بالقرأة ثم يكبر ثلثا بعدها ويكبر رابعة يركع بها و هذا قول ابن مسعود وهو قولنا و قال ابن عباس يكبر فى الاولى للافتتاح و خمسا بعدها وفى الثانية يكبر خمسا ثم يقرأ و في رواية يكبر اربعا وظهر عمل العامة اليوم بقول ابن عباس الامر بنو الخلفاء فاما المذهب فالقول الأول لان التكبير ورفع الايدى خلاف المعهود فكان الاخذ بالاقل اولى ثم التكبيرات من اعلام الدين حتى يجبر بها فكان الأصل فيها الجمع وفي الركعة الأولى يجب الحاقها بتكبيرة الافتتاح لقوتها من حيث الفرضية والسبق و في الثانية لم يوجد الاكبيرة الركوع فوجب الضم اليها والشافعي اخذ بقول ابن عباس الا انه حمل المروى كله على الزوائد فصارت التكبيرات عنده خمسة عشر اوستة عشر
And the imam prays with the people two rak'ahs. He says takbir in the first for opening and three after it, then recites al-Fatihah and a surah, and says the takbir for ruku. Then he begins the second rak'ah with recitation, then says three takbirs after it, and says a fourth takbir for ruku. This is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud, and it is our saying. Ibn Abbas said: he says takbir in the first for opening and five after it, and in the second he says five takbirs then recites, and in one narration he says four. And today the practice of the common people has appeared according to the saying of Ibn Abbas by the order of the caliphs. As for the madhhab, it is the first saying, because takbir and raising the hands is contrary to what is customary, so taking the lesser is better. Then the takbirs are from the symbols of the religion, so the principle in them is gathering. In the first rak'ah, they must be joined to the takbir of opening due to its strength in terms of fardiyyah and precedence, and in the second there is only the takbir of ruku, so joining to it is necessary. Al-Shafi'i took the saying of Ibn Abbas, but he interpreted all that is narrated as additions, so the takbirs according to him are fifteen or sixteen.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the number and placement of takbirs in Eid prayer. The Hanafi position, attributed to Ibn Mas'ud, is: In the first rak'ah, say takbirat al-ihram, then three additional takbirs, then recite, then takbir for ruku. In the second rak'ah, recite first, then three additional takbirs, then takbir for ruku. Ibn Abbas proposed more takbirs (five after the opening in each rak'ah or four in some narrations). The Hanafi reasoning is that takbir and raising the hands are contrary to the customary practice, so taking the lesser number is preferable. Also, the takbirs are from the symbols of the religion, so the principle is to gather them. In the first rak'ah, they are joined to the opening takbir due to its strength (fard nature and precedence), and in the second they are joined to the ruku takbir. The passage notes that the common people followed Ibn Abbas's view due to the caliphs' order, but the madhhab remains the first. Imam al-Shafi'i adopted Ibn Abbas's view but considered all narrated numbers as additional, resulting in 15 or 16 total takbirs.

Key Terms
تکبیرات (takbirat): The additional takbirs recited in Eid prayer beyond the regular prayer.
الاولى (al-ula): First rak'ah in the context of Eid prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many extra takbirs are recited in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer?
A) Three before recitation
B) Three after recitation
C) Five after recitation
D) Four after recitation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes 3 extra takbirs after the opening in the first rak'ah and 3 after recitation in the second, based on Ibn Mas'ud and the principle of taking the lesser.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Manner of Eid Prayer and Dispute on Extra Takbirs
Explains the method of Eid prayer and the ikhtilaf between Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Abbas on takbirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method for Eid prayer and explain why the Hanafi school prefers Ibn Mas'ud's ruling (6 extra takbirs) over Ibn 'Abbas's ruling on the number and placement.

Core Idea
Eid prayer's extra takbirs are minimized (6 total) to avoid excessive deviation from normal prayer, following Ibn Mas'ud.

Eid prayer is a distinctive act of worship marked by extra takbirs. The Hanafi school has a specific method for their number and placement, based on the practice of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. This lesson explains that method and the scholarly disagreement with the Shafi'i school, which follows Ibn 'Abbas. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies why we act on the lesser number and how the takbirs are attached to the opening and bowing takbirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi method
State the Hanafi ruling for the number and order of takbirs in each rak'ah of Eid prayer.
First rak'ah: opening takbir, then 3 extra, then recitation, then bowing takbir. Second rak'ah: recitation, then 3 extra, then bowing takbir.
2
Locate the Hanafi proof
Identify the narration from Ibn Mas'ud that the Hanafi school relies on.
Ibn Mas'ud taught 9 takbirs total: 5 in first (including opening and bowing) and 4 in second (including bowing).
3
Identify the opposing school's view
State the Shafi'i position following Ibn 'Abbas: different number and placement of extra takbirs.
Ibn 'Abbas: 5 extra in first rak'ah (after opening) and 5 in second (before recitation), totaling 15 or 16 takbirs.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the reasoning: extra takbirs are a deviation from the norm, so taking the lesser number is preferred. The attachment rule (ilhāq) determines placement.
Extra takbirs are attached to the strongest takbir in each rak'ah: opening in first, bowing in second.
5
Determine the practical difference
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: the actual number of takbirs in each rak'ah and their position relative to recitation.
Hanafi: 9 total, extra after opening in first, after recitation in second. Shafi'i: 15+ total, extra before recitation in both.

باب العيدين
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم تشریح صاحب قدوری نے نماز عید کی کیفیت اس طرح بیان کی ہے۔ کہ امام لوگوں کو دو رکعت بایں طور پڑھائے کہ پہلے تکبیر تحریمہ کہئے پھر ثناء پڑھ کر تین زائد تکبیریں کہے پھر قرآت فاتحہ اور ضم سورت کرئے پھر تکبیر رکوع کہہ کر رکوع کرے اور سجدہ کرئے اس طرح رکعت اولی پوری ہو جائے گی دوسری رکعت میں پہلے قرآت فاتحہ اور ضم سورت کرے پھر تین زائد تکبیریں کہے اور رکوع کی تکبیر کہ کر رکوع کرے اس تفصیل کے مطابق دونوں رکعتوں میں نو تکبیریں ہوئیں چھ زائد دو تکبیرات رکوع اور ایک تکبیر تحریمہ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ ابن مسعود کا قول ہے گویا ابن مسعودؓ کے نزدیک عید کی دونوں رکعتوں میں کل 4 تکبیریں ہیں، یہی علماء احناف کا مذہب ہے۔ ابن مسعود کا قول اس لئے ہے کہ روایت کیا گیا ہے کان ابن مسعود جالساً وعنده خذيفة وابو موسى الاشعرى فسالهم سعيد بن العاص عن التكبيرا فى صلوة العيد فقال حذيفة سل لاشعرى فقال الاشعرى سل عبدالله فانه اقدمنا واعلمنا فسأله فقال ابن مسعود يكبر اربعاً ثم يقرأ ثم يكبر فيركع ثم يقوم فى الثانيه فيقرأ ثم يكبر اربعاً بعد القراءة ليني ابن مسعود ، خذیفہ اور ابوموسی اشعری تشریف فرما تھے کہ ان سے سعید بن العاص نے نماز عید کی تکبیروں کے بارے میں دریافت کیا خذیفہ نے کہا اشعری سے پوچھو اشعری نے کہا کہ عبداللہ سے پوچھ لو اس لئے عبداللہ ہم میں قدیم العبد بھی ہیں اور صاحب علم بھی چنانچہ ابن مسعود سے دریافت کیا تو ابن مسعودؓ نے کہا کہ چار تکبیروں کے پھر قرآت کرے، پھر تکبیروں کہہ کر رکوع کرے۔ پھر دوسری رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو جائے اور قرآت کرے پھر قرآت کے بعد چار تکبیریں کہے پہلی رکعت میں جن چار تکبیروں کا ذکر کیا گیا ہے ان میں ایک تعبیر تحریمہ اور زمین زوائد ہیں اور دوسری رکعت میں چار تکبیروں میں سے ایک تکبیر ورکوع اور تین زوائد ہیں بہر حال بن مسعودؓ کے اس قول سے تکبیروں کا ثبوت ملتا ہے نیز سروق سے مروی ہے قال عبدالله بن مسعود يعلمنا التكبير في العيدين تسع تكبيرات خمس في الاولى واربع في الاخيرة ويوالى بين القراء تین یعنی ابن مسعود ہم کو عیدین میں 4 تکبیروں کی تعلیم دیتے تھے پانچ پہلی رکعت میں اور چار دوسری دکرت میں اور دونوں قراتوں کے درمیان وصل کرتے تھے۔ روایت میں پانچ تکبیروں سے مراد تکبیر تحریمہ تکبیر رکوع اور تین زوائد ہیں۔ اور چار سے مراد تین زوائد اور ایک تکبیر رکوع ہے۔ اس اثر سے بھی تکبیرات عید کا 9 ہونا ثابت ہوتا ہے چھ زوائد اور تین تکبیرات نماز ( شرح نقایه ) حاصل یہ کہ احناف کے مذہب کی بنیاد عبداللہ بن مسعودؓ کے قول پر ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کے بیان کے مطابق ابن عباس نے فرمایا کہ پہلی رکعت میں تکبیر تحریمہ کہے اور پانچ تکبیر اس کے بعد کہے اور دوسری رکعت میں پانچ تکبیر کہے پھر قرأت کرے اور ایک روایت میں ہے کہ دوسری رکعت میں چار تکبیریں کہے۔
پس ابن مسعود اور ابن عباس کے قول کے درمیان دو جگہ اختلاف ہوا ایک تکبیرات زوائد کی تعداد میں دوم ان کے محل میں ۔ چنانچہ ابن مسعودؓ کے نزدیک تکبیر زوائد چھے ہیں۔ تین رکعت ادلی میں اور تین رکعت ثانیہ میں اور بن عباس کے نزدیک ایک روایت کے مطابق دس، از وائد تکبیریں ہیں پانچ رکعت اولی ۔۔ اور پانچ رکعت ثانیہ میں اور ایک روایت کے مطابق تکبیرات زوائد نو ہیں۔ پانچ رکعت ادلی میں اور چار رکعت ثانیہ میں دوسری بات کے بارے میں اختلاف یہ ہے کہ ابن مسعود کے نزدیک دوسری رکعت میں تکبیر زوائد کا محل قرآت سے فراغت کے بعد ہے اور ابن عباس کے نزدیک قرآت سے پہلے ہے۔ فاضل مصنف علامہ برہان الدین اپنے زمانہ کا حال بیان کرتے ہوئے لکھتے ہیں کہ آج کل عام لوگوں کا عمل حضرت ابن عباس کے قول پر ہے اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ وہ زمانہ خلفاء بنوعباس کے عروج کا زمانہ ہے۔ خلفاء بنوعباس تکبیرات عید کے سلسلہ میں اپنے جدا مسجد حضرت ابن عباس کے قول پر عمل کرنے کا امر کرتے تھے۔ یہی وجہ ہے
Method of Eid Prayer. And the imam leads the people in two rak'ahs. He says the opening takbir in the first rak'ah, then three (takbirs) after it, then recites al-Fatihah and a surah, then says a takbir and bows. Then he begins the second rak'ah with recitation, then says three takbirs after it, and says a fourth takbir and bows. This is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud, and it is our saying. Ibn 'Abbas said: He says the opening takbir in the first rak'ah and five after it, and in the second rak'ah he says five takbirs, then recites. In one narration, he says four. And today the common people act upon the saying of Ibn 'Abbas due to the command of the caliphs from his descendants. As for the madhhab, it is the first saying, because takbir and raising hands are contrary to the customary; so taking the lesser is preferable. Then the takbirs are from the symbols of the religion, so the principle in them is accumulation. In the first rak'ah, they must be attached to the opening takbir due to its strength in terms of obligatory nature and precedence. In the second rak'ah, only the bowing takbir is found, so they must be attached to it. Al-Shafi'i took the saying of Ibn 'Abbas, considering all the narrated (numbers) as extra, so the takbirs according to him become fifteen or sixteen. Translation: ... [then detailed Urdu commentary explaining the method, the narration from Ibn Mas'ud, the differences, and the reliance on Ibn Mas'ud's position]
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage discusses the manner of performing Eid prayer and the scholarly disagreement regarding the number and placement of extra takbirs. The Hanafi school, following Ibn Mas'ud, holds that there are nine takbirs in total: six extra takbirs (three in each rak'ah) plus the opening takbir and two bowing takbirs. The extra takbirs are said after the opening takbir in the first rak'ah and after recitation in the second rak'ah. The Shafi'i school, following Ibn 'Abbas, holds that there are more takbirs (fifteen or sixteen). The commentary explains the reasoning behind preferring Ibn Mas'ud's view: taking the lesser number is preferable since extra takbirs are a departure from the usual prayer practice, and the principle is to add minimally. It also notes that during the Abbasid period, the caliphs enforced Ibn 'Abbas's practice, leading to its adoption by the public, but the madhhab of the Hanafis remains the first opinion. The passage also includes a narration where Ibn Mas'ud taught the takbirs as nine, with five in the first rak'ah (including opening and bowing) and four in the second (including bowing).

Key Terms
تکبیرات زوائد (takbīrāt zawā'id): The extra takbirs recited in Eid prayer beyond the regular takbirs of prayer
الحاق (ilhāq): The attachment of extra takbirs to the primary takbir of each rak'ah (opening or bowing) for placement
اعلام الدین (a'lām al-dīn): Symbols or distinguishing features of the religion; the takbirs of Eid are considered such

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where are the extra takbirs placed in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer?
A) Before recitation, attached to the opening takbir of the second rak'ah
B) After recitation, attached to the bowing takbir
C) Between the opening takbir and recitation
D) After the bowing takbir

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school follows Ibn Mas'ud with 6 extra takbirs (3 per rak'ah) in Eid prayer, placed after the opening takbir in the first rak'ah and after recitation in the second, based on the principle of ilhāq and taking the lesser deviation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Number and Placement of Extra Takbirs in Eid Prayer
Explaining Hanafi ruling on extra takbirs with proof from Ibn Mas'ud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number and placement of extra takbirs in Eid prayer, cite the proof from Ibn Mas'ud, and compare it with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school follows Ibn Mas'ud: six extra takbirs (three per rak'ah), placed after the opening takbir in the first and after recitation in the second.

Eid prayer has extra takbirs that are sunnah muakkadah. But how many? And where are they placed? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, its proof from the companion Ibn Mas'ud, and why the school prefers this view over others, including how Abbasid political pressure created a historical detour from the original madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the extra takbirs (takbirat zawa'id) in Eid prayer. Their legal level is sunnah muakkadah – not wajib, but highly recommended. Omission does not invalidate the prayer.
Eid prayer itself is wajib, but the extra takbirs are sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (radiAllahu anhu), where he describes the practice: in the first rak'ah, four takbirs (including opening takbir) then recitation, then takbir for ruku'; in the second, recitation then four takbirs (including ruku' takbir).
The full text is given in the source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Ibn Mas'ud's statement 'takbir four times' in each rak'ah means: in the first, opening takbir + 3 extra = 4; in the second, 3 extra + ruku' takbir = 4. This yields 6 extra takbirs total. A second report explicitly says '9 takbirs' (the 6 extra + 3 original).
The Hanafi usul takes the literal meaning as definitive (dalalah qati'ah) for the count and placement.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Ibn 'Abbas reports different numbers (5 extra in each, or 5+4) and places the extra takbirs in the second rak'ah before recitation. Imam al-Shafi'i follows Ibn 'Abbas, leading to 12 or 13 extra takbirs (making total 15 or 16). Maliki and Hanbali schools have intermediary positions.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf among companions and schools.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah gives a rational argument: since extra takbirs are a deviation from normal prayer, the certain (lesser) number is preferred. The Hanafi school takes Ibn Mas'ud's view as the mufta bihi, even though Abu Yusuf and Muhammad acted on Ibn 'Abbas's view under Abbasid caliphs.
The tarjih authority is Al-Marghinani, and the authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

رکعتوں میں کل 4 تکبیریں ہیں، یہی علماء احناف کا مذہب ہے۔ ابن مسعود کا قول اس لئے ہے کہ روایت کیا گیا ہے کان ابن مسعود جالساً وعنده خذيفة وابو موسى الاشعرى فسالهم سعيد بن العاص عن التكبيرا فى صلوة العيد فقال حذيفة سل لاشعرى فقال الاشعرى سل عبدالله فانه اقدمنا واعلمنا فسأله فقال ابن مسعود يكبر اربعاً ثم يقرأ ثم يكبر فيركع ثم يقوم فى الثانيه فيقرأ ثم يكبر اربعاً بعد القراءة ليني ابن مسعود ، خذیفہ اور ابوموسی اشعری تشریف فرما تھے کہ ان سے سعید بن العاص نے نماز عید کی تکبیروں کے بارے میں دریافت کیا خذیفہ نے کہا اشعری سے پوچھو اشعری نے کہا کہ عبداللہ سے پوچھ لو اس لئے عبداللہ ہم میں قدیم العبد بھی ہیں اور صاحب علم بھی چنانچہ ابن مسعود سے دریافت کیا تو ابن مسعودؓ نے کہا کہ چار تکبیروں کے پھر قرآت کرے، پھر تکبیروں کہہ کر رکوع کرے۔ پھر دوسری رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو جائے اور قرآت کرے پھر قرآت کے بعد چار تکبیریں کہے پہلی رکعت میں جن چار تکبیروں کا ذکر کیا گیا ہے ان میں ایک تعبیر تحریمہ اور زمین زوائد ہیں اور دوسری رکعت میں چار تکبیروں میں سے ایک تکبیر ورکوع اور تین زوائد ہیں بہر حال بن مسعودؓ کے اس قول سے تکبیروں کا ثبوت ملتا ہے نیز سروق سے مروی ہے قال عبدالله بن مسعود يعلمنا التكبير في العيدين تسع تكبيرات خمس في الاولى واربع في الاخيرة ويوالى بين القراء تین یعنی ابن مسعود ہم کو عیدین میں 4 تکبیروں کی تعلیم دیتے تھے پانچ پہلی رکعت میں اور چار دوسری دکرت میں اور دونوں قراتوں کے درمیان وصل کرتے تھے۔ روایت میں پانچ تکبیروں سے مراد تکبیر تحریمہ تکبیر رکوع اور تین زوائد ہیں۔ اور چار سے مراد تین زوائد اور ایک تکبیر رکوع ہے۔ اس اثر سے بھی تکبیرات عید کا 9 ہونا ثابت ہوتا ہے چھ زوائد اور تین تکبیرات نماز ( شرح نقایه ) حاصل یہ کہ احناف کے مذہب کی بنیاد عبداللہ بن مسعودؓ کے قول پر ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کے بیان کے مطابق ابن عباس نے فرمایا کہ پہلی رکعت میں تکبیر تحریمہ کہے اور پانچ تکبیر اس کے بعد کہے اور دوسری رکعت میں پانچ تکبیر کہے پھر قرأت کرے اور ایک روایت میں ہے کہ دوسری رکعت میں چار تکبیریں کہے۔
پس ابن مسعود اور ابن عباس کے قول کے درمیان دو جگہ اختلاف ہوا ایک تکبیرات زوائد کی تعداد میں دوم ان کے محل میں ۔ چنانچہ ابن مسعودؓ کے نزدیک تکبیر زوائد چھے ہیں۔ تین رکعت ادلی میں اور تین رکعت ثانیہ میں اور بن عباس کے نزدیک ایک روایت کے مطابق دس، از وائد تکبیریں ہیں پانچ رکعت اولی ۔۔ اور پانچ رکعت ثانیہ میں اور ایک روایت کے مطابق تکبیرات زوائد نو ہیں۔ پانچ رکعت ادلی میں اور چار رکعت ثانیہ میں دوسری بات کے بارے میں اختلاف یہ ہے کہ ابن مسعود کے نزدیک دوسری رکعت میں تکبیر زوائد کا محل قرآت سے فراغت کے بعد ہے اور ابن عباس کے نزدیک قرآت سے پہلے ہے۔ فاضل مصنف علامہ برہان الدین اپنے زمانہ کا حال بیان کرتے ہوئے لکھتے ہیں کہ آج کل عام لوگوں کا عمل حضرت ابن عباس کے قول پر ہے اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ وہ زمانہ خلفاء بنوعباس کے عروج کا زمانہ ہے۔ خلفاء بنوعباس تکبیرات عید کے سلسلہ میں اپنے جدا مسجد حضرت ابن عباس کے قول پر عمل کرنے کا امر کرتے تھے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ ایک بار حضرت امام ابو یوسف نے بغداد میں لوگوں کو عید کی نماز پڑھائی اور تکبیروں کے سلسلہ میں ابن عباس کے قول پر عمل کیا۔ کیونکہ خلیفہ ہارون رشید عباس آپ کا مقتدی تھا اس نے آپ کو اس کا حکم کیا تھا اسی طرح امام محمد سے ابن عباس کے قول پر عمل کرنا مروی ہے لیکن یہ عمل مذہب اور اعتقاد ا نہیں تھا بلکہ خلفاء بنو عباس کے حکم کے پیش نظر تھا ورنہ مذہب قول اول یعنی عبداللہ بن مسعودؓ کا قول ہی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے قول اول کے مذہب ہونے کی عقلی دلیل یہ پیش کی ہے کہ تکبیر اور ہاتھوں کا اٹھانا مجموعہ من حیث المجموعہ نمازوں کے اندر خلاف معہود ہے۔ اس لئے اقل کو اختیار کرنا اولی اور افضل ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ اقل اور منتر کا ثبوت بالیقین ہوتا ہے۔ ثم التكبيرات الخ سے تکبیرات زوائد کے محل وقوع پر بالدلیل کلام کیا گیا ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ تکبیرات دین کے اعلام اور علامتوں سے ہیں حتی کہ ان میں جہر کیا جاتا ہے تا کہ دین کا جھنڈا بلند ہو اور ان تکبیرات زوائد میں اصل یہ ہے کہ اصلی تکبیرات کے ساتھ مجتمع ہوں پس رکعت اولیٰ میں تکبیرات زوائد کو تکبیر تحریمہ کے ساتھ لاحق کیا گیا ہے اور تکبیر رکوع کے ساتھ لاحق نہیں کیا گیا، کیونکہ تکبیر تحریمہ فرض ہونے کی وجہ سے قوی بھی ہے اور تکبیر رکوع سے مقدم بھی اور چونکہ دوسری رکعت میں تکبیر رکوع کے سوا کوئی تکبیر نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے دوسری رکعت میں تکبیر رکوع کے ساتھ لاحق کرنا واجب ہو گیا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ امام شافعی نے حضرت ابن عباس کے قول کو اختیار کیا ہے اور ابن عباس کے قول میں تکبیرات کی جو تعداد روایت کی گئی ہے ان کو زوائد پر محمول کیا ہے اس طرح امام شافعی کے نزدیک تکبیرات کل پندرہ ہوں گی یا سولہ ہوں گی۔ مصنف کی عبارت الا انہ جمل المروی کلہ علی الزوائد میں قدرے اشتباہ ہے وہ یہ کہ المروی سے مراد یا تو وہ ہے جو ہدایہ میں ان الفاظ کے ساتھ مروی ہے و قال ابن عباس يكبرافى الاولى للافتتاح وخمساه بعد ها و فى الثانيه يكبر خمسا ثم يقرأ وفي رواية يكبرا ربعا اور یا اس کے علاوہ مراد ہے اگر ثانی ہے تو کلام میں تعقید ہوگی کیونکہ جو چیز کتاب میں مذکور نہیں ہے اس کا حوالہ دے کر خواہ مخواہ قارئین کو پریشان کیا گیا ہے اور اگر اول ہے تو تکبیرات اس مقدار کو نہیں پہنچتیں۔ کیونکہ مذکورہ روایت کے مطابق زوائد نو ہیں یا دس ہیں۔ اور تین اصلی تکبیروں ( تکبیر تحریمہ رکعت ادلی کے رکوع کی تکبیر اور رکعت ثانیہ کے رکوع کی تکبیر ) کے ساتھ مل کر بارہ ہوں گی یا تیرہ ہوں گی۔
نیز صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے وظهر عمل العامة اليوم بقول ابن عباس مچھر کہا والشافعی اخذ بقول ابن عباس یہ عبارت تقاضا کرتی ہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ کے زمانے میں عام لوگوں کا عمل پندرہ تکبیروں پر تھا یا سولہ پر حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ اس زمانے میں تیرہ تکبیروں پر یا بارہ تکبیروں پر عمل تھا اس شبہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ابن عباس سے دور وایتیں ہیں۔ ایک تو یہ کہ عیدین میں بارہ تکبیریں ہیں۔ دوم یہ کہ تیرہ تکبیریں ہیں۔ امام مالک اور امام احمد نے کہا کہ بارہ یا تیرہ اصلی تین تکبیروں کے ساتھ مل کر ہیں یعنی تکبیر تحریمہ اور دونوں رکعتوں کی تکبیر رکوع کے ساتھ مل کر بارہ یا تیرہ ہیں۔ بایں طور کہ پہلی اور دوسری رکعت میں پانچ پانچ تکبیریں زائد اور تکبیر تحریمہ اور دونوں رکعتوں کے رکوع کی دو تکبیر میں اس طرح کل تکبیریں تیرہ ہوئیں اور دوسری روایت کے مطابق پہلی رکعت میں پانچ زوائد اور دوسری رکعت میں چار زوائد اور تین اصلی تکبیریں، تو اب کل تکبیریں بارہ ہوں گی ۔ ابن عباس کی انہیں روایات پر اس زمانہ میں عام لوگوں کا عمل تھا۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ یہ بارہ یا تیرہ تمام کی تمام زائد تکبیر میں ہیں اب ظاہر ہے کہ جب ان کے ساتھ تین اصلی تکبیر میں یعنی تکبیر تحریمہ اور دونوں رکعتوں کے رکوع کی دو تکبیریں ملیں گی تو بارہ تکبیر والی روایت کی صورت میں کل
Chapter of the Two Eids. Ashraf al-Hidayah commentary on al-Hidayah Volume 2: Sahib al-Quduri described the manner of Eid prayer: The Imam leads people in two rak'ahs as follows: first say the opening takbir, then recite Thana', then say three extra takbirs, then recite al-Fatihah and a surah, then say the bending takbir and bow, then prostrate. Thus the first rak'ah is completed. In the second rak'ah, first recite al-Fatihah and a surah, then say three extra takbirs, then say the bending takbir and bow. According to this description, there are nine takbirs in the two rak'ahs: six extra, two bending takbirs, and one opening takbir. Sahib al-Hidayah says: This is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud. Thus according to Ibn Mas'ud, there are nine takbirs in the two rak'ahs of Eid. This is the madhhab of the Hanafi scholars. The saying of Ibn Mas'ud is based on the narration: 'Ibn Mas'ud was sitting with Hudhayfah and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari. Sa'id ibn al-'As asked them about the takbirs in Eid prayer. Hudhayfah said: Ask al-Ash'ari. Al-Ash'ari said: Ask 'Abdullah, for he is the oldest among us and the most knowledgeable. So he asked him. Ibn Mas'ud said: He says takbir four times, then recites, then says takbir and bows, then stands for the second (rak'ah), recites, then says takbir four times after the recitation.' This is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud... Also from Sufyan: 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud taught us the takbirs in the two Eids: nine takbirs: five in the first and four in the last, and he joined between the recitations.' In this narration, five takbirs means the opening takbir, the bending takbir, and three extra. And four means three extra and one bending takbir. This report also proves that the takbirs of Eid are nine: six extra and three takbirs of the prayer. Conclusion: The foundation of the Hanafi madhhab is on the saying of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. According to the statement of Sahib al-Hidayah, Ibn 'Abbas said: In the first rak'ah, say the opening takbir and then five takbirs after it, and in the second rak'ah, say five takbirs, then recite. And in one narration, in the second rak'ah, say four takbirs. So between Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn 'Abbas there is difference in two matters: one in the number of extra takbirs, and second in their place. For Ibn Mas'ud, extra takbirs are six: three in first rak'ah, three in second. For Ibn 'Abbas, in one narration, extra takbirs are ten: five in first and five in second; in another narration, extra takbirs are nine: five in first and four in second. The second difference is regarding the placement: For Ibn Mas'ud, in the second rak'ah, the extra takbirs come after recitation; for Ibn 'Abbas, before recitation. The author, 'Allamah Burhan al-Din, writes about the situation of his time: Now the common practice is on the saying of Ibn 'Abbas, and the reason is that it was the era of the Abbasid caliphs. The Abbasid caliphs used to order acting on the saying of their ancestor Ibn 'Abbas regarding the takbirs of Eid. For this reason, once Imam Abu Yusuf led the people in Eid prayer in Baghdad and acted on the saying of Ibn 'Abbas regarding the takbirs, because Caliph Harun al-Rashid was his follower and ordered him to do so. Similarly, it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that he acted on the saying of Ibn 'Abbas. But this action was not according to the madhhab and belief; rather, it was due to the order of the Abbasid caliphs. Otherwise, the madhhab is the first saying, i.e., the saying of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. Sahib al-Hidayah gave a rational proof for the first saying being the madhhab: that raising hands along with takbir is contrary to the usual practice in prayers, so choosing the lesser is preferable and better, because the proof of the lesser is certain. Then regarding the placement of extra takbirs, it is said that takbirs are among the symbols and signs of the religion, so much so that one raises one's voice in them so that the banner of the religion may be raised. The principle for these extra takbirs is that they be combined with the original takbirs. So in the first rak'ah, the extra takbirs are attached to the opening takbir and not to the bending takbir, because the opening takbir is stronger due to being obligatory and is ahead of the bending takbir. And since in the second rak'ah there is no other takbir besides the bending takbir, it became necessary to attach them to the bending takbir. Sahib al-Hidayah said that Imam al-Shafi'i adopted the saying of Ibn 'Abbas, and he considered the number of takbirs narrated from Ibn 'Abbas to be all extra. Thus according to al-Shafi'i, the total takbirs would be fifteen or sixteen. The author's phrase 'except that he included all that is narrated as extra' has some confusion: what is meant by 'that which is narrated' is either what is narrated in al-Hidayah with these words 'Ibn 'Abbas said: he says takbir in the first for opening and five after it, and in the second he says five takbirs then recites, and in a narration he says four takbirs' or something else. If the latter, then there is complication because referencing something not mentioned in the book unnecessarily confuses readers. If the former, then the takbirs do not reach that number, because according to the mentioned narration, the extra are nine or ten, and with the three original takbirs (opening takbir, bending takbir of first rak'ah, bending takbir of second rak'ah) combined, they would be twelve or thirteen. Also, Sahib al-Hidayah said: 'And it appears that the common practice today is on the saying of Ibn 'Abbas' and 'al-Shafi'i adopted the saying of Ibn 'Abbas'. This statement implies that in Sahib al-Hidayah's time, the common practice was on fifteen or sixteen takbirs, but that is not the case; rather, at that time practice was on thirteen or twelve takbirs. The answer to this doubt is that there are two narrations from Ibn 'Abbas: one that there are twelve takbirs in the two Eids, and second that there are thirteen. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad said that twelve or thirteen include the three original takbirs, i.e., combined with the opening takbir and the bending takbirs of both rak'ahs, they are twelve or thirteen. In this way, the first narration: five extra takbirs in the first and five in the second, plus opening takbir and two bending takbirs totals thirteen. The other narration: five extra in first, four extra in second, plus three original takbirs totals twelve. In Sahib al-Hidayah's time, the common practice was on these narrations of Ibn 'Abbas. Imam al-Shafi'i said that these twelve or thirteen are all extra takbirs. Obviously, when the three original takbirs (opening takbir and the two bending takbirs) are added, then in the case of the twelve-takbir narration, the total becomes ...
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the number and placement of extra takbirs (takbirat zawa'id) in the two Eid prayers. The author begins by stating the Hanafi position based on the practice of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (radiAllahu anhu). According to the Hanafi madhhab, the total takbirs in the two rak'ahs of Eid prayer are nine: the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah), the bending takbir (takbir ruku') for each rak'ah (two total), and six extra takbirs (three in the first rak'ah after the opening takbir, three in the second rak'ah after recitation). The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud where he instructed that in the first rak'ah one says four takbirs (including opening takbir and then three extra, then recites, then takbir for ruku'), and in the second rak'ah one recites first, then says four takbirs (three extra and one for ruku'). A second report explicitly states nine takbirs total. The author then contrasts the view of Ibn 'Abbas (radiAllahu anhu), which has two narrations: one with five extra takbirs in each rak'ah (total ten extra, plus three original = thirteen), another with five in first and four in second (total nine extra, plus three = twelve). The difference is both in count and in placement: Ibn 'Abbas places the extra takbirs in the second rak'ah before recitation, whereas Ibn Mas'ud places them after recitation. The author explains that during the Abbasid caliphate, due to political pressure, the common practice shifted to Ibn 'Abbas's view, and even Imams Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani acted accordingly when leading the caliph in prayer, but this was not their personal madhhab. The actual Hanafi madhhab remains that of Ibn Mas'ud. A rational argument is given: since adding extra takbirs is a deviation from the norm of regular prayers, the minimum number (which is certain) should be chosen; hence six extra (three per rak'ah) is preferred over more. The author also critiques the claim that Shafi'i's view leads to 15 or 16 total takbirs, clarifying that the narrations from Ibn 'Abbas yield only 12 or 13 if properly understood, and that Shafi'i considered all those as extra, which would then add the three original takbirs to reach 15 or 16. The passage concludes with the author resolving a potential confusion about the text of al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
تكبيرات زوائد (takbirāt zawā'id): The extra takbirs recited in Eid prayer beyond the regular takbirs of the prayer (opening and bending takbirs).
تكبير تحريمه (takbīr al-taḥrīmah): The opening takbir that enters one into the state of prayer; it is a fard (obligatory) pillar.
تکبیر رکوع (takbīr al-rukū'): The takbir said when going into bowing posture; it is wajib according to Hanafi school (neither fard nor sunnah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, how many extra takbirs (takbirat zawa'id) are there in the two rak'ahs of Eid prayer?
A) 6 (three per rak'ah)
B) 9 (five in the first, four in the second)
C) 10 (five per rak'ah)
D) 12 (seven in the first, five in the second)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab, based on Ibn Mas'ud, prescribes six extra takbirs (three per rak'ah) in Eid prayer, with placement after the opening takbir in the first rak'ah and after recitation in the second.

Salah — Prayer

Number of Takbirat in Eid Prayer: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Explaining Hanafi position on takbirat and refuting Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of takbirat in Eid prayer, explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) behind it, and compare it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
The Hanafi school prefers the lesser number of takbirat because certainty lies with the lesser, and it is based on the authority of Ibn Mas'ud.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key point of difference between the schools: how many additional takbirat (takbirat zawa'id) are recited in the Eid prayer. The Hanafi school holds that there are six additional takbirat (three per rak'ah), while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that there are twelve or thirteen additional, leading to totals of fifteen or sixteen. The passage presents the Hanafi rational proof and clarifies the interpretation of narrations from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Mas'ud.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its basis
Identify the exact number: 6 additional takbirat (3 in each rak'ah) apart from the 3 original takbir (takbirat al-ihram and two takbir of bowing), total 9. The primary evidence is the saying (qawl) of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (RA).
The Hanafi school considers qawl sahabi as a binding source in the absence of contradictory hadith.
2
Understand the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The text argues that takbir and raising hands are contrary to the usual practice in prayer. Therefore, adopting the lesser number is better and more virtuous, because the proof of the lesser number is certain.
This is a rational preference for what is established with certainty over what is doubtful.
3
Examine the Shafi'i position and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i adopts narrations from Ibn Abbas: one with 12 takbir, another with 13. He interprets all these as additional (zawa'id), excluding the three original takbir, leading to totals of 15 or 16.
The difference hinges on whether the original takbir are included in the numbers narrated from Ibn Abbas.
4
Resolve the ambiguity in the Hidayah text
The author's phrase 'al-marwi' is ambiguous. The clarification is that 'al-marwi' refers to what is narrated from Ibn Abbas in general, not limited to what is cited in Hidayah. The two narrations (12 and 13) cause the confusion about the number in the author's time.
Common practice in the author's time was upon the two narrations from Ibn Abbas at 12 or 13 total (including originals), not 15 or 16.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis recite 3 additional takbir in each rak'ah; Shafi'is recite 6 or 7 in the first and 5 or 6 in the second; Malikis/Hanbalis recite 5 in the first and 4 or 5 in the second (including original takbir).
This affects the actual number of takbir recited in congregations led by different imams.

مذہب کی بنیاد ابن عباس کی دونوں روایتوں (بارہ نبرد والی ) پر ہے لیکن وہ ان تمام کو زائد قرار دیتے ہیں۔ اصلی تین ان کے علاہ ہیں ۔ واللہ اعلم
Chapter of the Two Eids. 320. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume two: That once Imam Abu Yusuf led the Eid prayer for the people in Baghdad and acted upon the saying of Ibn Abbas regarding the takbirat. Because Caliph Harun al-Rashid al-Abbasi was his follower and he had ordered him to do so. Similarly, it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that he acted upon the saying of Ibn Abbas. But this action was not according to the madhhab and belief; rather it was due to the order of the Abbasid caliphs. Otherwise, the madhhab is the first saying, i.e., the saying of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (RA). The author of Hidayah presented a rational proof for the first saying being the madhhab: that the takbir and raising of hands, as a whole, is contrary to the usual practice in prayers. Therefore, adopting the lesser (number) is better and more virtuous, because the proof of the lesser (number) is certain. Then (the text says) 'thumma al-takbirat...' etc., discussing the placement of the additional takbirat with proof. Thus he said: Takbirat are from the symbols and signs of the religion, to the extent that they are recited aloud so that the flag of religion is raised. And the principle regarding these additional takbirat is that they are attached to the original takbirat. So in the first rak'ah, the additional takbirat are attached to the takbirat al-ihram, not to the takbir of bowing, because the takbirat al-ihram is stronger due to being fard and precedes the takbir of bowing. And since in the second rak'ah there is no takbir except the takbir of bowing, it became wajib to attach it to the takbir of bowing. The author of Hidayah said that Imam al-Shafi'i chose the saying of Ibn Abbas, and he interpreted the number of takbirat narrated from Ibn Abbas as all additional. Thus according to Imam al-Shafi'i, the total takbirat would be fifteen or sixteen. In the author's phrase 'illa annahu jamala al-marwi kullahu ala al-zawaid' there is some ambiguity: that is, by 'al-marwi' is meant either that which is narrated in the Hidayah with these words: 'wa qala Ibn Abbas: yukabbiru fi al-ula li al-iftitah wa khamsan ba'daha, wa fi al-thaniyati yukabbiru khamsan thumma yaqra'u, wa fi riwayatin yukabbiru arba'an', or something else. If it is the latter, then there is confusion in the speech, because by referencing something not mentioned in the book, the readers are unnecessarily troubled. And if it is the former, then the takbirat do not reach that number, because according to the mentioned narration, the additional (takbirat) are nine or ten. And together with the three original takbirat (takbirat al-ihram, takbir of bowing in first rak'ah, and takbir of bowing in second rak'ah), they would be twelve or thirteen. Also, the author of Hidayah said: 'wa zahara amalu al-'ammati al-yawma bi qawli Ibn Abbas' – the phrase 'machhar kaha wa al-Shafi'i akhadha bi qawli Ibn Abbas' implies that in the time of the author of Hidayah, the practice of the common people was upon fifteen or sixteen takbirat, whereas this is not so; rather at that time, the practice was upon thirteen or twelve takbirat. The answer to this doubt is that there are two narrations from Ibn Abbas: one that in the two Eids there are twelve takbirat, and the other that there are thirteen. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad said that twelve or thirteen are together with the three original takbirat, i.e., takbirat al-ihram and the two takbirat of bowing in the two rak'ahs, making twelve or thirteen. In this way: in the first and second rak'ah, five additional takbirat each, plus takbirat al-ihram and the two takbirat of bowing in both rak'ahs, thus total thirteen. And according to the second narration: in the first rak'ah five additional, in the second rak'ah four additional, plus three original takbirat, so total twelve. The common people in that time acted upon these narrations of Ibn Abbas. Imam al-Shafi'i said that these twelve or thirteen are all additional takbirat. Now it is obvious that when three original takbirat (takbirat al-ihram and two takbirat of bowing of the two rak'ahs) are added to them, in the case of the twelve-takbir narration the total would be fifteen, and in the case of the thirteen-takbir narration the total would be sixteen. So by 'al-marwi' is meant what is narrated from Ibn Abbas. Thus the conclusion is: according to the Hanafis, in both rak'ahs of Eid, the additional takbirat are six. According to Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad, they are six [should be 'twelve or thirteen'?]. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, they are twelve or thirteen. (Sharh Niqayah). The basis of the Hanafi madhhab is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud (RA). The basis of the madhhab of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad is the narration of thirteen takbirat from Ibn Abbas. In this way, the day of Monday the takbir are additional, and three are original. The basis of Imam al-Shafi'i's madhhab is both narrations from Ibn Abbas (the twelve and thirteen ones), but he considers all of them as additional, excluding the three original ones. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of takbirat in the Eid prayer. The author begins with a historical anecdote about Imam Abu Yusuf acting upon the view of Ibn Abbas due to caliphal order, affirming that the true Hanafi madhhab is based on the saying of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. A rational proof (dalil aqli) is presented: since takbir and hand-raising deviate from normal prayer practice, the lesser number (which is certain) is preferred. The text then discusses the placement of additional takbirat: in the first rak'ah they attach to takbirat al-ihram (stronger, fard), in the second rak'ah to the takbir of bowing (since no other takbir exists). The Shafi'i position is explained: they adopt Ibn Abbas's narrations and consider all takbirat as additional, leading to totals of 15 or 16. A confusion in the Hidayah text is resolved by distinguishing between what is explicitly narrated in the Hidayah and the narrations of Ibn Abbas. The conclusion contrasts the Hanafi (6 additional, 3 original = 9 total), Maliki/Hanbali (12 or 13 total including originals), and Shafi'i (15 or 16 total, all additional) positions.

Key Terms
تکبیرات زوائد (takbirat zawa'id): The additional takbirat recited in Eid prayer beyond the fundamental takbirat (takbirat al-ihram and takbir of bowing).
قول ابن مسعود (qawl Ibn Mas'ud): The legal opinion of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (RA) that Eid prayer has six additional takbirat, which is the basis of the Hanafi position.
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbirat al-ihram): The opening takbir of the prayer that initiates the state of ihram (consecration).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, how many additional takbirat (takbirat zawa'id) are said in the Eid prayer?
A) Three
B) Six
C) Twelve
D) Fifteen

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab definitively holds that the Eid prayer includes six additional takbirat, with the placement determined by the strength of the original takbir in each rak'ah.

Raising Hands in Eid Takbirat: The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Ruling on raf' yadayn in Eid takbirat with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on raising hands (raf' yadayn) in the extra takbirat of Eid prayer and identify the evidence used by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Hands are raised in Eid takbirat except the takbir of bowing, despite Abu Yusuf's dissent, based on the Prophet's hadith of seven occasions.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific difference within the Hanafi school regarding whether the hands should be raised during the additional takbirat of Eid prayer. While the dominant view (Abu Hanifa, supported by Muhammad al-Shaybani) holds that hands are raised based on a hadith enumerating seven occasions, Imam Abu Yusuf argues by analogy to the takbir of bowing. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the rationale behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling of the matn
Al-Quduri says the worshipper raises his hands in all Eid takbirat except the takbir of bowing. This is the starting point of the dispute.
The exception of takbir al-ruku' is significant because it becomes the basis of Abu Yusuf's analogy.
2
Identify the evidence for Abu Hanifa's view
The hadith 'لا ترفع الأيدي إلا في سبع مواطن' (Hands are not raised except in seven places) explicitly mentions 'تكبيرات العيدين' (Eid takbirat). This is the primary textual evidence (dalil naqli).
The hadith is khabar ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, but it is accepted by the Hanafi school in this context.
3
State Abu Yusuf's opposing view and his proof
Abu Yusuf holds that hands should not be raised in the extra takbirat. His proof is qiyas (analogy): just as hands are not raised in the takbir of bowing (because it is not an opening takbir), so too the extra takbirat are not openings and thus do not warrant hand-raising.
This analogy relies on the common element of 'not being the opening of the prayer'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The text argues that the hadith is a specific textual evidence that overrides the analogy. Since the hadith explicitly includes Eid takbirat, it takes precedence over qiyas. This is consistent with Hanafi usul: a specific textual proof (nass) prevails over general analogy.
The response does not dismiss Abu Yusuf's analogy as invalid, but rather prioritizes the explicit text.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference (thamarah) is whether the worshipper raises their hands during the extra takbirat. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that hands are raised, following Abu Hanifa. This is the view taken by the majority of later Hanafi scholars.
The text explicitly calls the hadith 'حجة' (proof) against Abu Yusuf, indicating tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويرفع يديه في تكبيرات العيدين يريد به ماسوى التكبير فى الركوع لقوله صلى لا ترفع الايدى لا في سبع مواطن وذكر من جملتها تكبيرات الاعياد وعن ابى يوسف انه لا يرفع والحجة عليه ماروينا رجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ عیدین کی تکبیروں میں اپنے دونوں ہاتھ اٹھائے اس سے مراد تکبیر رکوع کے علاوہ ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہاتھ نہ اٹھائے جائیں مگر سات جگہوں میں منجملہ ان میں سے عیدین کی تکبیروں کا ذکر کیا ہے اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ اتھ نہ اٹھائے جائیں اور امام ابو یوسف پر حجت وہ حدیث ہے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے۔ فریح ہمارے نزدیک تکبیرات عیدین میں کانوں تک ہاتھ اٹھائے جائیں گے یہی امام شافعی اور امام احمد کا مذہب ہے۔ دلیل انحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول لا ترفع الايدى الا فی سبع مواطن ہے۔ ان سات جگہوں میں عیدین کی تکبیرات زوائد بھی ہیں۔ امام یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ تکبیرات عیدین میں ہاتھ نہ اٹھائے جائیں۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہاتھوں کا اٹھانا افتتاح کی سنت ہے چونکہ تکبیرات زوائد میں افتتاح صلوۃ نہیں اس لئے رفع یدین بھی نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ رکوع کی تکبیر کے اندر رفع یدین نہیں ہے امام ابو ہف کے خلاف حدیث لا ترفع الابدی حجت ہوگی
He (al-Quduri) said: And he raises his hands in the takbirat of the two Eids, meaning other than the takbir of bowing, because of his (the Prophet's) saying: 'Hands are not raised except in seven places' and he mentioned among them the takbirat of the Eid festivals. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he does not raise (his hands). And the proof against him is what we have narrated. (The commentary says:) Al-Quduri said: In the takbirat of the two Eids, one should raise both his hands, meaning except the takbir of bowing, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Hands are not raised except in seven places' and among them he mentioned the takbirat of the Eids. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that hands should not be raised. And the argument against Abu Yusuf is the hadith that we have narrated. (Then:) The resolution: According to us, in the takbirat of the two Eids, the hands should be raised up to the ears. This is also the madhhab of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad. The proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Hands are not raised except in seven places.' Among those seven places are the additional takbirat of the two Eids. It is narrated from Imam Yusuf (Abu Yusuf) that hands should not be raised in the takbirat of the two Eids. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that raising the hands is a sunnah of the opening takbir; since the additional takbirat do not involve the opening of the prayer, there should be no raising of hands, just as there is no raising of hands in the takbir of bowing. Against Imam Abu Hanifa, the hadith 'Hands are not raised except in seven places' would be a decisive argument.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding raising hands (raf' yadayn) in the extra takbirat of Eid prayer. The base text (from al-Quduri) states that hands are raised in all Eid takbirat except the takbir of bowing, based on a hadith that mentions seven occasions for hand-raising, which include Eid takbirat. However, a contrary view is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf, who argues that raising hands is a sunnah specifically for the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram); since the additional takbirat are not opening the prayer, they do not warrant hand-raising, analogous to the takbir of bowing. The commentary favors the view attributed to Abu Hanifa (and also held by Shafi'i and Ahmad) that hands are raised, citing the hadith as evidence.

Key Terms
رفع یدین (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands to the ears during takbir, specifically here in the extra takbirat of Eid prayer.
تکبیر رکوع (takbir al-ruku'): The takbir said when moving into bowing position in prayer; used here as an analogy to argue against hand-raising.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hands are not raised at all
B) Hands are raised in all takbirat except the takbir of bowing
C) Hands are raised only in the first takbir of each rak'ah
D) Hands are raised only by the Imam, not the followers

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is to raise both hands in all Eid takbirat except the takbir of bowing, based on a hadith listing seven occasions for hand-raising.

The Pause Between Eid Prayer Takbirat
Ruling on the recommended silence between additional takbirat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the recommended pause between additional takbirat in Eid prayer and explain the practical rationale.

Core Idea
A brief silence between each extra takbir in Eid prayer removes confusion in large congregations.

This passage addresses a practical aspect of the Eid prayer: what to do between the extra takbirat. Imam Abu Hanifa provides clear guidance on the recommended interval, based on the need for clarity in a large gathering. This lesson clarifies both the ruling and its wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act in question
Recognize that the passage discusses the pause (sukut) between each additional takbir in Eid prayer.
The additional takbirat are the extra 'Allahu Akbar' statements in the first two rak'ahs of Eid prayer.
2
State the ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa
Imam Abu Hanifa ruled that one should pause silently for the duration of saying 'Subhanallah' three times (three tasbihat) between each takbir.
This is a sunnah, not wajib.
3
Understand the rationale (hikmah)
The pause prevents confusion among distant worshippers who might lose count of the takbirat if said rapidly.
The 'illa (cause) is the large congregation (jam' ghafir).
4
Note the absence of prescribed dhikr
The text specifies silence, not any specific remembrance. The pause itself is the sunnah.
Contrast with the Shafi'i school which recommends reciting tasbih or tahmid during the pause.
5
Contrast with other schools
Other schools may not prescribe a pause or prescribe dhikr instead. Recognize the Hanafi specificity.
This ikhtilaf is based on different interpretations of the practice of the Prophet and the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رہی یہ بات کہ تکبیرات زوائد کے درمیان کوئی مسنون ذکر ہے یا نہیں ہے۔ امام ابو نیفہ سے مروی ہے کہ ہر دو تکبیروں کے درمیان تین تسبیحات کی مقدار سکوت کرے۔ کیونکہ عید کی نماز جم غفیر کے ساتھ ادا کی جاتی ہے اگر نبیرات کے درمیان موالات اور وصل کیا گیا تو جولوگ امام سے دور ہوں گے ان پر امام کا حال مشتبہ ہو جائے گا کہ امام کون کی تکبیر کہہ رہا ہے البتہ اتنی مقدار ٹھہرنے سے اشتباہ دور ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے تکبیرات کے درمیان تین تسبیحات کی مقدار خاموش رہنے کا حکم دیا گیا ہے۔
As for the issue whether there is any prescribed sunnah dhikr between the additional takbirat or not: It is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that between every two takbirat one should remain silent for the duration of three tasbihat (saying Subhanallah). Because the Eid prayer is performed with a large congregation; if the takbirat are performed in quick succession (muwalat) and connected, then those who are far from the Imam will be confused about which takbir the Imam is saying. However, by pausing for that amount, the confusion is removed. Therefore, the ruling is to remain silent between the takbirat for the duration of three tasbihat.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the interval between the additional takbirat in Eid prayer. It is recommended (mustahabb or sunnah) to pause between each takbir for a duration of saying 'Subhanallah' three times. The reason ('illa) is practical: in a large congregation, if the takbirat are said rapidly one after another, people at the back may lose count or become uncertain which takbir the Imam is reciting. This pause eliminates confusion. The text does not mention any dhikr during the pause, only silence.

Key Terms
سکوت (sukut): Silence; specifically, the pause between additional takbirat in Eid prayer for the duration of three tasbihat.
تسبیحات (tasbihat): The phrase 'Subhanallah'; here used as a measure of time (duration of saying it three times).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Imam Abu Hanifa prescribe to do between each additional takbir in Eid prayer?
A) Recite Surah al-Fatihah
B) Pause silently for the duration of three tasbihat
C) Raise the hands and say Allahu Akbar again
D) Make a prostration

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a silent pause of three tasbihat between each additional takbir in Eid prayer is a recommended sunnah, rooted in the practical need to maintain order in large congregations.

The Timing and Content of the Eid Khutbah
Ruling on the timing and content of Eid khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that the Eid khutbah is delivered after the prayer, identify the proof (naql mustafidh), and explain why its content focuses on Sadaqat al-Fitr.

Core Idea
The Eid khutbah is after prayer, unlike Jumu'ah, and its purpose is to teach about Sadaqat al-Fitr.

Many assume all congregational khutbahs follow the same pattern, but the Hanafi school distinguishes clearly between Jumu'ah and Eid. The source passage establishes the timing and content of the Eid khutbah based on widespread practice, not just a single hadith. Let us examine the proof and the rationale behind the content requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the delivery of the Eid khutbah. According to the Hanafi madhhab, it is a sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah), not a fard. It consists of two khutbahs with a sitting in between.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is naql mustafidh – a widespread transmission that is nearly mutawatir in strength. The text states that the practice of delivering the khutbah after prayer has been transmitted widely from the Prophet and the Companions.
Hanafi usul classifies mustafidh as stronger than ahad, providing near-certainty.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The mustafidh transmission establishes two facts: (1) The khutbah is given after the prayer, not before. (2) There are two khutbahs. The content – teaching about Sadaqat al-Fitr – is derived from the purpose of the legislation: because the khutbah was prescribed specifically for that end.
4
Contrast with Jumu'ah
Unlike Jumu'ah, where the khutbah precedes the prayer, the Eid khutbah follows the prayer. This distinction is based on the same widespread practice.
Some early scholars (like Imam Malik) disagreed, but the Hanafi position is based on strong transmission.
5
Apply the content requirement
The khutbah must include a portion dedicated to teaching the rulings of Sadaqat al-Fitr. This is not an exhaustive requirement but reflects the wisdom behind the legislation.
Modern application: imams today should still prioritize zakat al-fitr education during Eid khutbah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نماز کے بعد عیدین کے خطبے دیئے جائیں قال ويخطب بعد الصلاة خطبتين بذلك ورد النقل المستفيض يعلم الناس فيها صدقة الفطر واحكامها لانها شرعت لا جله زمہ کہا کہ نماز عید کے بعد امام دو خطبہ پڑھے اسی پر نقل جو شائع ہے دار ہوئی خطبہ عید میں لوگوں کو صدقہ فطر اور اس کے احکام سکھلائے کیونکہ خطبہ اسی وجہ سے مشروع کیا گیا ہے۔
The khutbah of the two Eids should be delivered after the prayer. He (al-Quduri) said: And he (the Imam) delivers two khutbahs after the prayer. Upon this the widely transmitted (mustafidh) narration has come. In it he teaches people about Sadaqat al-Fitr and its rulings, because the khutbah was legislated for that purpose. (Commentary:) The author (of Hidayah) said: After the Eid prayer, the Imam should deliver two khutbahs. The transmission that has become widespread is upon this. In the Eid khutbah, he should teach the people about Sadaqat al-Fitr and its rulings, because the khutbah was legislated for that reason.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling regarding the timing and content of the Eid khutbah. It is established by widespread transmission (naql mustafidh) that the Eid khutbah is delivered after the prayer, unlike the Friday khutbah which precedes the prayer. The khutbah consists of two parts (two khutbahs with a sitting in between). The purpose of the khutbah is to teach the congregation about Sadaqat al-Fitr (the obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan) and its rulings, as this was the reason for which the Eid khutbah was prescribed. The text implies the khutbah is not a place for general exhortation only but specifically for educating about fitrah.

Key Terms
نقل مستفیض (naql mustafidh): A transmission that is widespread but not reaching the level of mutawatir; considered strong evidence in Hanafi usul.
صدقہ فطر (sadaqat al-fitr): The obligatory charity paid at the end of Ramadan, which the Eid khutbah is meant to teach about.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is the Eid khutbah delivered?
A) Before the Eid prayer
B) After the Eid prayer
C) Both before and after
D) It is not prescribed

Key Takeaway
The Eid khutbah is a sunnah muakkadah delivered after the prayer in two parts, primarily to teach about Sadaqat al-Fitr.

Number of Extra Takbirs in Eid Prayer: Hanafi vs Other Madhhabs
Compares extra takbirs across four madhhabs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of extra takbirs in Eid prayer and evaluate the proofs from different madhhabs.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds 6 extra takbirs; others hold 9-10. The dispute stems from differing Companion narrations.

The Eid prayer is a special act of worship with extra takbirs. However, the number of these extra takbirs differs among the madhhabs. This lesson examines the Hanafi position and compares it with the views of Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and Imam Shafi'i, based on the narrations from the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Pinpoint what is being disputed: the number of additional takbirs (takbīrāt zawā'id) in the two rak'ahs of the Eid prayer. Note that these are considered wājibāt in the Hanafi school.
The extra takbirs are separate from the opening takbir (takbīr al-tahrīm) and the takbirs for bowing (rukū') and prostrations.
2
State the Hanafi position and its dalīl
The Hanafi school holds that there are six extra takbirs: three in the first rak'ah after the opening takbir, before recitation, and three in the second rak'ah after the takbir for standing, before recitation. The proof is the narration from Ibn Mas'ud (R) that the Prophet (S) prayed the Eid prayer with fifteen total takbirs: the opening takbir, six extra, and the transition takbirs.
The Hanafis count only the takbirs beyond the opening and transition takbirs as extra.
3
Identify the opposing positions and their dalīl
Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad (Hanbalis) hold nine extra takbirs based on a narration from Ibn Abbas (R) of thirteen total takbirs. Imam Shafi'i has two narrations: twelve or thirteen total takbirs, leading to nine or ten extra. He considers all takbirs after the opening as extra.
The dispute aris from different transmissions from the Companions about the practice of the Prophet (S).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and the practical consequence
The Hanafi response is that the narration of Ibn Mas'ud is more reliable (thābit) and that the principle is to separate the original takbirs from the extra ones. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilāf) is that a Hanafi praying alone says 6 extra takbirs, while a Maliki says 9, a Hanbali says 9, and a Shafi'i says 9 or 10.
The Hanafi tarjīh prefers the six-takbīr view, which is the muftā bihī position in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نبیر یں پندرہ ہوں گی اور تیرہ تکبیر والی روایت کی صورت میں کل تکبیر میں سولہ ہوں گی پس مردی سے مراد وہ ہے جو ابن عباس سے ایت کی گئی ہے اب حاصل یہ ہوا کہ احناف کے نزدیک عید کی دونوں رکعتوں میں تکبیرات زوائد چھ ہیں۔ اور امام مالک اور امام نو کے نزدیک اس ہیں۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک بارہ یا تیرہ ہیں۔ (شرح نقایه ) اسٹاف کے مذہب کی بنیاد ابن مسعودؓ کے قول پر ہے۔ اور امام مالک اور امام احمد کے مذہب کی بنیا دا بن عباس کی تیرہ تکبیروں والی روایت پر ہے۔ اس طرح پیر کے دن تکبیر میں زائد ہیں اور تین اصلی ہیں اور امام شافعی کے مذہب کی بنیاد ابن عباس کی دونوں روایتوں (بارہ نبرد والی ) پر ہے لیکن وہ ان تمام کو زائد قرار دیتے ہیں۔ اصلی تین ان کے علاوہ ہیں ۔ واللہ اعلم
The takbirs will be fifteen, and in the narration of thirteen takbirs, the total takbirs will be sixteen. So what is meant by 'mardī' is that which is narrated from Ibn Abbas. Now the result is that according to the Hanafis, the extra takbirs in both rak'ahs of Eid are six. According to Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad, they are nine. According to Imam Shafi'i, they are twelve or thirteen. (Sharh al-Nuqayah) The basis of the Shafi'i school is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud (R). The basis of Malik and Ahmad's school is the narration of thirteen takbirs from Ibn Abbas. In this way, on the first day, the extra takbirs are [four?] and the original are three. The basis of Shafi'i school is on both narrations from Ibn Abbas (twelve and thirteen) but he considers all of them extra. The original three are besides them. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of extra takbirs (takbīrāt zawā'id) in the Eid prayer. The Hanafi position, based on the narration of Ibn Mas'ud (R), holds that there are six extra takbirs: three in the first rak'ah after the opening takbir (excluding the takbir for bowing) and three in the second rak'ah after the takbir for standing. The Malikis and Hanbalis hold that there are nine extra takbirs, based on a narration from Ibn Abbas (R) of thirteen total takbirs (including the opening takbir), yielding nine extra. The Shafi'is have two narrations from Ibn Abbas: twelve and thirteen total takbirs (i.e., nine or ten extra), but they consider all beyond the opening takbir as extra. The Hanafi tarjih prefers the six-takbir view, which is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, as this is from Zahir al-Riwayah. The ikhtilaf stems from differing transmissions from the Companions.

Key Terms
تکبیرات زوائد (takbīrāt zawā'id): The extra takbirs recited in the Eid prayer beyond the ordinary takbirs of the prayer.
عیدین (al-'Īdayn): The two Eid festivals: Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Six
B) Nine
C) Twelve
D) Fifteen

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school counts six extra takbirs in Eid prayer, based on the narration of Ibn Mas'ud, differing from the nine or ten of other schools.
